401 of 745 DOCUMENTS


State v. Arrington


CR-10-0634


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


74 So. 3d 482; 2011 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 35



May 27, 2011, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 31, 2012.

Released for Publication October 20, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-10-0202). William E. Shashy, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: PETITION GRANTED; WRIT ISSUED; STAY LIFTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of violating Ala. Code § 15-20-23 of the Community Notification Act (CNA). The Montgomery Circuit Court granted defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal notwithstanding the verdict, finding that statute unconstitutional as it applied to him. The State filed a petition for a writ of mandamus directing the trial court to set aside its order, reinstate defendant's conviction, and sentence defendant.


OVERVIEW: Before trial, defendant moved to dismiss the charges against him. After he was convicted, he filed a motion for acquittal, arguing for the first time that the CNA was unconstitutional as applied to him. The State argued that the trial court exceeded the scope of Ala. R. Crim. P. 20.3 by setting aside the jury's verdict for grounds other than the sufficiency of the evidence. The court found that the constitutionality of statute was an issue that should have been challenged in a pretrial motion pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 15.4. As the trial court's ruling did not address the sufficiency of the evidence to convict defendant, but rather the constitutionality of the statute, it exceeded the scope of Rule 20.3.


OUTCOME: The court granted the State's petition for a writ of mandamus and directed the trial court to reinstate the jury's guilty verdict and to sentence defendant in accordance with the law.

 

402 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Herring v. State


CR-10-0019


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


100 So. 3d 616; 2011 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 42



May 27, 2011, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 7, 2013.
Released for Publication November 27, 2012.
Rehearing denied by Herring v. State, 2011 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 718 (Ala. Crim. App., Aug. 19, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court (Bessemer Division). (CC-09-1676). Trial Judge: Teresa Petelos.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to establishing a residence where a minor resides in violation of Ala. Code § 15-20-26(c) of the Community Notification Act (CNA), Ala. Code § 15-20-20 et seq., but he expressly reserved the right to appeal the decision of the Jefferson Circuit Court, Alabama, which denied his pretrial motion to dismiss the indictment on the ground that § 15-20-26(c)(3) and (4) were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been convicted of molesting a 10-year old niece while she was residing with him. He argued § 15-20-26(c)(3) and (4) violated his rights to due process and equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV as they prohibited him from residing with his biological children. Although defendant had a fundamental right to parent his children, the court applied a strict scrutiny analysis and held that § 15-20-26(c)(3) and (4) did not unconstitutionally infringe upon his due process or equal protection rights as they were narrowly tailored to serve the compelling state interest of protecting children. The CNA did not contain a blanket prohibition preventing sex offenders from residing with their minor children. Rather, defendant belonged to a limited subset of offenders who were treated equally under the CNA; offenders victimized a child under 12 years old or a minor who was living with the offender. There was no less restrictive alternative to protecting children from sex offenders under the Alabama Juvenile Justice Act, Ala. Code § 12-15-101 et seq., as it was limited to only those children under a juvenile court's jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

403 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Peak v. City of Tuscaloosa


CR-09-0805


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


73 So. 3d 5; 2011 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 23



April 29, 2011, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended June 17, 2011.

As Amended January 25, 2012.

As Amended January 31, 2012.

Released for Publication September 9, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Tuscaloosa Circuit Court. (CC-07-268). William S. Donaldson, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a municipal court for failure to register a septic tank under Tuscaloosa Municipal Code, Ala., § 13-51(3) and (16). He appealed to the Tuscaloosa Circuit Court, Alabama, which again convicted of him of failing to register a septic tank and ordered him to pay a fine. He sought review, claiming a city was without authority to enact § 13-51 and it violated due process and equal protection principles.


OVERVIEW: The court found that in enacting § 13-51(3), the city was engaging in a governmental function within its statutory police powers, and not a proprietary function as defendant argued. The legislature did not intend to preempt the entire field of wastewater regulation by providing a comprehensive scheme for the regulation of septic tanks by the Alabama Onsite Wastewater Board under Ala. Code § 34-21A-1 et seq., and by the State Board of Health under Ala. Code § 22-26-1 et seq. Ala. Code § 34A-21A-10 provided the licensing requirements of the Onsite Wastewater Board did not apply to residential homeowners and Ala. Admin. Code r. 420-3-1-.104 provided that approval by the State Board of Health was not to be construed as approval by a municipality. The registration requirement under § 13-51(3) was rationally related to protecting a lake within the city's jurisdiction from contaminants from leaking septic tanks and did not violate principles of due process or equal protection. The disclosure risks of § 13-51 did not pose a substantial hazard of self-incrimination as the registration requirement itself did not require defendant to admit to anything inherently criminal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Stanley v. State


CR-06-2236


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


143 So. 3d 230; 2011 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 24



April 29, 2011, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 20, 2015.

As Corrected October 9, 2014.
Released for Publication August 13 2014.
As Corrected February 25, 2013.

As Corrected June 9, 2011
Appeal after remand at, Decision reached on appeal by Stanley v. State, 143 So. 3d 230, 2011 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 64 (Ala. Crim. App., Aug. 26, 2011); On Remand from the Alabama Supreme Court; Stanley v. State, 2013 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 14 (Ala. Crim. App., Feb. 15, 2013).


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Colbert Circuit Court. (CC-05-608). Harold V. Hughston, Jr., Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS TO CONVICTION; REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS AS TO SENTENCING. *



* *Note from the reporter of decisions: On February 3, 2012, the defendant, filed a petition i:or certiorari review. On August 17, 2012, the Alabama Supreme Court issued an order vacating the August 26, 2011, judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals affirming Stanley's sentence of death and remanding the case with instructions 1110298)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Colbert Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted him of capital murder for the intentional murder of his victim by stabbing him during the course of a first-degree robbery in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) (1975).


OVERVIEW: After defendant and his wife had been using illegal narcotics for several days, they called the victim and told him to come to their apartment so that he could be paid for drugs that they had previously obtained from him. Defendant then planned to rob and kill the victim, which he did with the help of his wife. Defendant was sentenced to death. During the penalty phase of the trial, the jury, by a vote of 8 to 4, recommended life imprisonment without the possibility of parole. The trial court overrode the jury's recommendation, finding that the aggravating circumstances outweighed the mitigating circumstances. The circuit court's order did not clearly state that it found the jury's recommendation to be a mitigating circumstance and did not contain written findings concerning what weight the jury recommendation was given. Thus, the court remanded the case to the trial court for it to amend its sentencing order to clarify its findings regarding the judicial override. The trial court was ordered to reweigh the aggravating circumstances and the mitigating circumstances and resentence defendant and state how it considered the jury's advisory verdict and the weight it was accorded.


OUTCOME: The conviction was upheld but sentencing was remanded.

 

406 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Powell v. State


CR-09-1192


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


72 So. 3d 1268; 2011 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 28



April 29, 2011, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 9, 2011.

As Amended November 21, 2011.

As Amended January 31, 2012.
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Powell v. Arrington, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 105803 (N.D. Ala., July 14, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Blount Circuit Court. (CC-08-301). Steven D. King, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Blount Circuit Court (Alabama) of one count of unlawful transport of articles containing sounds transferred without the consent of the owner, a violation of Ala. Code § 13A-8-81(a)(3). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction because the State failed to present evidence showing that the copyrighted material contained on the disks was transferred without the consent of owner in that a representative from the trade organizations who testified for the State at trial was not an "owner" under Ala. Code § 13A-8-80 or one "authorized to maintain custody and control over business records reflecting consent" under Ala. Code § 13A-8-81(a)(e). The court of criminal appeals disagreed. The representative testified that the disks were not made pursuant to industry standards in that they were "burned" onto a disk as opposed to being "pressed" into the disk. None of the disks were packaged in a manner consistent with industry practice, and no disk was accompanied by the artwork or information generally associated with typical commercial reproduction. The State also presented evidence indicating that defendant was involved with the buying and selling of the reproductions. The evidence gave rise to the inference that defendant was operating with the knowledge that his activities were taking place without the consent of the owners.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Wilkerson v. State


CR-08-1779


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


70 So. 3d 442; 2011 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 17



March 25, 2011, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 31, 2012.

As Corrected January 25, 2012.
Released for Publication August 30, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Lee Circuit Court. (CC-02-1097.60). TRIAL JUDGE: Jacob A. Walker III.
Wilkerson v. State, 978 So. 2d 72, 2006 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1087 (Ala. Crim. App., 2006)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Defendant's confession was voluntary under U.S. Const. amend. V because the evidence established that defendant was advised of his juvenile Miranda rights before his confession and that he signed a waiver-of-rights form. The evidence also established that defendant had completed the 11th grade, that he could read, write, and understand English, and that he indicated to the officers that he understood his rights. Moreover, the evidence established that law-enforcement officers did not coerce or threaten defendant to make a statement.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Revis v. State


CR-06-0454


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


101 So. 3d 247; 2011 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 51



January 13, 2011, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended January 25, 2013.

Released for Publication November 27, 2012.
Decision reached on appeal by Revis v. State, 101 So. 3d 247, 2011 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 68 (Ala. Crim. App., 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Revis v. Alabama, 133 S. Ct. 1267, 185 L. Ed. 2d 207, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 1344 (U.S., Feb. 19, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Marion Circuit Court. (CC-2005-142). John H. Bentley, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: In defendant's capital murder trial for the intentional killing of the victim during the course of committing a first-degree robbery of money and drugs, defendant's drug use was admissible under Ala. R. Evid. 404(b) as an exception to the exclusionary rule because it was part of the res gestae and interwoven into the offense. Further, because evidence of defendant's drug use established his motive for committing the capital offense, the evidence was relevant and admissible.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the trial court with instructions to vacate one of the murder convictions and the sentence imposed for that conviction because the two counts of murder during a robbery charged defendant twice with committing the same offense.

 

409 of 745 DOCUMENTS


McCray v. State


CR-06-0360


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


88 So. 3d 1; 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 136



December 17, 2010, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended August 22, 2012.

Released for Publication May 8, 2012.
Rehearing denied by McCray v. State, 2011 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 146 (Ala. Crim. App., Mar. 18, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Houston Circuit Court. (CC-05-1532), S. Edward Jackson, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Houston Circuit Court (Alabama) of capital murder and sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court abused its discretion when it denied defendant's Batson motion because the State's use of two of its peremptory strikes to remove two of the three remaining African-American prospective jurors established a prima facie case of discrimination. The court of criminal appeals disagreed. Although the State used two peremptory strikes to remove two of the three African-Americans remaining on the venire, that fact did not establish a prima facie case of racial discrimination. The record did not reflect, and defendant did not argue, that the two African-Americans struck by the State shared only the characteristic of race, that anything in the type or manner of the State's statements or questions during voir dire examination indicated an intent to discriminate against African-American jurors, that there was a lack of meaningful voir dire directed at African-American jurors, or that African-American jurors and Caucasian jurors were treated differently. With nothing more than an attenuated history of improper peremptory challenges, it could not be said that the trial court abused its discretion in denying defendant's Batson motion.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Cosper v. State


CR-09-0747


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


89 So. 3d 186; 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 135



December 17, 2010, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended December 18, 2012.

Released for Publication May 8, 2012.
Rehearing denied by Cosper v. State, 2011 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 150 (Ala. Crim. App., Feb. 18, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Morgan Circuit Court. (CC-08-1414), Glenn E. Thompson, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Defendant violated Ala. Code §§ 15-20-23 and 15-20-24 of the Community Notification Act (CNA), Ala. Code § 15-20-20 et seq., and he was convicted. A challenge to the constitutionality of the CNA was not preserved for review, and moreover, it lacked merit. The evidence was sufficient to support his conviction for failing to notify the authorities of his intent to transfer his residence under § 15-20-23. However, the State did not provide sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction for failing to report semiannually pursuant to § 15-20-24.


OUTCOME: Judgment convicting defendant of failing to semiannually verify his residence reversed; judgment to be rendered in defendant's favor. Remainder of judgment affirmed.

State v. Jemison


CR-09-0399


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


66 So. 3d 832; 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 142



December 17, 2010, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 21, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Chilton Circuit Court. (CC-09-332).
State v. Jemison, 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 64 (Ala. Crim. App., July 30, 2010)



DISPOSITION: APPLICATION OVERRULED; OPINION OF JULY 30, 2010, WITHDRAWN; OPINION SUBSTITUTED; REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Defendant's motion to suppress a package of "ecstasy" pills was granted in defendant's prosecution under Ala. Code §§ 13A-12-212 and 32-6-19. A prior decision on appeal was withdrawn upon rehearing and a new one was entered. A police officer acted reasonably under U.S. Const. amend. IV in following defendant, based on suspected drug activity and nervousness while driving, and defendant's arrest for disorderly conduct was lawful. He lacked standing to challenge a bag of drugs found in his uncle's yard. Evidence seized from his vehicle, even if improper, was not subject to the exclusionary rule.


OUTCOME: Prior opinion withdrawn and new opinion substituted. Trial court judgment reversed, remanded with instructions to set aside the suppression order; cased restored to the active docket.

 

414 of 745 DOCUMENTS


State v. Adams


CR-08-1728


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


91 So. 3d 724; 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 104



November 5, 2010, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended May 31, 2011.
As Amended June 17, 2011.
Released for Publication July 10, 2012.
Related proceeding at State v. Coppage, 92 So. 3d 814, 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 119 (Ala. Crim. App., Nov. 5, 2010)
Writ of certiorari denied State v. Adams, 91 So. 3d 755, 2012 Ala. LEXIS 21 (Ala., Feb. 24, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-08-1514). Truman M. Hobbs, Jr., Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Alabama sought review of an order of the Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama) dismissing an indictment of defendant and declaring unconstitutional that portion of former Ala. Code § 15-20-22(a)(1) in the Community Notification Act (CNA), Ala. Code § 15-20-20 et seq., that required an adult criminal sex offender to provide, prior to release from custody, the actual address at which he or she would reside or live upon release.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an adult criminal sex offender, was arrested on his scheduled prison release date and indicted for failing to meet the anticipated address reporting requirement of former Ala. Code § 15-20-22(a)(1). The court held that the statute violated the guarantee to equal protection under the Fourteenth Amendment and in Ala. Const. art. I, §§ 1, 6, and 22, because it resulted in an unreasonable and discriminatory classification based on wealth. The statute also was unconstitutional as applied to defendant under the Eighth Amendment and under Ala. Const. art. I, § 15. The requirement in former § 15-20-22(a)(1) that a sex offender provide an actual address at which he or she would reside punished defendant solely for his status of being homeless. The charge for violating the reporting provision of the CNA was a felony, and indigent offenders thus could eventually be sentenced as habitual felons to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole solely because they had no funds to secure a place to stay upon their release from prison. Thus, as applied to this defendant, § 15-20-22(a)(1) constituted cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court dismissing the indictment of defendant.

McMillan v. State


CR-08-1954


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


139 So. 3d 184; 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 106



November 5, 2010, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 20, 2015.

Released for Publication June 6, 2014.

As Corrected December 8, 2010.

As Amended April 7, 2011.

As Corrected August 1, 2011.

As Amended August 10, 2011.
Rehearing denied by McMillan v. State, 2011 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 2567 (Ala. Crim. App., Jan. 13, 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by McMillan v. Alabama, 134 S. Ct. 1760, 188 L. Ed. 2d 597, 2014 U.S. LEXIS 2317 (U.S., Mar. 31, 2014)
Writ denied by Ex parte McMillan, 207 So. 3d 854, 2015 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 370 (Ala. Crim. App., Jan. 29, 2015)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at McMillan v. State, 2017 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 54 (Ala. Crim. App., Aug. 11, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Elmore Circuit Court. (CC-08-476). John B. Bush, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Elmore Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted him of capital murder under Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2), (a)(17) and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital murder for the intentional murder of one victim by shooting him in the course of a first-degree robbery, and for the intentional murder of the second victim by shooting him inside a vehicle. The trial court sentenced defendant to death following the jury's 8-4 advisory verdict of life imprisonment without parole. The appellate court affirmed the convictions and sentence. Because the investigator did not interrogate defendant until he had indicated that he understood his rights and chose to waive them, there was no constitutional violation of his right to counsel and his statement was properly admitted. Defendant also failed to make a prima facie showing of discrimination by the State in striking the jury and there was no plain error resulting from the admission into evidence of a wedding photograph and the identification by his widow of the victim in the photograph. There was also no showing, through the voir dire examination, of actual prejudice, nor was there any showing that the community was so saturated with pretrial publicity that defendant was prevented from receiving a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

416 of 745 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gamble


CR-06-2274


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


63 So. 3d 707; 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 82



October 1, 2010, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 18, 2011. As Corrected October 11, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Shelby Circuit Court. (CC-96-813.60). J. Michael Joiner, Trial Judge.
Gamble v. State, 791 So. 2d 409, 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 275 (Ala. Crim. App., 2000)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision of the Shelby Circuit Court (Alabama), which granted, in part, the inmate's postconviction petition attacking his capital-murder conviction and sentence of death. The inmate filed a cross-appeal from the circuit court's partial denial of claims in his postconviction petition.


OVERVIEW: The State appealed the order that granted, in part, the inmate's postconviction petition attacking his capital-murder conviction and sentence of death. The inmate cross-appealed the partial denial of his claims in his postconviction petition. The supreme court affirmed the judgment granting Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 relief in part. The judgment was reversed insofar as it held that the inmate could not have been sentenced to death because his codefendant was sentenced to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole. The inmate was denied the effective assistance of counsel at the penalty phase of his capital-murder trial because counsel failed to investigate and present mitigating evidence. Counsel's investigation was so inadequate that they failed to discover any mitigation evidence to present at the penalty phase, although the R. 32 evidentiary hearing clearly showed that there was a plethora of evidence that could have been presented on the inmate's behalf. The circuit court erred in finding that the inmate's death sentence was improper because it was constitutionally disproportionate and excessive to his codefendant's sentence of life imprisonment.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the judgment insofar as it held that the inmate could not be sentenced to death merely because his codefendant was sentenced to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole. The case was remanded to the circuit court for proceedings consistent with the opinion and the remainder of the judgment was affirmed.

 

417 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. State


CR-05-0066


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


157 So. 3d 131; 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 83



October 1, 2010, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 25, 2013.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Mobile Circuit Court. (CC-98-1328.60).
Ex parte Taylor, 157 So. 3d 122, 2008 Ala. LEXIS 12 (Ala., Jan. 18, 2008)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of four counts of capital murder and sentenced to death. Following the circuit court's denial of defendant's Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 petition, the appellate court dismissed the appeal. The Alabama Supreme Court reversed the dismissal of the appeal and remanded for the appellate court to consider the circuit court's denial of the Rule 32 petition.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the parties agreed that certain claims remained pending after the circuit court entered the orders of partial dismissal, so the appellate court remanded the cause for resolution of those pending claims. The court rejected defendant's remaining challenges to his conviction and sentence. The adoption of the State's proposed orders partially dismissing claims was not error and did not warrant reversal; the orders required an analysis of defendant's petition and the State's answer, along with the record from the trial and the direct appeal, and they were not based on the any alleged personal knowledge or observations garnered by the judge during the trial. Even if a cumulative-effect analysis were required by Alabama law, that factor would not have eliminated defendant's obligation to plead each claim of ineffective assistance of counsel in compliance with the directives of Ala. R. Crim. P. 32. Defendant's cursory summary of the allegations of the petition did not comport with Ala. R. Crim. P. 28(a)(10). Because the primary method of execution in Alabama was then lethal injection, Ala. Code § 15-18-82(a), defendant's argument about electrocution was moot.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the cause to the circuit court for resolution of those claims that the parties agreed had not been dismissed by the orders of partial dismissal, and it affirmed the remaining parts of the judgment of conviction and sentence.

 

418 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Mitchell v. State


CR-06-0827


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


84 So. 3d 968; 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 78



August 27, 2010, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 30, 2012.

As Amended May 31, 2011. As Corrected August 1, 2011. As Corrected October 11, 2011.
Rehearing denied by Mitchell v. State, 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 2017 (Ala. Crim. App., Dec. 10, 2010)
Writ quashed Ex parte Mitchell, 84 So. 3d 1013, 2011 Ala. LEXIS 195 (Ala., 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Mitchell v. Ala., 2012 U.S. LEXIS 6694 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-06-1059). J. William Cole, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) convicting him, upon a jury's verdict, of four counts of capital murder, in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2), (10), and overriding the jury's recommendation of life in prison and instead sentencing him to death on all four counts.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another took the lives of three people during the course of a robbery. He was also convicted of an additional count of capital murder under § 13A-5-40(a)(10) because two or more people were murdered pursuant to one course of conduct. Although the jury recommended life by a vote of 10-2, the trial court's override of the recommendation under Ala. Code § 13A-5-47(d) did not violate Ala. Const. art. I, §§ 9, 15, or U.S. Const. amends. V, VI, VIII, or XIV. The judicial-override provision did not result in the arbitrary imposition of the death penalty. The capital sentencing procedure ensured that the trial judge was given adequate information and sufficient guidance in deciding whether to accept the jury's recommendation, and Ala. Code § 13A-5-53 provided sufficient guidelines for an appellate determination of whether the trial judge's override was appropriate. Further, the trial court clearly set forth its reasons for overriding the recommendation, expressly stating that the jury's recommendation weighed heavily in favor of defendant. Finally, the trial court's consideration of additional facts in weighing the aggravating and mitigating circumstances was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Miller v. State


CR-06-0741


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


63 So. 3d 676; 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 77



August 27, 2010, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 18, 2011. As corrected August 24, 2011. As Corrected October 11, 2011.
US Supreme Court certiorari granted by, Motion granted by Miller v. Alabama, 132 S. Ct. 548, 181 L. Ed. 2d 395, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 7959 (U.S., 2011)
Motion denied by Miller v. Alabama, 132 S. Ct. 1733, 182 L. Ed. 2d 251, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 1957 (U.S., 2012)
Reversed by, Remanded by Miller v. Ala., 2012 U.S. LEXIS 4873 (U.S., June 25, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Lawrence Circuit Court. (CC-06-68). A. Phillip Reich III, Trial Judge.
Miller v. State, 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 61 (Ala. Crim. App., June 25, 2010)



DISPOSITION: OPINION OF JUNE 25, 2010, WITHDRAWN; OPINION SUBSTITUTED; AFFIRMED; APPLICATION FOR REHEARING IS OVERRULED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Lawrence Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted him of capital murder committed during the course of an arson in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(9) and sentenced him to life in prison without the possibility of parole. He filed an application for rehearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of murder made capital because it was committed during the course of an arson and his sentence of life in prison without the possibility of parole. The appellate court affirmed, stating that considering defendant's age and his crime, his sentence of life in prison without the possibility of parole for capital murder was not categorically disproportionate. Defendant committed the worst crime recognized in Alabama, capital murder, and, solely because of his age, was not eligible for the harshest penalty. Further, assuming, without deciding, that the State failed to present sufficient evidence to establish that an expert was an expert in blood-spatter analysis, any error in allowing her testimony regarding what could have caused the blood spatter on defendant's shirt was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt because the testimony was cumulative. Even if the admission of defendant's statement was erroneous, the error was harmless because the statement, at most, helped to link him to the stolen cards; however, defendant's connection to the cards was also established by his formal statement to the investigator in which he admitted stealing the cards.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the application for rehearing was overruled.

OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of three counts of capital murder for murdering the victim during the course of a robbery, during the course of a burglary, and for causing the victim's death by firing a shot from outside a dwelling into a dwelling. McFadden v. State


CR-07-1923


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


67 So. 3d 169; 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 48



June 25, 2010, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 27, 2011
Rehearing denied by McFadden v. State, 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 162 (Ala. Crim. App., Sept. 24, 2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by McFadden v. Ala., 2011 U.S. LEXIS 8926 (U.S., Dec. 12, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Baldwin Circuit Court. (CC-05-1848). Trial Judge: James H. Reid, Jr.
McFadden v. State, 27 So. 3d 637, 2008 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1433 (Ala. Crim. App., 2008)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Baldwin Circuit Court (Alabama) convicting him of possession and production of obscene matters containing a visual reproduction of a person under the age of 17 years, violations of Ala. Code §§ 13A-12-192(b), -197, and sentencing him as a habitual offender to concurrent sentences of life and 30 years' imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: During a routine visit to defendant's residence, his probation officer noticed a pair of children's underwear, toys, and children's clothing. In a more thorough search, the officer found depictions of nude children in collages surrounded by depictions of adult genitalia. The evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's convictions because the collages or montages, which included pictures or photographs of unclothed young children combined with adult sexual acts, were clearly obscene and in violation of the conduct proscribed by Ala. Code § 13A-12-190(12), (13), of the Alabama Child Pornography Act, Ala. Code § 13A-12-190 et seq. Further because the collage or montage evidence contained genital nudity, which amounted to child pornography, it was afforded no protection under U.S. Const. amend. I. The First Amendment did not protect pornography involving actual children. Additionally, the statutes under which defendant was convicted, Ala. Code §§ 13A-12-192(b), -197, did not violate the First Amendment. Finally, the collage or montage exhibits were properly admitted into evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Dotch v. State


CR-07-1913


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA

Released for Publication July 27, 2011.
Rehearing denied by Dotch v. State, 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 160 (Ala. Crim. App., June 11, 2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Dotch v. Alabama, 131 S. Ct. 3030, 180 L. Ed. 2d 846, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 4695 (U.S., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Mobile Circuit Court. (CC-07-788). Trial Judge: Roderick P. Stout.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction entered by the Mobile Circuit Court (Alabama) for capital murder for the intentional murder of the victim by the use of a deadly weapon while she was in a vehicle, in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(17) and his resulting sentence of death. Defendant asserted numerous arguments.


OVERVIEW: None of defendant's allegations of suggestive techniques used by the police was supported by the record. Neither the cited discrepancies in the witnesses' descriptions nor the differences in the descriptions in their original statements and those in their testimony at trial discredited their identifications. As the indictment properly mentioned the prior convictions, the trial court's instructions to the jury, in which the judge read the indictment and charged as to the requisite proof of the elements of the charged offenses, were also proper. As the prior offenses were properly charged in the indictment as the factual basis of an element of the offense, it was incumbent upon the State to prove them. Further, the convictions were relevant as they were also introduced to prove motive and intent. Because a rational basis existed for making the intentional killing of a victim who was inside a vehicle a capital offense, defendant's claim of unreasonableness was meritless. Moreover, the statute was not overly broad or too vague.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Smith v. Houston


CR-07-2027


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


71 So. 3d 721; 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 17



March 5, 2010, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended January 25, 2012.

Released for Publication September 12, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CV-06-2356). Charles Price, Trial Judge.
Smith v. State, 745 So. 2d 922, 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 122 (Ala. Crim. App., 1999)



DISPOSITION: APPEAL TRANSFERRED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of an order from the Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama), which denied his action filed under the Declaratory Judgment Act, Ala. Code § 6-6-220 et seq., seeking a declaration that defendants, State of Alabama and various public officials (State), had improperly and unconstitutionally interpreted and applied Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(18).


OVERVIEW: The inmate initially appealed to the Court of Civil Appeals of Alabama. That court transferred the appeal to the Alabama Supreme Court, and the Supreme Court transferred the appeal back to that court, the Court of Civil Appeals then transferred the appeal to the court. Upon review, the court noted that the inmate's sole request for relief was a judgment declaring that the State had been unconstitutionally interpreting § 13A-5-40(a)(18). The inmate's action was not a Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 petition challenging his conviction or sentence. A declaratory-judgment action was, by its nature, a civil action, not a postconviction writ in a criminal case. Therefore, the court had no jurisdiction to hear the appeal from a declaratory-judgment action under Ala. Const. art. VI, § 141(a) and Ala. Code § 12-3-9. Finally, the court determined that the matter had to be transferred back to the Court of Civil Appeals rather than the Supreme Court as the Supreme Court had previously deflected the matter to the Court of Civil Appeals under Ala. Code § 12-1-4.


OUTCOME: The court transferred the case back to the Court of Civil Appeals of Alabama.

The jury recommended, by a vote of 10 to 2, that appellant be sentenced to death. The Houston Circuit Court followed the jury's recommendation and sentenced appellant to death. The instant appeal was automatic in a death penalty case and the lower-court proceedings were reviewed for plain error.


OVERVIEW: There was no indication that the circuit court abused its discretion in denying appellant's motion for a change of venue or in denying appellant's motion for a continuance to secure a second pathologist. Code § 13A-5-49, and to make specific findings of facts consistent with the requirements of Ex parte Kyzer concerning the aggravating circumstances set out in § 13A-5-49(8). The circuit court was to then reweigh the aggravating and mitigating circumstances and resentence appellant.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed as to appellant's conviction, but the case was remanded with directions as to sentencing.

Code § 13A-5-40(a)(4), and the intentional killing of the victim during the course of a first-degree robbery, Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2). PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Calhoun Circuit Court. (CC-07-552). Brian P. Howell.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.

3-26-2010: On return to remand: AFFIRMED BY UNPUBLISHED MEMORANDUM (Wise, P.J., and Welch and Kellum, JJ., concur; Windom and Main, JJ., concur in part and dissent in part, with opinions)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Calhoun Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted him of murder, a Class A felony, and sentenced him to 120 years in the State penitentiary pursuant to the Habitual Felony Offender Act, Ala. Code § 13A-5-9(b)(3).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the circuit court abused its discretion when it denied his request for a continuance to secure the testimony of an inmate, who defendant argued could have testified that he overheard an accomplice tell someone that the accomplice was responsible for the victim's death. The court of criminal appeals held that the circuit court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's request to delay the trial in order to transport the inmate from a correctional facility. Defendant failed to establish that the inmate's testimony would be admissible. He offered no explanation as to how the inmate's testimony fit within any exception to the hearsay rule. The statement was not offered against a party as required under Ala. R. Evid. 801(d)(2) but was offered in the defense. The court of criminal appeals concluded that defendant's sentence exceeded the limits set by statute. It read § 13A-5-9(a)(3) in conjunction with Ala. Code § 13A-5-6(a)(1), which stated that sentences for a Class A felony could be for life or not more than 99 years or less than 10 years. Therefore, the only sentences available for defendant were either 99 years' imprisonment or life.


OUTCOME: The court of criminal appeals remanded the case to the circuit court with direction to resentence defendant in accordance with the terms set out in the opinion.

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended August 10, 2011.
Rehearing denied by Dunaway v. State, 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 3003 (Ala. Crim. App., Feb. 19, 2010)
Reversed by, Remanded by Ex parte Dunaway, 198 So. 3d 567, 2014 Ala. LEXIS 59 (Ala., Apr. 18, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Barbour Circuit Court. (CC-97-75.60 and CC-97-76.60).
Ex parte Dunaway, 746 So. 2d 1042, 1999 Ala. LEXIS 280 (Ala., 1999)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an inmate on death row, appealed from an order of the Barbour Circuit Court (Alabama) denying his petition for postconviction relief filed pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murdering two people in the course of an arson, in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(9). Defendant failed to meet his burden of proving by a preponderance of the evidence that juror misconduct caused him prejudice. Further, defendant's several allegations that his attorneys were ineffective were without merit. The attorneys' performance was not deficient simply because they did not present cumulative evidence. Further, any alleged conflicts of interest did not rise to the level of ineffective assistance because they did not create actual conflicts of interest nor did they adversely affect the attorneys' representation. The doctrine of collateral estoppel did not bar review of whether or not defendant was mentally retarded. A review of defendant's trial testimony showed that he was clear and articulate on the stand, even during a vigorous cross-examination by the prosecutor. Defendant did not have significant subaverage intellectual functioning or significant or substantial deficits in adaptive behavior before turning 18 years old. Thus, he did not meet his burden of proving that he was mentally retarded and, thus, not eligible for the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Worley


CR-06-1879


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


102 So. 3d 408; 2009 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 152



November 13, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended August 10, 2011. As Corrected October 11, 2011.

Released for Publication November 27, 2012.
Rehearing denied by State v. Worley, 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 164 (Ala. Crim. App., Feb. 5, 2010)
Reversed by, Remanded by Ex parte Worley, 102 So. 3d 428, 2010 Ala. LEXIS 159 (Ala., Sept. 10, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-07-475). Trial Judge: Truman M. Hobbs, Jr.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state appealed the judgment of the Montgomery Circuit Court (Ala.) that dismissed the indictment against appellee defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was the state secretary of state. Defendant sent a letter to her employees in which she asked for their support in her bid for reelection. The trial court held that because former Ala. Code § 17-1-7(c) (recodified) specifically addressed campaign practices involving subordinates, the more general felony statute -- former Ala. Code § 17-1-7(b) (recodified and amended)-- did not control. The trial court also concluded that the state had overreached by attempting to charge misdemeanor offenses as felony offenses. The trial court also stated that § 17-1-7(b) was unconstitutionally vague. The appellate court found that the trial court should have permitted the state to present to the jury all the evidence it had to offer toward proving both the felony charges and the misdemeanor charges. The trial court made a pretrial determination as to the sufficiency of the evidence, and such a determination was not permitted by the Alabama Rules of Criminal Procedure or by Alabama caselaw. The terms in § 17-1-7(b), particularly as applied to defendant, were not so vague that people of ordinary intelligence were required to guess at their meaning.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the action was remanded for further proceedings.

 

434 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Billups v. State


CR-05-1767


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


86 So. 3d 1032; 2009 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 155



November 13, 2009, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended December 17, 2010.

Released for Publication May 1, 2012.
Rehearing denied by Billups v. State, 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1483 (Ala. Crim. App., Jan. 22, 2010)
Reversed by, Remanded by Ex parte Billups, 86 So. 3d 1079, 2010 Ala. LEXIS 247 (Ala., 2010)
Petition granted by, Writ granted by State v. Billups, 2016 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 39 (Ala. Crim. App., June 17, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-05-1755). J. William Cole, Trial Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Jefferson Circuit Court that convicted him of capital murder under Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) (1975), arguing that the trial court erred under Ala. R. Evid. 404(b) in introducing evidence that he had been convicted of murdering four other men a few days before the murder at issue.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the trial court did not err under Ala. R. Evid. 404(b) in allowing the State to introduce evidence that defendant had been convicted of capital murder in the killing of four other men because there were several similarities between the two offenses. The victims in both cases were young men involved with drugs, defendant telephoned the victims and lured them to a location of his choosing with the offer of making a drug deal and then shot the victims in the head after they arrived and took their property, the offenses occurred within a period a three days, and there was evidence that the same gun was used at both crime scenes. In light of the similarities between the two offenses, the two crimes were committed in the same novel and peculiar manner, and the evidence about the killing of the four men was thus admissible under the identity and plan or pattern exception to the general exclusionary rule. Further, because both offenses involved killings that facilitated robberies for drugs and/or money, the evidence about the prior killings was also admissible under the intent and motive exceptions to the general exclusionary rule.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and the capital sentence were affirmed.

 

435 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Lewis v. State


CR-06-1770


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


57 So. 3d 807; 2009 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 123



October 2, 2009, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 9, 2011

As Corrected June 28, 2011.
Appeal after remand at Lewis v. State, 2009 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 169 (Ala. Crim. App., Dec. 18, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-06-3554 and CC-06-3555).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of three counts of capital murder in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(18). The Jefferson Circuit Court, Alabama sentenced defendant to death. Defendant was also convicted of attempted murder, first-degree kidnapping, and first-degree robbery and was sentenced to serve consecutive terms of life in prison on those convictions. Defendant's motion for a new trial was denied by operation of law. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Alabama's method of execution was unconstitutional. However, he did not raise this claim in the trial court. Rather, he raises it for the first time on appeal. Therefore, we review this argument for plain error pursuant to Ala. R. App. P. 45A. The appellate court found that the Alabama Supreme Court had concluded that Alabama's use of lethal injection as a method of execution did not violate the Eighth Amendment to the United States Constitution. Therefore, there was no error, plain or otherwise, in that regard. Defendant's second argument was that indicting him for, convicting him of, and sentencing him for three counts of capital murder violated double jeopardy principles. He based his contention on the fact that all three counts, Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(1), Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) and Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(18) were predicated on the same act. The appellate court found that each offense required proof of an element the other did not require. Therefore, even though the counts were based on the same act, under Blockburger, defendant was properly indicted for, convicted of, and sentenced for three counts of capital murder.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences for capital murder during the course of a first-degree kidnapping, during the course of a first-degree robbery, and by or through the use of a deadly weapon, attempted murder, and first-degree kidnapping with regard to the toddlers were affirmed. Defendant's convictions and sentences for first-degree robbery and for the first-degree kidnapping of the adult victim could not stand. The case was remanded.

Newton v. State


CR-05-1517


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


78 So. 3d 458; 2009 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 122



October 2, 2009, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 1, 2011.
As Corrected August 1, 2011.
Rehearing denied by Newton v. State, 2009 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 195 (Ala. Crim. App., Oct. 30, 2009)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Newton v. Alabama, 182 L. Ed. 2d 177, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 1579 (U.S., Feb. 21, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Madison Circuit Court. (CC-01-49). Tom F. Young, Jr., Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of capital murder committed during the course of a first-degree robbery. Defendant was also convicted of first-degree arson under Ala. Code § 13A-7-41 and first-degree theft of property under Ala. Code § 13A-8-3(b). The Madison Circuit Court, Alabama sentenced defendant to death on the capital murder conviction, 15 years in prison on the arson conviction, and 10 years in prison on the theft conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's first argument was that the prosecution's opening statement in the penalty phase in which it stated to the jury that defendant had two prior robbery convictions but never proved such deprived defendant of his right to a fair sentencing hearing and his right to due process of law and protection from cruel and unusual punishment under the Eighth and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution. The appellate court found that during its closing argument, the State referred to only two aggravating circumstances, and the trial court instructed the jury on only those two aggravating circumstances. Under those circumstances, any error in that regard was harmless and the jury would have returned the same recommendation even without the error in the prosecutor's opening argument. The trial court did not err when it excluded evidence about the bad circumstances of defendant's upbringing because much of the information that was included in the excluded documentation was not relevant and could have resulted in a confusion of the issues for the jury, and the information that was relevant was merely cumulative to testimony that had not been disputed by the State.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

Johnson v. State


CR-99-1349


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


120 So. 3d 1130; 2009 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 124



October 2, 2009, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 28, 2011.

As Corrected July 18, 2011.

As Corrected January 22, 2014.

Released for Publication October 7, 2013.
Rehearing denied by Johnson v. State, 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 3000 (Ala. Crim. App., June 18, 2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Johnson v. Alabama, 134 S. Ct. 192, 187 L. Ed. 2d 131, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 7200 (U.S., Oct. 7, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Walker Circuit Court. (CC-99-19).
Johnson v. State, 120 So. 3d 1119, 2006 Ala. LEXIS 277 (Ala., Oct. 6, 2006)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from Walker Circuit Court, Alabama, where she was sentenced to death upon convicted of capital murder, in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(14), for intentionally murdering a witness in a criminal proceeding against defendant, where the murder stemmed from his role as a witness in a bigamy case against defendant. The Alabama Supreme Court reversed and remanded the court's prior decision reversing defendant's conviction.


OVERVIEW: Raising a multitude of issues, defendant first argued that the trial court erred by failing to allow her to impeach the State's primary witness with evidence of his prior convictions for distributing harmful material to minors and further failing to allow her to admit evidence of these convictions during the penalty phase of her trial. Affirming the conviction and sentence, the court ruled that the accomplice's prior convictions did not constitute one of the statutorily enumerated mitigating circumstances in Ala. Code § 13A-5-51. Moreover, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in determining that the prior convictions did not constitute a nonstatutory mitigating circumstance. The court also ruled that the evidence that defendant murdered the victim because he was going to testify in the bigamy proceedings against her both supported the jury's verdict and proved the aggravating circumstance. In defendant's capital murder case, where the jury clearly indicated that they were having difficulty understanding the aggravating and mitigating circumstances, the trial judge did not abuse his discretion in deciding to send the written instructions back with the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence of death.

 

438 of 745 DOCUMENTS


State v. Martin


CR-07-2011


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


56 So. 3d 709; 2009 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 112



August 28, 2009, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 1, 2011.
As Amended December 17, 2010.
Rehearing denied by State v. Martin, 2009 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1692 (Ala. Crim. App., Sept. 25, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Mobile Circuit Court. (CC-99-2696.60). Robert H. Smith, Trial Judge.
State v. Martin, 4 So. 3d 1196, 2008 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 157 (Ala. Crim. App., 2008)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of capital murder and the Mobile Circuit Court, Alabama sentenced him to death. The appellate court affirmed. The state supreme court reversed the death sentence and remanded to the appellate court which reversed the sentence and remanded to the trial court. On remand, the trial court sentenced defendant to death. The appellate court affirmed. Defendant filed a Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 petition and challenged his conviction.


OVERVIEW: An Ala. Code § 13A-5-9.1 motion involved reopening an existing case, in which there had been a conviction and sentence, for possible resentencing. Logically, then, any order either granting or denying a request for reconsideration of a sentence would be appealable. The circuit court's ruling in the instant case would, in effect, extend the proceedings on defendant's direct appeal from his conviction and sentence. Therefore, the appellate court concluded that the circuit court's order constituted a final judgment or ruling that supported an appeal to the appellate court. By its plain language, Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.1(f) applied only in situations where the notice of appeal from a conviction and sentence or from a dismissal or denial of a Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 petition was untimely. It did not mention and did not have any application to petitions for writs of certiorari in the Alabama Supreme Court. Therefore, the circuit court erred in granting defendant permission to file an out-of-time application for a rehearing with the appellate court and a petition for a writ of certiorari in the Alabama Supreme Court if the appellate court denied his application for a rehearing.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's order was reversed and the case was remanded for proceedings that were consistent with the opinion.

Gann v. City of Gulf Shores


CR-07-1765


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


29 So. 3d 244; 2009 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 99



August 7, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 19, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Baldwin Circuit Court. (CC-08-257) Charles C. Partin, Trial Judge..



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction by the Baldwin Circuit Court (Alabama) of violating Gulf Shores, Ala., Ordinance No. 1478, which prohibited smoking in enclosed public places, following the denial of her motions to dismiss the charge because Ord. 1478 was unconstitutional and for a judgment of acquittal, and sentence to a $ 50 fine.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that defendant did not have standing to raise the argument that Ordinance 1478 interfered with the property rights associated with the bar in which she worked as she had no property interest in the bar. Ordinance 1478 did not conflict with the Alabama Clean Indoor Air Act, Ala. Code § 22-15A-1 et seq. Ordinance 1478 did not include provisions that could not coexist with the Act or that would require the abrogation or abandonment of the Act. Both the ordinance and the Act were established for the same purpose and followed the same basic guidelines for enforcement and implementation; the penalty for violations of each were also similar. Ordinance 1478 merely added forums to the prohibition of smoking, which did not conflict with the subject or purpose of the state law. Under Ala. Code § 22-15A-10, municipalities were not restricted from adopting and enforcing local laws, ordinances, or regulations that complied with at least the minimum applicable standards set forth in the Act. Ordinance 1478 did not run afoul of Ala. Const. § 89 because it did not authorize the passing of any laws inconsistent with the laws of Alabama.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Toole


CR-07-2189


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


25 So. 3d 486; 2009 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 65



May 29, 2009, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 25, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC 08-816).



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a pretrial order by the Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama) that dismissed the indictment charging defendant with obstructing justice by using a false identity, a violation of Ala. Code § 13A-8-194; the State claimed that the indictment properly tracked the statutory language and was sufficient to put defendant on notice of the charge against her.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a passenger in an automobile that was pulled over by the police. During the traffic stop, defendant, who had an outstanding warrant for Medicaid fraud, provided a false date of birth and two false Social Security numbers, as well as a military identification with a false Social Security number. The appellate court found that the trial court was clearly aware of the grounds of the State's objections to the dismissal of the indictment because the grounds were those stated by the trial court. Since there were no proper grounds to justify the dismissal of the indictment, the State's general objection to the dismissal was sufficient to preserve the matter. In addition, the indictment tracked the language of § 13A-8-194, and was sufficient to place defendant on notice of the nature and cause of the charge against her. Finally, § 13A-8-194 was not unconstitutionally vague. Therefore, the trial court's dismissal of the indictment was erroneous.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Later proceeding at Bush v. State, 2009 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 3203 (Ala. Crim. App., July 24, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-81-1335.60). Truman M. Hobbs, Jr., Trial Judge.
Pringle v. State, 428 So. 2d 1380, 1983 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 4420 (Ala. Crim. App., 1983)
Ex parte Bush, 695 So. 2d 138, 1997 Ala. LEXIS 110 (Ala., 1997)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama) entered a judgment that denied defendant's Ala. R. Crim. OVERVIEW: Defendant and a companion entered a convenience store to rob it. When defendant was unable to open the cash register, he fatally shot the store clerk twice. Defendant and the companion fled. Defendant then shot a clerk at a different convenience store, killing him instantly. Defendant took some money from the cash register at that store and fled. It also found that he did not plead sufficient facts to show that he was entitled to postconviction relief or rebut the presumption that counsel provided effective assistance in defending him.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying defendant's postconviction petition attacking his capital murder conviction and sentence of death.

Byrd v. State


CR-07-0113


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


78 So. 3d 445; 2009 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 60



May 1, 2009, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 1, 2011.
As Amended May 31, 2011.
Rehearing denied by Byrd v. State, 2009 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 3192 (Ala. Crim. App., June 19, 2009)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Byrd v. Alabama, 182 L. Ed. 2d 177, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 1676 (U.S., Feb. 21, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-06-2222). J. William Cole, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of four counts of capital murder. Three counts were for his taking the lives of three persons during the course of a robbery (Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2)). The fourth count was based on his murder of two or more people by one act or pursuant to one scheme or course of conduct (§ 13A-5-40(a)(10)). The Jefferson County Court (Alabama) accepted the recommendation of the jury and sentenced him to death. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed he was mentally retarded and his death sentence was therefore cruel and unusual punishment under U.S. Const. amend. VIII. The appellate court disagreed. In Alabama, a person was deemed retarded if, before age 18, he manifested mental deficits and had an IQ of 70 or below. When he was 17, his IQ was 75; a pre-trial test placed his IQ at 72. The record established that he understood his Miranda rights and knowingly waived them. His statement that he did not "want to answer no more questions right now" did not clearly communicate a desire to cease all questioning. As police narrowly tailored their subsequent questions to clarify his ambiguous statement, his right to remain silent under U.S. Const. amend. V was not violated. He did not have standing to challenge the constitutionality of Alabama's judicial-override provision, Ala. Code § 13A-5-47(d), as the trial court followed the jury's recommendation. The sentence was not a product of passion, prejudice, or other arbitrary factors. Pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-5-53(b)(2) and (3), the appellate court found that the aggravating circumstances outweighed the mitigators, and that the death sentence was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

444 of 745 DOCUMENTS


State v. Anderson


CR-07-1171


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


8 So. 3d 1033; 2008 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 169



September 26, 2008, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-07-1531).



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to unlawfully breaking and entering a vehicle and second-degree property theft. The Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama) adjudicated him guilty of the first crime, but reserved adjudication of guilt on the theft charge so the State could present witnesses as to the factual basis for the plea. As the State did not present witnesses at sentencing as to the theft charge, the trial court dismissed that charge. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: In his plea colloquy, defendant admitted breaking a car window and taking $ 160 in cash from the car, but said that he did not take the CDs and the CD player police later found in his car. He claimed not to know how the CDs and CD player got into his car. The trial court reserved adjudication on the second degree theft of property charge, finding some question as to whether there was a factual basis for second or third degree theft of property. When the State failed to present testimony to establish a factual basis for second degree theft, the trial court dismissed that charge. The appellate court held that as the case involved a guilty plea rather than a trial, the trial court should not have dismissed the indictment based on lack of evidence to support the plea. By doing so, it encroached on the prosecutor's power to prosecute crimes conferred by Ala. Code § 12-17-184, in violation of the separation of powers doctrine, Ala. Const. art. III, § 43. It should have allowed the State to determine, in its discretion, whether to amend the charge to third-degree theft of property or to allow defendant to withdraw his plea and proceed to trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for proceedings that were consistent with the appellate court's opinion.

Thompson v. State


CR-07-0314


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


12 So. 3d 723; 2008 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 134



August 29, 2008, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication, June 18, 2009.
Dismissed by Thompson v. State, 2009 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1581 (Ala. Crim. App., Apr. 10, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Coffee Circuit Court. CC-07-100. Jeffrey W. Kelley, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.*



* Note from the reporter of decisions: On April 10, 2009, the Court of Criminal Appeals dismissed the appeal on Thompson's motion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Coffee Circuit Court (Alabama) of possession of a controlled substance, dihydrocodeinone, a violation of Ala. Code § 13A-12-212. The trial court sentenced defendant to five years in prison. The trial court also fined defendant as a subsequent offender pursuant to the Alabama Drug Demand Reduction Assessment Act and ordered him to pay an assessment to the Alabama Forensic Sciences Trust Fund. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that defendant was aware of the time and place for defendant's rescheduled trial and that defendant by his absence from the commencement of his trial had voluntarily waived under Ala. R. Crim. P. 9.1(b) his right to be present under Ala. R. Crim. P. 9.1(a). On appeal, the court found that, although the trial court's order referenced facts that would support a finding that defendant voluntarily absented himself from jury selection and the trial of the case, the record did not contain evidence in support of those facts. Therefore, there was no affirmative evidence in the record indicating that defendant had notice of the time and place of the trial after it was rescheduled. Accordingly, the circuit court on remand was to hold an evidentiary hearing on the issue of whether defendant waived his right to be present at jury selection and at trial.


OUTCOME: The cause was remanded to the circuit court with directions for that court to hold an evidentiary hearing on the issue of whether defendant waived his right to be present at jury selection and at trial.

 

446 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Hooks v. State


CR-04-2220


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


21 So. 3d 772; 2008 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 147



August 29, 2008, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 29, 2009.
As Corrected August 20, 2009.
Rehearing denied by Hooks v. State, 2008 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 904 (Ala. Crim. App., Dec. 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-85-588.60). William A. Shashy.
Ex parte Hooks, 534 So. 2d 371, 1988 Ala. LEXIS 382 (Ala., 1988)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a direct appeal affirmed a conviction for murder during the course of a robbery and the death sentence imposed, appellant inmate on death row appealed the decision of the Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama) that denied his Ala. R. Crim. P. 20 (now Ala. R. Crim. P. 32) petition for postconviction relief attacking his conviction and sentence on grounds of ineffective assistance of trial and appellate counsel.


OVERVIEW: Although the trial court adopted the State's proposed order denying relief, the inmate's due process rights were not violated because the circuit court's findings were not clearly erroneous. His right to an impartial jury was not violated because the juror misconduct claim was procedurally barred and due to be dismissed for that reason alone. Counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise a Batson or Powell challenge because those cases represented new law and were decided after defendant's trial. The inmate's claims of ineffective assistance of trial and appellate counsel had to be dismissed because he failed to meet his burden of proof under Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.3 and 32.6(b). His argument did not show deficient performance and prejudice, nor did he offer evidence to show how counsel could have argued claims more adequately such that the result would have been different. Under Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.2(a)(3), (a)(4) and (a)(5) the substantive ineffective assistance claims were procedurally barred because they could have been raised at trial or on appeal but were not, and many of the claims were addressed by the court on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the postconviction petition.

 

447 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Connell v. State


CR-06-0668


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


7 So. 3d 1068; 2008 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 108



May 30, 2008, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 27, 2009.
As Corrected August 29, 2008.
As Corrected November 3, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Bibb Circuit Court. (CC-05-8).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Bibb Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted him of capital murder in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40 and second-degree assault. The murder was made capital because defendant committed it (1) through the use of a deadly weapon while the victim was in a vehicle, (2) through the use of a deadly weapon fired from a vehicle, and (3) during the course of a first-degree robbery or an attempt thereof.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he was entitled to a jury trial on the issue of his competence to stand trial. The appellate court held that because the trial court found that there were not any grounds to doubt that defendant was competent to stand trial, defendant was not entitled to a jury trial on that issue. Under Ala. R. Crim. P. 11.6(a), the trial court had the authority to make a preliminary determination regarding whether there were reasonable grounds to doubt that defendant was competent to stand trial. The trial court properly admitted the victim's in-court identification into evidence. Even if the victim's pretrial identification was gained by impermissibly suggestive means, her trial testimony was clearly based on her independent recollection of defendant and the events on the night of the murder and assault. The trial court properly allowed evidence of defendant's prior bad acts. The evidence and the crimes were part of one continuous transaction. The jury could have reasonably concluded that the killing and robbery were part of a continuous chain of events, that defendant was an accomplice to the robbery, and that the robbery was intentional and not a mere afterthought.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

448 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Spencer v. State


CR-04-2570


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


58 So. 3d 215; 2008 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 74



April 4, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 29, 2008.
Released for Publication March 24, 2011.
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Spencer v. State, 58 So. 3d 215, 2009 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 18 (Ala. Crim. App., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-04-4129; CC-04-4130; CC-04-4131; CC-04-4132; CC-04-4383). Tommy Nail, Trial Judge.
Woods v. State, 13 So. 3d 1, 2007 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 218 (Ala. Crim. App., 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS TO CONVICTIONS; REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS AS TO SENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) convicted defendant of capital murder and attempted murder of four police officers, violations of Ala. Code §§ 13A-5-40(a)(5), (10), 13A-6-2, and 13A-4-2. The circuit court overrode a jury's recommendations and imposed the death sentence for the capital murder convictions and life in prison for the attempted murder conviction. Pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-5-53(a), the death sentence was automatically appealed.


OVERVIEW: An instruction on voluntary intoxication or the lesser included offense of reckless manslaughter was not required because there was insufficient evidence from which a jury could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was unable to form the requisite intent to commit capital murder due to the effects of intoxication as defined in Ala. Code § 13A-1-9(b). Defendant's rights under the Sixth Amendment and Ala. Const. art. I, § 6, were protected because an attachment under Ala. Code § 12-21-182(a) did not have to issue to secure the presence of a missing witness who had not been subpoenaed under Ala. R. Crim. P. 17.5. A self-defense instruction was not warranted. The limited mandates of Ring were satisfied because by returning a guilty verdict as to the capital offense of the murder, Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(10), the jury unanimously found at least one statutory aggravating circumstance, making defendant eligible for the death penalty. The sentencing order had to be clarified because the trial court did not make specific findings as to the nonstatutory mitigating circumstances, pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-5-52, or state why it overrode the jury's recommendation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions and remanded the case to amend the sentencing order to clarify the findings regarding the nonstatutory mitigating circumstances and judicial override of the jury's recommendation of life imprisonment without parole. On remand, the trial court was directed to reweigh the aggravating and mitigating circumstances and resentence defendant.

 

449 of 745 DOCUMENTS


State v. Livingston


CR-06-1846


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


8 So. 3d 1014; 2008 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 18



February 1, 2008, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied State v. Livingston, 8 So. 3d 1017, 2008 Ala. LEXIS 281 (Ala., Nov. 14, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-06-218).



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama) found that a felony indictment charging defendant, a convicted sex offender, with failure to notify the sheriff's department of a change in her residence at least 30 days prior to her move, violated the constitutional prohibition against ex post facto laws. Thus, the State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court's order specifically found that because the offense with which defendant was indicted was a class A misdemeanor at the time the offense was committed, the State could not properly indict her for the offense as a class C felony. But, it did not dismiss the indictment in whole or in part. Thus, contrary to the State's assertion that the court's order was fatal to the prosecution, the order did nothing to alter the elements that the State was required to prove in showing a violation of Ala. Code § 15-20-23. Second, the issue which was made the basis of the State's appeal was not one that could properly be the subject of a pretrial appeal by the State, pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 15.7. Thus, because the appeal did not fall into one of the other categories offering the State a limited right of appeal, pursuant to either Ala. Code § 12-12-70 or Ala. Code § 12-22-91, it had to be dismissed.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.
