Sharifi v. State


CR-04-1185


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


993 So. 2d 907; 2008 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 50



February 1, 2008, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended May 6, 2009. Released for Publication October 2, 2008.
Rehearing denied by, Without opinion by Sharifi v. State, 2008 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 124 (Ala. Crim. App., Mar. 21, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Motion denied by Sharifi v. Alabama, 555 U.S. 1010, 129 S. Ct. 491, 172 L. Ed. 2d 386, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 8006 (2008)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Sharifi v. State, 2016 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 57 (Ala. Crim. App., Sept. 9, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Madison Circuit Court. (CC-01-845). Laura W. Hamilton.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Madison Circuit Court (Alabama) of murdering two victims by one act or pursuant to one scheme or course of conduct, an offense defined as capital by Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(10). The jury recommended that defendant be sentenced to death. The circuit court followed the jury's recommendation and sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered the United States on a tourist visa and married his wife. His immigration status was changed to illegal alien. The State of Alabama presented evidence that the bodies of defendant's wife and another man were recovered from a river. The State also showed that a gun defendant owned was the murder weapon. On appeal, the court found that (1) defendant's rights under international treaties were not violated, nor were the remedies which he sought available under the treaties; (2) defendant's right to a speedy trial under the Sixth Amendment was not violated; (3) the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motions to remove jurors for cause; (4) the State did not violate the Equal Protection Clause by using its peremptory strikes to remove blacks and female jurors from the venire; (5) the trial court did not err by admitting an autopsy report as a business record; (6) the State's burden of proof in a capital case was beyond a reasonable doubt; (7) the jury instructions were correct except for a harmless error in the mitigation instruction; (8) the death penalty was not unconstitutional under the Eighth Amendment; and (9) the death sentence was properly imposed.


OUTCOME: The capital-murder conviction and the sentence of death were affirmed.

Saunders v. State


CR-05-0281


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


10 So. 3d 53; 2007 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 236



December 21, 2007, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 22, 2009.
As Corrected May 30, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Saunders v. State, 2008 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 109 (Ala. Crim. App., Jan. 25, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Saunders v. Alabama, 556 U.S. 1258, 129 S. Ct. 2433, 174 L. Ed. 2d 229, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 3939 (2009)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Saunders v. State, 107 So. 3d 232, 2011 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 815 (Ala. Crim. App., 2011)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Saunders v. State, 161 So. 3d 1232, 2013 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 784 (Ala. Crim. App., 2013)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Saunders v. State, 2016 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 78 (Ala. Crim. App., Dec. 16, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Baldwin Circuit Court. (CC-04-1741). Robert E. Wilters.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Baldwin Circuit Court (Alabama) convicting him of two counts of capital murder and one count of attempted murder, Ala. Code §§ 13A-6-2(a)(1) and 13A-4-2. The murder was made capital because it was committed during the course of a robbery in the first degree, Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2), and during the course of a burglary in the first degree, § 13A-5-40(a)(4).


OVERVIEW: The appeals court found that the evidence established all the elements of robbery-murder and burglary-murder, § 13A-5-40(a)(2), (a)(4), as defendant admitted he struck a victim on the head with a crowbar, that he feigned an asthma attack so that the victim's wife would let him into the house, and that he must have gone into the house to get money for crack cocaine. While inside the house, he stole money from a wallet and a purse and took keys to a vehicle. The evidence was sufficient for attempted murder, as he dragged the wife around the house by the neck and struck her repeatedly, causing her to fall to the ground and hit her head several times and causing her to fear for her life. The trial court's instruction on the "especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel" aggravator (Ala. Code § 13A-5-49(8)) and the trial court's finding that aggravating circumstance were not erroneous. Defendant repeatedly struck and then strangled the victim before inflicting the fatal blows, the initial blows and the strangulation would have caused appreciable suffering, and the victim suffered extreme psychological trauma because he knew death was imminent and that he was unable to protect his wife.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

Sneed v. State


CR-05-2033


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


1 So. 3d 104; 2007 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 223



December 21, 2007, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 4, 2009.
As Corrected June 16, 2009. As Corrected August 20, 2009.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Sneed v. Ala., 129 S. Ct. 1039, 173 L. Ed. 2d 472, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 937 (U.S., Jan. 26, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Morgan Circuit Court. (CC-93-1307.80). Sherrie W. Paler.
Sneed v. State, 783 So. 2d 874, 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 165 (Ala. Crim. App., 2000)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In 1996, in a second trial in the Morgan Circuit Court, Alabama, appellant was convicted of the capital offense of robbery-murder under Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2). After a sentencing hearing, by a vote of 7 to 5, the jury recommended that appellant be sentenced to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole. The trial court overrode the jury's recommendation and sentenced appellant to death. This appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of capital murder because he committed the murder during the course of a robbery. In imposing the death penalty, the trial court found the following aggravating circumstances: (1) appellant committed the capital offense while he was accomplice in the commission of a robbery; and (2) the offense was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel when compared to other capital offenses, Ala. Code § 13A-5-49(8). At the same time, (1) appellant did not have a significant history of prior criminal activity; (2) he was an accomplice to the robbery-murder and did not personally shoot and kill the victim; and (3) he was relatively young that the time of the offense, Ala. Code §§ 13A-5-51(1), (4), and (7). Further, he was from an abusive home, he was likely raped as a young boy, and his drug and alcohol problems drove him to a life of petty crimes. Moreover, the jury recommended that he be sentenced to life without the possibility of parole. In rejecting the jury's recommendation, the trial court properly weighed the aggravating circumstances and mitigating circumstances and correctly sentenced appellant to death.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction and death sentence were affirmed.

Harris v. State


CR-04-2363


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


2 So. 3d 880; 2007 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 224



December 21, 2007, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 4, 2009.
As Corrected May 6, 2008.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Crenshaw Circuit Court. (CC-02-106; CC-02-107; and CC-04-36). H. Edward McFerrin.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Crenshaw Circuit Court (Alabama) entered final judgments of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of two counts of murder for the killings of two people during the course of a burglary, two additional counts of murder for the deaths of two different people during the course of a burglary, and one murder count because his six victims were killed pursuant to one scheme or course of conduct. He was then sentenced to death. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Following a domestic dispute with his in-laws, defendant returned to their farm and shot to death his wife's grandmother, defendant's mother-in-law, father-in-law, and three brothers-in-law. Defendant was tried and convicted of two counts of murder made capital for the killings of two victims because the killings occurred during the course of a burglary, a violation of Ala. It also found that death was the proper punishment, and that neither Ring nor Apprendi prohibited the trial court from imposing a death sentence, especially since the jury found defendant to be eligible for it.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgments of conviction and sentence of death by lethal injection were affirmed.

Mashburn v. State


CR-06-0328


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


7 So. 3d 453; 2007 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 199



November 2, 2007, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 27, 2009.
Appeal after remand at Mashburn v. State, 7 So. 3d 453, 2008 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 90 (Ala. Crim. App., Apr. 25, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Calhoun Circuit Court. (CC-03-413). Samuel H. Monk II.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to five counts of capital murder. The matter was presented to a jury, which found defendant guilty and recommended that defendant be sentenced to death. The trial court accepted the jury's recommendation and sentenced defendant to death. Defendant filed a motion for a new trial, which was denied by the Calhoun Circuit Court (Alabama) by operation of law. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his Batson motion after the State used eight of its 40 peremptory strikes to remove black veniremembers. The prosecutor stated that he struck the challenged veniremembers based on their ambiguous answers to questions regarding the imposition of the death penalty or their opposition to the death penalty. The appellate court found that the State's reasons for its strikes were not pretextual, noting that the prosecutor struck both black and white veniremembers who indicated that they were unsure whether or not they favored the death penalty. The appellate court also found no merit in defendant's argument that the trial judge's failure to instruct him on the right to withdraw his guilty plea within 30 days of its entry voided the plea and thereby diminished the evidence presented to the jury to such a degree as to render their verdict improper because the withdrawal of a guilty plea was solely a matter within the discretion of a trial court. Finally, the appellate court upheld the imposition of the death penalty, noting, inter alia, that it had previously been held not to amount to cruel and usual punishment.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.

In his petition, defendant attacked his May 2004 conviction for sodomy in the first degree and his resulting sentence of 40 years' imprisonment. R. Crim. P. 32.3 and Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.6(b). Overall, the court found that defendant's allegations were insufficient and that despite the reasons stated by the trial court, it was affirming the summary denial of defendant's petition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary denial of defendant's petition.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Houston Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted him of capital murder, in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(1), and sentenced him to death. Based on defendant's claim on appeal regarding a Batson challenge, the court remanded the matter to the trial court for an evidentiary hearing on that issue. The matter was before the court on return from remand.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and others badly beat and killed a victim. Defendant was convicted of capital murder, based on it having been committed during a kidnapping in the first degree or an attempt thereof. The trial court accepted the jury's recommendation of the death sentence. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Eatmon v. State


CR-04-2241


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


992 So. 2d 64; 2007 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 126



August 31, 2007, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 11, 2008.
Related proceeding at Marshall v. State, 2008 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 142 (Ala. Crim. App., Aug. 29, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Eatmon v. Alabama, 129 S. Ct. 185, 172 L. Ed. 2d 132, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 7159 (U.S., Oct. 6, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. Bessemer Division. (CC-04-614). Teresa Petelos.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of two counts of murder made capital because it occurred during the first degree kidnapping of the two victims, and of two counts of murder made capital because the same victims were killed pursuant to one scheme or course of conduct. The Jefferson Circuit Court, Bessemer Division (Alabama), sentenced him to death for each count. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant beat one victim with an iron bar; the victims were bound and forced into the trunk of a car. Defendant and his accomplice doused the car with gasoline and kerosene and ignited it; the victims, who had been doused with gasoline, died in the fire. Defendant sought a continuance on grounds his mitigation expert could not complete his evaluation in time for the trial. The appellate court held that as defendant failed to show he expected the expert to adduce any valid mitigating circumstance, denial of the continuance motion was not an abuse of discretion. Defendant's claims that Alabama's statutory scheme allowing for judicial override of a jury's recommendation of life imprisonment without parole violated Ring v. Arizona, and that its death penalty violated the Fourth, Fifth, Sixth, Eighth, and Fourteenth Amendments, had been previously rejected. After the jury recommended life imprisonment without parole, the trial court properly ordered a presentence investigation report and made findings concerning aggravators and mitigators. Under Ala. Code § 13A-5-53(b)(3), his death sentence was not disproportionate or excessive when compared to the penalty imposed in similar cases.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and death sentence were affirmed.

Woods v. State


CR-05-0448


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


13 So. 3d 1; 2007 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 137



August 31, 2007, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication, June 18, 2009.
Appeal after remand at Woods v. State, 13 So. 3d 1, 2007 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 218 (Ala. Crim. App., Dec. 21, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. CC-04-4133; CC-04-4134; CC-04-4135; and CC-04-4384. Tommy Nail, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS TO CONVICTIONS; REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS AS TO SENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his convictions in the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) for four counts of capital murder in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(5), (10) for his involvement in the shootings of four police officers.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court found that the evidence was insufficient to sustain defendant's conviction as an accomplice pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-2-23. The State established that defendant and a co-defendant had engaged in a hostile, profanity-laced argument with officers on the morning of the subject shootings, and that defendant threatened an officer. In addition, testimony of three witnesses and others who testified about drug sales and gun possession established that drug sales and weapons were part of the res gestae or the continuous transaction of events in defendant's capital murder case, and was not improperly admitted. However, although the trial court thoroughly addressed and made specific fact findings regarding the statutory aggravating circumstances and statutory mitigating circumstances, it did not make specific findings regarding the existence or nonexistence of nonstatutory mitigating circumstances offered pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-5-52. Thus, although it was clear that the trial court considered the evidence defendant offered as nonstatutory mitigation, it was not clear whether the trial court found any of the evidence to constitute nonstatutory mitigation.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed. The case was remanded to the trial court for it to amend its sentencing order to clarify its findings regarding the nonstatutory mitigating circumstances. If it found it necessary, the trial court could reweigh the aggravating and mitigating circumstances and resentence defendant. The trial court's amended sentencing order was to be submitted to the court within 42 days.

State v. Turner


CR-06-1033


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


976 So. 2d 508; 2007 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 109



June 29, 2007, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 7, 2008.
Writ of mandamus denied Ex parte Turner, 2008 Ala. LEXIS 128 (Ala., June 27, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Limestone Circuit Court. (CC-99-318.60). James W. Woodroof, Jr.
Turner v. State, 924 So. 2d 737, 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 206 (Ala. Crim. App., 2003)



DISPOSITION: PETITION GRANTED; WRIT ISSUED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An inmate, convicted of capital murder in the course of a robbery, filed a petition for post-conviction relief under Ala. R. Crim. P. 32. The Limestone Circuit Court (Alabama) granted his motion for discovery of official documents relating to himself, his relatives, and two law enforcement officers. The State of Alabama filed a petition for a writ of mandamus directing the trial court to set aside its ruling.


OVERVIEW: The inmate sought discovery of the officers' personnel files, his own county jail records, and records of the Alabama Department of Human Resources (DHR) concerning his family members. The appellate court noted that a petitioner for post-conviction relief could not use the discovery process to "fish" through official files or to investigate possible claims. To obtain discovery, the inmate had to allege facts that, if proved, would entitle him to relief. He sought the officers' personnel files to find evidence to support his claim his counsel was ineffective for failing to properly impeach them. But as he failed to allege how he was prejudiced by counsel's failure to cross-examine and impeach the officers, he failed to satisfy his burden under Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.3 and 32.6(b) and failed to establish "good cause" for the disclosure of that information. Information in his jail records that he sought would have been, in part, cumulative to other evidence that had been presented. The information he sought from the DHR records was confidential and was available by questioning his family members. Accordingly, he failed to show good cause for the discovery of those records.


OUTCOME: The appellate court granted the State's petition and issued a writ of mandamus directing the trial court to set aside its ruling allowing the inmate the requested discovery.

 

462 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. State


CR-04-0293


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


11 So. 3d 866; 2007 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 111



June 29, 2007, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 15, 2009.
As Corrected May 7, 2008. As Corrected March 10, 2010.
Affirmed by Ex parte Brown, 11 So. 3d 933, 2008 Ala. LEXIS 205 (Ala., Oct. 3, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court Bessemer Division. (CC-02-348). Teresa Petelos.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Bessemer Division of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) of murder during the course of committing a robbery and a burglary, offenses defined as capital by Ala. Code §§ 13A-5-40(a)(2) and 13A-5-40(a)(4). The jury recommended that defendant be sentenced to death. The circuit court followed the jury's recommendation and sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The jury convicted defendant of murdering the victim during the course of a robbery and a burglary in the victim's home. On appeal, the court found that defendant's conviction and sentence were proper because (1) there was no indication that defense counsel suffered from any conflict, much less an actual conflict of interest; (2) the trial court did not deny defendant a fair and impartial trial by committing errors during jury selection; (3) the trial court did not err in allowing a police detective to testify about a statement defendant made to the police, in admitting photographs of the victim made during the autopsy and at the crime scene, or in admitting DNA evidence; (4) defendant was not denied a fair trial because of comments the prosecutor made during the guilt and sentencing phases of the trial; (5) the trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion for an acquittal; (6) there was not a material variance between the indictment and the proof at trial that affected defendant's substantial rights; (7) the trial court did not err in instructing the jury during the guilt and sentencing phases of the trial; and (8) the imposition of the death penalty was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence to death were affirmed.

Egbuonu v. State


CR-05-0143


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


993 So. 2d 35; 2007 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 90



May 25, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 29, 2008.

Released for Publication October 2, 2008.
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Egbuonu v. Oakdale, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 102636 (N.D. Ala., July 6, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-04-1422). Alfred Bahakel.
Ex parte Egbuonu, 911 So. 2d 755, 2005 Ala. LEXIS 58 (Ala., 2005)



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.*



* Note from the reporter of decisions: On February 22, 2008, on return to remand, the Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed, without opinion. On March 21, 2008, that court denied rehearing, without opinion. On May 9, 2008, the Alabama Supreme Court denied certiorari review, without opinion (1070921).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant was convicted of two counts of identity theft (Ala. Code § 13A-8-192(a)), the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) sentenced him to 10 years' imprisonment for each conviction, to run consecutively. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: A sheriff's office employee learned that someone had opened credit card accounts in his name at four stores. The State presented evidence that defendant's handwriting was on the credit applications for accounts at one store, that a phone call adding another name to one of the accounts was placed from a cell phone found in defendant's apartment, and that defendant had picked up mail at a mailbox listed as the address of the account holder. The appellate court held that as defendant failed to bring an alleged Brady violation to the trial court's attention until after his conviction, he waived any objection. His other arguments either failed to comply with Ala. R. App. P. 28(a)(10) or were meritless. However, the appellate court took notice, sua sponte, of what it deemed to be a double-jeopardy violation, as such a transgression implicated the jurisdiction of the trial court. Since both of the charges stemmed from the same theft of the employee's identity, and the two charges were merely based on alternative methods of proving that single theft, defendant's convictions and sentences for two counts of identity theft for a single theft violated double-jeopardy principles.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded with instructions to the trial court to enter a new order that adjudged defendant guilty of the single offense of identity theft and sentenced him for that single offense. The appellate court pretermited discussion of defendant's remaining issue pending the trial court's return to its remand.

Hodges v. State


CR-04-1226


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


147 So. 3d 916; 2007 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 62



March 23, 2007, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 20, 2015.

 [**1] As Corrected May 9, 2007. Released for Publication August 5, 2014.
Post-conviction proceeding at, Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Hodges v. State, 147 So. 3d 916, 2008 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 137 (Ala. Crim. App., Aug. 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Lee Circuit Court. (CC-99-264.60). Robert M. Harper (retired) and Jacob A. Walker III, Trial Judges.
Ex parte Hodges, 856 So. 2d 936, 2003 Ala. LEXIS 84 (Ala., 2003)



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32, an inmate, who had been convicted of capital-murder and sentenced to death, filed a petition for postconviction relief raising numerous claims, including ineffective assistance of counsel. The State moved for summary dismissal as to a majority of the claims. The Lee Circuit Court (Alabama) granted the motion. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: Among other things, the appellate court held that the fact that the circuit court adopted the State's proposed order did not, without more, support the inmate's claim that reversal was due. The inmate made numerous claims of ineffective assistance of counsel, for which the inmate was required to identify specific acts or omissions of counsel that were alleged not to have been the result of reasonable professional judgment. The appellate court found summary dismissal of these claims proper because the inmate failed to plead sufficient facts supporting both prongs of the Strickland test, and merely asserted bare conclusions of deficient performance and prejudice. The appellate court did find, however, that the inmate pled sufficient facts to support the claim that counsel was ineffective for failing to conduct adequate mitigation investigation and failing to present mitigation evidence that counsel should have discovered. The appellate court further found that it was not plausible that the circuit court had personal knowledge of the facts underlying such claims and thus, the inmate should have been afforded an opportunity to present evidence in support thereof.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded for the circuit court to either conduct an evidentiary hearing or accept evidence in the form of affidavits, written interrogatories, or depositions regarding the inmate's allegations that trial counsel failed to conduct an adequate mitigation investigation and failed to adequately present mitigation evidence at the penalty phase.

 

466 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Brooks v. State


CR-03-1113


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


973 So. 2d 380; 2007 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 50



March 2, 2007, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Brooks v. Alabama, 128 S. Ct. 806, 169 L. Ed. 2d 608, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 13032 (U.S., Dec. 10, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Talladega Circuit Court. (C-03-693; CC-03-694; CC-03-695; and CC-03-696).
Brooks v. State, 2006 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 129 (Ala. Crim. App., June 30, 2006)



DISPOSITION: OPINION OF JUNE 30, 2006, WITHDRAWN; OPINION SUBSTITUTED; APPLICATIONS OVERRULED; AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of four counts of capital murder, attempted murder, robbery, and burglary. The jury unanimously recommended sentencing appellant to death for his capital-murder convictions. The Talladega Circuit Court, Alabama, accepted the jury's recommendation and sentenced appellant to death. In addition, the trial court sentenced appellant to life imprisonment for his other convictions. This appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant raised eight issues on appeal. Most were rejected, but the appellate court identified error with respect to appellant's convictions of burglary and capital murder during a robbery. Appellant's burglary conviction was vacated as violating double jeopardy principles because the burglary underlying appellant's conviction of capital murder during a burglary under Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(4) was the same burglary that formed the basis for the separate indictment charging burglary under Ala. Code § 13A-7-5. Although defendant's robbery conviction under Ala. Code § 13A-8-41 did not require reversal on double jeopardy grounds, his conviction for capital murder during a robbery under Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) was reversed because the trial court's jury instructions constituted an amendment to defendant's capital-murder-during-a-robbery indictment. The jury instructions changed the robbery from the robbery of the victim's father to the robbery of the victim and thus charged a new or different offense that was not contemplated by the original indictment, running afoul of Ala. R. Crim. P. 13.5. As such, the jury-instruction amendment constituted plain error under Ala. R. App. P. 45A.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed appellant's convictions and death sentence for three counts of capital murder. The court likewise affirmed appellant's convictions and sentences for attempted murder and robbery. However, the court reversed the convictions for one count of capital murder and for burglary, and remanded the case to the trial court to vacate those convictions.

Belisle v. State


CR-02-2124


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


11 So. 3d 256; 2007 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 49



March 2, 2007, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication June 15, 2009.
As Corrected May 6, 2008. As Corrected March 10, 2010.
Affirmed by Ex parte Belisle, 11 So. 3d 323, 2008 Ala. LEXIS 280 (Ala., Oct. 3, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Marshall Circuit Court. (CC-99-200075). Tim Jolley.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of two counts of murder during the course of a robbery and a burglary, offenses defined as capital by Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(4). Defendant waived his sentencing hearing before a jury, and the Marshall Circuit Court (Alabama) sentenced defendant to death. Pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-5-55, an automatic appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: After reviewing defendant's conviction and sentence for plain error, the appellate court found nothing worthy of reversal. Among other things, the appellate court found no speedy-trial violation where a majority of the delays during the four years defendant awaited trial were due to motions filed by defendant and defendant failed to assert the right until 10 months before trial. The appellate court also held that defendant was not entitled to hybrid representation. A sua sponte change of venue was not required merely because there was publicity surrounding defendant's case. Contrary to defendant's contention, Ala. Code § 13A-5-54 was not violated where at least one of his attorney's met the statutory experience requirements. The appellate court further found no error in the denial of defendant's various challenges for cause, as any of the chosen jurors who initially indicated a potential bias were rehabilitated during voir dire. As for the alleged hearsay violations, the appellate court concluded that a majority of instances cited did not constitute hearsay and in the others, the testimony was merely cumulative of other lawfully admitted testimony and thus, any error was harmless.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

468 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Griggs v. State


CR-06-0002


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


980 So. 2d 1031; 2006 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 300



December 20, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication April 4, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Mobile Circuit Court. (CC-82-3594.61). Ferrill D. McRae.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to unlawful possession of pentazocine and/or meprobamate. He was sentenced to 20 years in prison. Defendant's Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 petition challenging his conviction was summarily denied by the Mobile Circuit Court (Alabama). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Ala. Code § 20-2-70 was unconstitutional. The appellate court held that the claim was time-barred as it was not raised at trial and on appeal. Defendant was sentenced under the Alabama Habitual Offender Act, Ala. Code § 13A-5-9. Because the sentences applicable to drug offenses and repeat drug offenses were provided within the Alabama Controlled Substances Act, Ala. Code § 20-2-1 et seq., defendant had to be sentenced under its provisions. Defendant should not have been sentenced as a habitual offender. If defendant did not have any prior convictions for violations of the Alabama Controlled Substances Act, he should have been sentenced pursuant to Ala. Code § 20-2-70, rather than pursuant to the recidivist provisions in Ala. Code § 20-2-76. Under Ala. Code § 20-2-70, the proper range of punishment was not less than 2 nor more than 15 years in prison. If this section applied, defendant's sentence of 20 years in prison was excessive. The indictment did not allege that defendant had any prior convictions pursuant to the Alabama Controlled Substances Act. so defendant's argument might be meritorious.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded with instructions that the trial court make written findings as to whether defendant was sentenced pursuant to the Alabama Habitual Felony Offender Act or pursuant to Ala. Code § 20-2-76, whether he had any prior convictions for violations of the Alabama Controlled Substances Act, and whether any such prior convictions were used to enhance his sentence. If defendant was improperly sentenced, he was to be resentenced.

Ingram v. State


CR-03-1707


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


51 So. 3d 1094; 2006 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 214



September 29, 2006, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication November 29, 2010.

As Amended May 31, 2011.
Rehearing denied by Ingram v. State, 2006 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 3253 (Ala. Crim. App., Dec. 8, 2006)
Reversed by, Remanded by Ingram v. State, 51 So. 3d 1119, 2010 Ala. LEXIS 45 (Ala., Mar. 19, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Talladega Circuit Court. (CC-94-260.60). Jerry L. Fielding and William E. Hollingsworth III, Trial Judges.
Ex parte Ingram, 779 So. 2d 1283, 2000 Ala. LEXIS 263 (Ala., 2000)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged the judgment of the Talladega Circuit Court (Alabama), which summarily denied appellant's Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 petition for postconviction relief. Appellant was an inmate on death row after his conviction for murder, during the course of a kidnapping, an offense defined as capital by Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(1). Appellant's capital-murder conviction and death sentence were affirmed on direct appeal.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's conviction arose from the kidnapping of a man, taking him to a ballpark, taping him to a bench, and burning him to death for failing to pay appellant and co-defendants $ 200 for cocaine the victim had purchased a few days prior. Appellant asserted on appeal that the trial court erred by adopting the State's proposed order denying his petition verbatim. The court found no error, holding that even when the trial court adopts a proposed order by the State in toto, appellant still had the burden of showing that the findings of fact and conclusions of law were clearly erroneous before an appellate court will reverse the order on the sole basis that the order was drafted by the State. The court set forth numerous reasons how appellant failed to show clear error. Specifically, the trial court did not err by not appointing counsel to appellant before denying the petition because the record affirmatively showed that at all times during the postconviction proceedings appellant was represented by counsel. Further, none of the ineffective assistance of counsel claims raised by appellant were found to have any merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's postconviction petition.

City of Montgomery v. Zgouvas


CR-05-0039


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


953 So. 2d 434; 2006 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 208



September 29, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 29, 2007.
 [**1] Released for Publication March 23, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-05-5022). Tracy S. McCooey.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in a municipal court of violating Montgomery, Ala. Ordinance No. 1-9, for making harassing communications in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-11-8(b). Defendant appealed. The Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama) granted defendant's motion to dismiss the charge. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The complainant assisted defendant with a purchase he was making for his girlfriend. After the first encounter, defendant continued to send the complainant gifts and call the complainant at work, despite the complainant's repeated requests that defendant stop. Although defendant could challenge the constitutionality of Ala. Code § 13A-11-8(b)(1) based on a contention that it was overbroad, the appellate court held that defendant lacked standing to challenge the statute as being vague because defendant's acts, if true, clearly indicated that, if true, defendant's apparent intent was to harass, not alarm, the complainant. In upholding the constitutionality of § 13A-11-8(b)(1), the appellate court noted that the word "alarm" as used in the statute did not make it criminal to forecast a storm, predict political trends, or warn against epidemics of illness, as contended by defendant. When considering the word in the context of the entire section of the statute, it was obvious that the legislature intended the word "alarm" to only apply to situations when the speaker's words or actions caused fear of imminent danger, and that danger in some way found its impetus with the speaker.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's order dismissing the charge against defendant was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Blackmon v. State


CR-01-2126


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


7 So. 3d 397; 2006 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 184



August 25, 2006, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
As Corrected January 8, 2007. As Corrected August 20, 2009.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Blackmon v. Ala., 129 S. Ct. 2052, 173 L. Ed. 2d 1136, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 3189 (U.S., Apr. 27, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Houston Circuit Court. (CC-99-1177) Larry K. Anderson.
Blackmon v. State, 7 So. 3d 397, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 137 (Ala. Crim. App., Aug. 5, 2005)



DISPOSITION: APPLICATION OVERRULED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed an application for rehearing, challenging the judgment of the Houston Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted defendant of capital murder based on the beating death of her 28-month old daughter, in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(15), The court had already affirmed defendant's conviction and death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Because defendant's trial counsel was suspended from the practice of law, the court allowed her newly retained counsel the rare opportunity to file a brief on rehearing that raised new issues. As such, the court applied a plain error standard of review. Defendant raised numerous new issues, including that the State violated Batson by using peremptory strikes in a discriminatory manner and by discriminating against jurors based on gender. The court found that both white and black jurors were removed by peremptory strikes and that the State struck nine males and nine females. As such, there was no inference of purposeful discrimination drawn constituting plain error. The court found no error with regard to the admission of evidence or the comments made by the prosecutor, as well as the trial court's consideration of nonstatutory aggravating circumstances that the victim was adopted and abused. The court found that the trial court's sentencing order reflected that it found and considered one statutory aggravating circumstance, that the murder was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel when compared to other capital offenses, and that such consideration was within its province.


OUTCOME: The court overruled defendant's application for rehearing.

Brown v. State


CR-01-1900


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


982 So. 2d 565; 2006 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 63



April 28, 2006, Released

Petition for certiorari filed at, 02/11/2008

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Houston Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted defendant of capital murder for the intentional murder of an elderly woman during the commission of a burglary in the first degree, in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(4) (1975). Defendant was sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from his forced entry into the victim's apartment. He hog-tied the woman and gagged her so viciously, that her dentures were pushed to the back of her throat. Edmond v. State


CR-04-2392

James v. State


CR-04-0395


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


61 So. 3d 332; 2006 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 64



April 28, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication April 18, 2011.
Rehearing overruled by James v. State, 2006 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 177 (Ala. Crim. App., Aug. 25, 2006)
Reversed by, Remanded by Ex parte James, 61 So. 3d 352, 2009 Ala. LEXIS 260 (Ala., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-95-4747.60). Michael W. McCormick, Trial Judge.
James v. State, 788 So. 2d 185, 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 82 (Ala. Crim. App., 2000)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of the capital offense of burglary-murder for the killing of his former girlfriend, Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(4), and sentenced to death. He filed an Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 petition, challenging his conviction and sentence, and he subsequently amended his petition. After the State responded, the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) conducted an evidentiary hearing and denied the petition. The instant appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: Among other findings, appellant's ineffective-assistance-of-trial-counsel claim was precluded pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.2(a)(2), (a)(4), because it was raised and addressed at trial and on direct appeal. Appellant's claim of incompetency to stand trial also failed, as although appellant alleged that he had several mental problems, he did not allege any specific facts in his petition to indicate that he did not have the ability to assist in his defense and that he was not able to consult with trial counsel to a reasonable degree of rational understanding of the facts of his case and the legal proceedings against him; therefore, he had not satisfied his burden of pleading and proof as to this claim pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.3 and 32.6(b). In addition, a clinical psychologist in a previous appeal had concluded that he was competent to stand trial. That appellate counsel did not argue that the trial court erred in not instructing the jury each day before it separated did not constitute ineffective assistance; as long as the court properly admonished the jury once pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 19.3(b), it was not error for the court not to so admonish the jury every day.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Gaddy v. State


CR-02-2247


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


952 So. 2d 1149; 2006 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 32



March 3, 2006, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 28, 2007.
 [**1] As Corrected July 3, 2006.
Rehearing denied by, Without opinion by Gaddy v. State, 2006 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 321 (Ala. Crim. App., June 16, 2006)
Writ of certiorari denied Ex parte Gaddy, 952 So. 2d 1174, 2006 Ala. LEXIS 265 (Ala., Sept. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-90-2057.60). James H. Hard IV.
Ex parte Gaddy, 698 So. 2d 1150, 1997 Ala. LEXIS 103 (Ala., 1997)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, an inmate, appealed a decision from the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama), which denied his petition for postconviction relief (PCR) pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32. The inmate had been convicted of capital murder during the course of a robbery, and he was sentenced to death pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2).


OVERVIEW: The victim was brutally stabbed and strangled. His vehicle was stopped after it was associated with two robberies. The inmate, who was in the backseat, was Mirandized and he confessed. His conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal, and he filed his PCR petition. He amended the petition and after an evidentiary hearing, the trial court denied relief. On appeal, the court found that the inmate's claim as to ineffectiveness due to his counsel's lack of required experience under Ala. Code § 13A-5-54 was procedurally barred, and a showing under Strickland was required. As the inmate's confession was deemed voluntary, there was no ineffectiveness as to the suppression issue, and a jury instruction thereon was deemed harmless error, which did not satisfy the prejudice prong of Strickland. There was also no ineffectiveness in counsel's failure to object to other jury instructions, no inadequate investigation shown, and no failure to seek assistance of experts. Other claims were waived where there was insufficient support under Ala. R. App. P. 28. Counsel was effective during the penalty phase, there was no cumulative error, and many claims were procedurally barred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

477 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. State


CR-04-1183


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


946 So. 2d 903; 2006 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 2



February 3, 2006, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 17, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Jones v. State, 2006 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 308 (Ala. Crim. App., Mar. 10, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-04-3321). James H. Hard IV.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted him of two counts of capital murder committed during the course of a robbery or an attempted robbery, in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) and (10). Defendant was sentenced to death, and his new trial motion was denied by operation of law.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed his parents during the course of a robbery or attempted robbery, which was deemed pursuant to one scheme or course of conduct. He admitted to the actions, noting that he wanted to relieve them of the pain that he had continually caused them through his drug addictions and criminal history. Evidence included testimony regarding defendant's extensive psychological problems. The trial court accepted the jury's recommendation of the death sentence. On appeal, the court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding that defendant's statements were made to police voluntarily and after he was Mirandized and waived his rights. Denial of suppression of evidence seized from two residences and from his mother's vehicle was proper, as defendant lacked standing under U.S. Const. amend. IV to challenge searches of one residence and of the vehicle, and there was third party consent as to the other residence. There was sufficient evidence to support defendant's convictions and the aggravated factors under Ala. Code §§ 13A-5-40 and 13A-5-49, and lack of a diminished capacity defense under Ala. Code § 13A-3-1 did not violate defendant's constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

O'Callaghan v. State


CR-04-1941


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


945 So. 2d 467; 2006 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 17



February 3, 2006, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 16, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-03-3588). Clyde E. Jones.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS TO CONVICTION; REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS AS TO SENTENCING. *



* Note from the reporter of decisions: On March 17, 2006, on return to remand, the Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed, without opinion. On April 14, 2006, that court denied rehearing, without opinion. On June 9, 2006, the Supreme Court denied certiorari review, without opinion (1051036).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) of unlawful manufacture of a controlled substance in the first degree, under Ala. Code § 13A-12-218. She was sentenced to 10 years' imprisonment, and a $ 1,000 penalty was imposed, under Ala. Code § 13A-12-281(a). She appealed.


OVERVIEW: Material to make methamphetamine was found in defendant's truck. The appellate court held Ala. Code § 13A-12-218, barring "clandestine laboratory operations," was not void for vagueness by not stating where the methamphetamine had to be made, as a definition of a "clandestine laboratory operation" was transporting materials, and, under Ala. Code § 15-2-2, venue was where the crime occurred. Ala. Code § 13A-12-217(a)(2) said defendant had to possess precursor substances, but, under Ala. Code § 1-1-2, the plural included the singular, so possessing one precursor substance was required. She did not have to operate or intend to operate a lab in the county where she was prosecuted, as a "clandestine laboratory operation" was transporting materials. Testimony about a business located within 200 feet of where an officer first saw defendant's truck showed a clandestine laboratory operation within 500 feet of a business. Her request for her criminal history did not seek Ala. R. Evid. 404(b) evidence, so her subsequent criminal act could be introduced without notice, especially as it was a subsequent act. A $ 1,000 penalty, under Ala. Code § 13A-12-281(a), was erroneously imposed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed, but the matter was remanded for the trial court to set aside its imposition of a $ 1,000 fine.

 

479 of 745 DOCUMENTS


L.J.K. v. State


CR-04-0060


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


942 So. 2d 854; 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 263



December 23, 2005, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected June 5, 2006. As Corrected August 11, 2006. Released for Publication November 1, 2006.
Rehearing overruled by L.J.K. v. State, 942 So. 2d 854, 2006 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 40 (Ala. Crim. App., Mar. 3, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Dale Circuit Court. (CC-03-144). Kenneth W. Quattlebaum.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Dale Circuit Court (Alabama), which acquitted him of one count of sodomy, but which convicted him as charged on two counts of sodomy and three counts of sexual abuse, and which sentenced him to 10 years' concurrent imprisonment for each sexual abuse convictions and to consecutive life imprisonment sentences for each sodomy conviction.


OVERVIEW: The trial court overruled defendant's objections to testimony regarding hearsay statements made by the children victims, but that ruling was conditioned on the three children testifying. When the children were determined to be incompetent to testify, however, defendant did not renew his objection, move to exclude the hearsay statements, or move for a mistrial. He did not raise the matter of their hearsay statements until his motion for a new trial, which was made after his convictions and which was denied. He raised the same arguments challenging the hearsay nature of the testimony on appeal, but the court found that he failed to preserve the issue for appellate review by failing to raise the objection again. Also, because the hearsay statements were admitted without a proper objection, they were legal evidence. Therefore, defendant's argument regarding the sufficiency of the evidence without those hearsay statements was moot. Finally, defendant failed to properly raise issues in his appellate brief to satisfy Ala. R. App. P. 28(a)(10) because he did not support them with authority or he did not raise the issues until his reply brief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

 

480 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Sellers v. State


CR-04-1552


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


935 So. 2d 1207; 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 262



December 23, 2005, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected June 5, 2006. Released for Publication June 19, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-04-957).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction entered by the Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama) pursuant to a plea agreement for violating the Community Notification Act, Ala. Code § 15-20-20 et seq., specifically, Ala. Code § 15-20-26(c). Defendant reserved his right to appeal the denial of his motions to dismiss the indictment and to have § 15-20-26(c) declared unconstitutional as well as the sufficiency of the factual basis for his guilty plea.


OVERVIEW: The parties' stipulation of facts indicated that defendant, an adult registered sex offender, allowed a friend and her two-year-old daughter to stay at his residence for four days. The friend stated that she had nowhere else to go and that defendant slept in his truck while she and her child slept inside the house. Defendant claimed that § 15-20-26(c) was void for vagueness because it did not specifically define "living accommodation." Upon review of other provisions of the Act, precedent, and dictionary definitions, the court held that the plain, ordinary meaning of that term applied and that "living accommodation" meant any overnight lodging, either temporary or permanent. Thus, § 15-20-26(c) was not unconstitutionally vague. The indictment was properly amended under Ala. R. Crim. P. 13.5(a) to add an essential element, the phrase "where a minor resides," because the indictment otherwise charged an offense and the record indicated that defendant was fully aware of the charge against him. Defendant's challenge to the factual basis of his guilty plea had no merit based on the facts stipulated to and the interpretation of "living accommodation" in § 15-20-26(c).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Robitaille v. State


CR-01-2271


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


971 So. 2d 43; 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 237



November 23, 2005, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected July 3, 2006. Released for Publication January 11, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Robitaille v. State, 2006 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 341 (Ala. Crim. App., Jan. 27, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Robitaille v. Alabama, 128 S. Ct. 490, 169 L. Ed. 2d 339, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 11818 (U.S., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Cullman Circuit Court. 1 (CC-2002-221). Bobby R. Aderholt.


1 Robitaille was indicted by a Marion County grand jury for six counts of capital murder. Counsel moved for a change of venue; the case was transferred to Cullman County.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Cullman Circuit Court (Alabama) of six counts of capital murder for murdering the victim and her children during the course of a robbery. He was sentenced to death. The court considered the appeal, which was automatic in a death-penalty case.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court found, among other things, that the State's evidence was more than sufficient to convict defendant of capital murder. He confessed that he murdered the victims, he gave a detailed account of the injuries that he inflicted on each victim, and those details were corroborated by the wounds each victim sustained. When defendant was arrested he was in possession of a tool that was consistent with some of the injuries sustained by one of the victims. Counsel's performance was not ineffective, as counsel billed for approximately 210 hours related to the case, filed numerous and varied pretrial motions, and moved for a change of venue, which was granted. Counsel also filed a multitude of motions that were typically filed in capital cases, but had the Herculean task of representing a defendant who had confessed to murder. Defendant's sentence was appropriate under Ala. Code § 13A-5-53(b)(3) as neither disproportionate nor excessive to the sentences imposed in other capital cases; he viciously stabbed and killed a mother and her two small children while they were in their home, then took money and other items from the home.


OUTCOME: The capital-murder convictions and defendant's sentence of death were affirmed.

Gilmore v. State


CR-04-1363


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


937 So. 2d 547; 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 230



November 23, 2005, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected June 5, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Lee Circuit Court. (CC-04-13.60).



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Lee Circuit Court (Alabama) summarily dismissed defendant's petition for postconviction relief, filed pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32, in which he challenged his February 2004 guilty-plea conviction for first-degree robbery and the resulting sentence of 21 years' imprisonment. Defendant appealed this order.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held that defendant's petition lacked merit and failed to state a claim for which relief could be granted. Defendant alleged on appeal that this was error. His first challenge was that the reference to Ala. Code § 13A-8-43 in the body of Ala. Code § 13A-8-41 violated Ala. Const. art. IV, § 45, which outlined the one-subject rule. However, this claim lacked merit, as both sections under chapter 13A fell within the exception for bills adopting a code. Second, defendant's claim that his indictment was void because it failed to allege the material element of intent also lacked merit, but claims regarding the involuntariness of his plea required remand as the trial court's order made no specific findings of fact regarding the merits of this claim. Given that defendant timely filed his petition under Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.2(c), his ineffective-assistance-of-counsel claim was not procedurally barred. Moreover, because this claim also involved his counsel's conduct as it related to the alleged errors during the plea proceeding, the court could not say that defendant failed to plead any facts which would entitle him to relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was remanded.

Burgess v. State


CR-02-0977


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


962 So. 2d 272; 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 197



September 30, 2005, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected July 3, 2006. Released for Publication July 26, 2007.
Adhered to, On rehearing at Burgess v. State, 962 So. 2d 272, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 228 (Ala. Crim. App., Nov. 23, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Colbert Circuit Court. (CC-94-781.60). Harold V. Hughston, Jr.
Ex parte Burgess, 723 So. 2d 770, 1998 Ala. LEXIS 235 (Ala., 1998)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed the denial by the Colbert Circuit Court (Alabama) of his petition for postconviction relief filed pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32, attacking his capital-murder conviction and death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that trial counsel was ineffective for permitting the State to introduce evidence of his prior acts of abuse toward the victim, first claiming that evidence of his abusive relationship with the victim was inadmissible because it permitted jurors to infer his guilt based on his prior conduct toward her. The appeals court found that his prior acts of violence were admissible under the motive and intent exceptions to Ala. R. Evid. 404(b). The evidence against him was overwhelming, and the circuit court's failure sua sponte to instruct the jury on the use of the prior bad acts would not have prejudiced his substantial rights. Defendant failed to meet either prong of the Strickland test. There was no evidence indicating that the expert assistance he received at trial failed to meet the Ake standards, and the circuit court did not err in denying his request for funds to hire yet more experts for the postconviction proceedings. Defendant was not mentally retarded under the most liberal definition of mental retardation adopted by the Alabama Supreme Court in Perkins. Therefore, Atkins did not bar the death sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Benjamin v. State


CR-03-2040


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


940 So. 2d 371; 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 199



September 30, 2005, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Appeal after remand at Benjamin v. State, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 225 (Ala. Crim. App., Nov. 23, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Houston Circuit Court. (CC-01-293).



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Houston Circuit Court (Alabama) that denied his motion for a new trial; defendant claimed, inter alia, that the trial court erred in admitting an audio-taped conversation between him and a confidential informant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant went to a mall with the specific intent of finding a victim to rob. As the victim approached, defendant demanded his wallet. A struggle ensued, and the defendant struck the victim several times and shot him twice. The victim was dead when the police and paramedics arrived. Defendant later related all of the details of the crime to a friend, who had previously arranged for a body wire so that the police could hear defendant's confession. The appellate court held, inter alia, that even though a police officer was not a party to the conversation between defendant and the informant, because he monitored the conversation while it was occurring and testified that the audiotape was a reliable representation of the conversation, his testimony established a foundation for the admissibility of the audiotape under Ala. R. Evid. 901(a), (b)(5) without violating the Confrontation Clause. However, the trial court did not make specific written findings concerning the existence or nonexistence of each aggravating, mitigating, and nonstatutory mitigating circumstance enumerated in Ala. Code §§ 13A-5-49, 13A-5-51, 13A-5-52. Consequently, it failed to comply with Ala. Code § 13A-5-47(d).


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed; the case was remanded for the trial court to amend its sentencing order.

Houston v. State


CR-04-0480


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


933 So. 2d 397; 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 151



August 26, 2005, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended February 9, 2006.
Rehearing denied by, Without opinion by Houston v. State, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1913 (Ala. Crim. App., Oct. 7, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Limestone Circuit Court. (CC-03-913).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed after he was convicted by a jury in the Limestone Circuit Court (Alabama) under Ala. Code § 13A-8-2 for theft by deception.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was the successful bidder for a tractor offered through an Internet auction service. He made a down payment on the tractor and arranged to pay the remainder of the purchase price when he picked the tractor up. Defendant paid with a check. He stopped payment on the check after returning home to North Carolina. When asked why, defendant told the seller he knew the tractor had a defect, he knew the seller would not give him his money back, and thus, he knew what he had to do. The court affirmed, holding that 1) jurisdiction in an Alabama trial court was proper because it could be inferred from the evidence that when defendant tendered the check for the balance due on the tractor, he had formed the intent to take the tractor and stop payment on the check; 2) the evidence supported a finding that the case involved a criminal theft of property rather than a prosecution for a civil debt; 3) the evidence supported a finding that the case involved a criminal theft rather than the collection of a civil debt; and 4) the evidence was sufficient for a jury to have inferred that defendant had a preexisting intent for the theft when he issued a check on which he could stop payment.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Minnifield v. State


CR-04-0171


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


941 So. 2d 1000; 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 149



August 26, 2005, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
As Amended February 9, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Minnifield v. State, 2006 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 239 (Ala. Crim. App., Oct. 14, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-03-1661.61).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) that denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus as an Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 petition for postconviction relief; defendant claimed, inter alia, that the indictment against him was void and his sentence was illegally imposed by the trial court rather than the jury.


OVERVIEW: The incident giving rise to the rape charge was committed on June 18, 1979. Defendant claimed that because his crime occurred after May 16, 1978, his case was governed by Ala. Code tit. 13A and not former Ala. Code tit. 13. The appellate court reviewed the legislative history and determined that former Ala. Code tit. 13 was the law in effect at the time of the commission of the offense. Therefore, former Ala. Code §§ 13-1-130, 13-1-131 governed the prosecution and sentencing. Because neither Ala. Code §§ 15-8-30 nor 15-8-31 required the time or place of the offense to be charged in the indictment, defendant's claim did not implicate the trial court's jurisdiction. Because Ala. Code § 13-1-130 contained no provision for jury sentencing, the sentence was properly imposed by the trial court instead of the jury and, thus, was not illegal. Finally, because defendant's habeas corpus petition challenged the validity of his conviction and sentence, the circuit court's treatment of the petition as an Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 petition was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Hunt v. State

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Walker Circuit Court (Alabama), which denied his petition for postconviction relief (PCR) that was filed pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 and attacked his capital-murder conviction and his sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for the capital murder of a woman during a burglary and sexual abuse. A jury recommended death, which was imposed and affirmed on direct appeal. Defendant's PCR petition was denied, On appeal, he challenged the standards of review used by the circuit court, the refusal to admit certain evidence at the PCR hearing, and the decision that his trial and appellate counsel were not ineffective. OVERVIEW: The appeals court found that because defendant did not make the required showing of need, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying his requests for expert assistance. Stephens v. State


CR-02-0154


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


982 So. 2d 1110; 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 139



August 12, 2005, Released

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Lee Circuit Court (Alabama) that convicted him of capital murders of his wife and son and sentenced him to death; defendant claimed, inter alia, that the trial court erred by admitting certain testimony evidence and by allowing the jury to consider an uncharged aggravating circumstance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant confessed to stabbing his wife and son over 30 times each. At trial, the victim's father testified about defendant's prior assault on her and photographs of the victims were admitted into evidence. The appellate court held that defendant's statement was voluntary. Evidence of defendant's prior conviction was admissible under Ala. R. Evid. 404(b) to prove motive and intent. Although the jury was permitted to consider a nonstatutory aggravating circumstance, it was harmless error.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Blackmon v. State


CR-01-2126


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


7 So. 3d 397; 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 137



August 5, 2005, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 27, 2009. [**1] 
Rehearing overruled by Blackmon v. State, 7 So. 3d 397, 2006 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 184 (Ala. Crim. App., Aug. 25, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Houston Circuit Court. (CC-99-1177).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment form the Houston Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted her for capital murder under Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(15) and sentenced her to death, resulting in an automatic appeal under Ala. Code § 13A-5-55.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to death for beating to death her 28-month-old daughter. She appealed, challenging denial of her request for the transcript from the grand jury proceedings, her motion for change of venue, her Batson motion regarding allegedly discriminatory removal of black jurors, her motion for acquittal due to lack of direct evidence, and her motion for a new trial on allegations that the death sentence was unconstitutionally arrived at. The court found the grand jury proceedings were properly held secret, that presumed prejudice or pretrial publicity was not satisfied to warrant change of venue, that race-neutral reasons existed for removing each of the black jurors that were removed, and that legally sufficient circumstantial evidence of defendant's guilt supported presenting the issue of defendant's guilt to the jury. Finally, the court found that the child-murder provision under Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(15) did not violate equal protection considerations regarding age and the Apprendi rule did not apply where the death penalty aggravator of killing a child under 14 was an element of the offense that the jury had already found.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's murder conviction and death sentence.

King v. State


CR-03-1704


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


929 So. 2d 1032; 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 123



June 24, 2005, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 4, 2006.
Rehearing denied by King v. State, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1910 (Ala. Crim. App., Sept. 16, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Madison Circuit Court. (CC-03-0419).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted on two counts of first-degree sexual abuse, Ala. Code § 13A-6-66. Following a jury trial, defendant was convicted of both charges. The Circuit Court of Madison County (Alabama) imposed 10-year concurrent sentences, and ordered defendant to pay a $ 2,500 fine for each count, $ 500 to the Crime Victims Compensation Fund for each count, court costs, and restitution. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the Child Sexual Abuse Victim Protection Act, Ala. Code § 15-25-31 et seq., was unconstitutional because it violated his right to confrontation and that the trial court erred when it allowed the State to introduce hearsay statements from the victim. The appellate court noted that any limitation on defendant's right to cross-examine the victim was the result of defense counsel's decisions and not the result of any action by the trial court or the prosecutor. Defendant also argued that the trial court erred when it denied his motion in limine and permitted the forensic investigator and the forensic interviewer to testify as to the victim's out-of-court statements because the testimony contained more details of the assaults than the victim provided in her testimony. Among other things, the appellate court noted that the testimony was admissible pursuant to Ala. Code §§ 15-25-31, 15-25-32. Finally, the appellate court concluded that there was no error as to the trial court's grant of the State's objection to a defense exhibit, defendant's complete medical records, because the trial court previously ruled that only those pages previously disclosed were admissible.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

492 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Clemons v. State


CR-01-1355


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


55 So. 3d 314; 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 128



June 24, 2005, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
As Corrected June 28, 2011.
Rehearing denied by Clemons v. State, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 3271 (Ala. Crim. App., Sept. 16, 2005)
Reversed by, Remanded by Ex parte Clemons, 55 So. 3d 348, 2007 Ala. LEXIS 78 (Ala., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Shelby Circuit Court. (CC-93-313.60).
Clemons v. State, 55 So. 3d 314, 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 217 (Ala. Crim. App., 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Shelby Circuit Court (Alabama) of murder, and sentenced to death. Defendant appealed. The case was remanded for the circuit court to conduct an evidentiary hearing. The circuit court determined following the hearing that defendant was not mentally retarded, and that his trial attorneys did not render ineffective assistance of counsel. Defendant raised additional issues concerning the remand.


OVERVIEW: Defendant approached a man in a parked car. When defendant told the man that defendant was taking the car, the man, a law enforcement agent, pulled a gun. Defendant then shot and killed the man. Various psychologists testified as to the results of intelligence tests that were administered to defendant. Some of the psychologists testified that defendant tried to score low test scores in the tests, but functioned in the borderline range of intellectual ability. Additionally, defendant's appellate counsel testified as to counsel's shortcomings and personal problems in representing defendant. On appeal, the court found that, even under the broadest definition of mental retardation, defendant was not mentally retarded and that imposition of the death penalty in the case was not in violation of the Eighth Amendment. Additionally, defendant's ineffective assistance of trial counsel claims were precluded pursuant to the provisions of Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.2(a). Finally, defendant did not satisfy his burden on his ineffectiveness of appellate counsel claim of showing that appellate counsel was deficient and that defendant was prejudiced by that performance.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

493 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Barber v. State


CR-03-0737


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


952 So. 2d 393; 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 120



May 27, 2005, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 23, 2007.

As Corrected April 30, 2008.
Rehearing denied by, Without opinion by Barber v. State, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 2674 (Ala. Crim. App., July 8, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Barber v. Alabama, 127 S. Ct. 1875, 167 L. Ed. 2d 366, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 3606 (U.S., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Madison Circuit Court. (CC-02-1794). Loyd H. Little, Jr.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Madison Circuit Court (Alabama) of one count of capital murder. The murder was made capital because defendant committed it during the course of a robbery or an attempted robbery, Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2). The jury recommended that he be sentenced to death. The trial court sentenced him to death. He filed two motions for a new trial, which the trial court denied, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant first challenged the testimony of a police latent print examiner. The appeals court found that because the case did not involve DNA evidence, the Daubert standard did not apply. Also, because print identification involved subjective observations and comparisons based on the expert's training, skill, or experience, it did not constitute scientific evidence; therefore, Frye did not apply. Rather, print identification constituted specialized knowledge that could be helpful to the jury in understanding or determining the facts. Therefore, Ala. R. Evid. 702 governed the admissibility of the examiner's testimony. Moreover, even if Daubert applied, the testimony was admissible. Defendant also alleged that the State improperly withheld witness statements based solely on speculative testimony by the victim's family members. However, he had not presented anything other than pure speculation to support his allegations. Defendant did not wear handcuffs and shackles throughout the trial but wore them going to and from the courtroom, and any jurors who saw him wearing handcuffs and shackles did so while he was going to and from the courtroom. He was not prejudiced by his appearance.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
