Bryant v. State


CR-98-0023


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


951 So. 2d 732; 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 100



April 29, 2005, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Rehearing denied by, Without opinion by Bryant v. State, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 2673 (Ala. Crim. App., July 29, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Bryant v. Alabama, 127 S. Ct. 1909, 167 L. Ed. 2d 569, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 3833 (U.S., Apr. 2, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Houston Circuit Court. (CC-97-403).
Bryant v. State, 951 So. 2d 732, 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 82 (Ala. Crim. App., Mar. 21, 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Houston Circuit Court (Alabama), which, on resentencing following remand, again imposed a sentence of death on defendant after he was convicted of murder during a kidnapping in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to death, his conviction was affirmed on direct appeal, but his death sentence was reversed. The court remanded the case for a new sentencing hearing. The circuit court conducted such a hearing and again sentenced defendant to death. He appealed on a multitude of grounds. The court rejected defendant's challenge to the seating of the jury, finding that challenges for cause regarding prospective jurors were not improperly granted where jurors indicated they would recommend death only if the evidence met a higher standard of proof than required under Ala. Code § 13A-5-46(e)(3). Moreover, there was no evidence that the State unconstitutionally used its peremptory challenges to remove African-Americans from the jury venire. Defendant had notice of the aggravating circumstance that would constitute the capital offense, and, since he had a second sentencing hearing, he had the added benefit of knowing precisely which aggravating circumstances the State would rely on. The aggravating factors were not required to be set out in the indictment or decided by special verdict forms and were sufficient to impose death.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder and capital punishment.

 

495 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Scott v. State


CR-03-1202


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


917 So. 2d 159; 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 92



April 29, 2005, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 1, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Mobile Circuit Court. (CC-01-1385; CC-01-1386).
Scott v. State, 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1503 (Ala. Crim. App., May 18, 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Mobile Circuit Court (Alabama), which, upon defendant's Alford pleas of guilty, convicted him of two charges of showing or allowing to be shown for entertainment purposes female genitals, pubic area, or buttocks with less than a fully opaque covering, violations of Ala. Code § 13A-12-200.11.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held: (1) that the State presented a sufficient factual basis to support defendant's pleas of guilty, in that the prosecutor's detailed statement of facts underlying the charges was sufficient to make defendant aware of the nature of the charges against him; (2) that defendant's motion to dismiss one of the two indictments against him on the ground of multiplicity was properly denied because defendant's acquiescence in the activities of his club constituted a separate criminal act under the statute each time a proscribed show was performed on the premises for the undercover officer, in that the language of § 13A-12-200.11 contemplated a separate and distinct violation each time a show was allowed; (3) that the absence of an express statement in § 13A-12-200.11 as to the requisite mental state did not render the statute unconstitutionally vague but, instead, indicated that the offense could be committed intentionally, knowingly, recklessly, or through criminal negligence; and (4) that § 13A-12-200.11 was not unconstitutionally vague because it set forth the offense with sufficient definitiveness so as to provide fair warning of what conduct was prohibited.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Calhoun v. State


CR-00-0002


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


932 So. 2d 923; 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 101



April 29, 2005, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected January 9, 2007.
Rehearing denied by, Without opinion by Calhoun v. State, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1911 (Ala. Crim. App., June 17, 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Calhoun v. Alabama, 548 U.S. 926, 126 S. Ct. 2984, 165 L. Ed. 2d 990, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 5233 (2006)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Calhoun v. State, 2016 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 26 (Ala. Crim. App., Apr. 29, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Talladega Circuit Court. (CC-98-215 through 98-218).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Talladega Circuit Court (Alabama), after a jury trial, convicted defendant of four counts of capital murder for murdering a victim during the course of each of four Ala. Code § 13A-5-49(4) aggravators of (1) a robbery, (2) a burglary, (3) a sodomy of the murder victim's wife, and (4) a rape of the murder victim's wife and, after the jury's 10 to 2 death sentence recommendation, sentenced him to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant visited the victims' home when the victims were preparing for a yard sale the day of the murders. That evening a neighbor called the victim's wife to tell her she saw a man looking through their window. Defendant was proven to have entered the victims' home, made the victim put his head between his wife's legs, shot the victim in the back of his head in front of his wife and child, and raped and sodomized the wife. The evidence convicting defendant included tapes of a "911" call, neighbors' testimony, the wife's testimony, teeth mark evidence (that could be physically inspected such that it was not subject to the stringent standards applied to scientific tests), and blood evidence from clothing defendant had abandoned to his mother. Ring was satisfied as the jury found the four aggravators to exist beyond a reasonable doubt. The mother's request that defendant live did not have to be considered to be a mitigator; there were no statutory or other mitigators. Defendant's intelligence quotient (IQ) tested 58 to 66, but the psychologist testified she thought he was malingering and probably had an IQ over 70; he was death sentence eligible under Ex Parte Perkins.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the convictions and the death sentence.

D.B.Y v. State


CR-04-0443


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


910 So. 2d 820; 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 71



March 18, 2005, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 28, 2005.
Writ of mandamus granted D.B.Y. v. State, 925 So. 2d 1020, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 794 (Ala. Crim. App., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-01-331 and CC-01-894).
D.Y. v. State, 841 So. 2d 304, 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 89 (Ala. Crim. App., 2002)



DISPOSITION: PETITION FOR WRIT OF MANDAMUS IS GRANTED; WRIT ISSUED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner district attorney sought a writ of mandamus directing a judge of the Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama) to reinstate a juvenile probationer's term of probation and to direct said probationer to undergo a sexual-offender risk assessment as required by law before he be released from probation.


OVERVIEW: In response to the district attorney's petition for relief, the juvenile probationer argued that the State had a remedy at law in that it could appeal the ruling rendered by the circuit judge. However, the instant court disagreed as the State had only a limited right to appeal and that right did not apply herein. Hence, mandamus was the State's only remedy. Moreover, the State's filing of its motion for a sexual-offender risk assessment before the expiration of the probation period operated to toll said term. Based on the mandatory wording of Ala. Code § 15-20-28, and on the clearly stated legislative intent, the judge had no authority to release the probationer from probation until he underwent a sexual-offender risk assessment. Ala. Code § 15-20-28(a) also specifically provided that the treatment provider was to provide a risk assessment of the juvenile probationer 60 days before his projected release date.


OUTCOME: The writ was issued.

Duncan v. State


CR-03-1634


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


925 So. 2d 245; 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 78



March 18, 2005, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 24, 2006.
Appeal after remand at Duncan v. State, 925 So. 2d 245, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 116 (Ala. Crim. App., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-94-3624.60).
Duncan v. State, 827 So. 2d 838, 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 224 (Ala. Crim. App., 1999)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) of kidnapping-murder, pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(1), and robbery-murder, pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2). The trial court accepted the jury's recommendation and sentenced defendant to death. After his direct appeal was denied, defendant filed for postconviction relief, pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32. The trial court summarily denied the petition. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court found that the record clearly established that defendant was 17 years old at the time of the offense. Therefore, his sentence of death was unconstitutional and had to be set aside. As to defendant's allegations regarding ineffective assistance of counsel and as to defendant's allegations of Brady violations, the court found that defendant's allegations failed to meet the specificity and factual pleading requirements of Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.6, failed to state a claim or establish that a material issue of fact or law existed as required by Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.7(d), failed to plead facts that would establish that counsel's performance was deficient or caused him to be prejudiced as required by Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.3, were procedurally barred by Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.2 as they were more properly addressed in a motion for a new trial or on direct appeal, and did not meet the pleading requirements of Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.9. Moreover, even reviewing the claims cumulatively, the court found that defendant was not entitled to relief. Therefore, the circuit court did not err in summarily denying defendant's motion for postconviction relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part as to defendant's convictions; however, the judgment was reversed in part as to the sentence, and the case was remanded to the circuit court with instructions that the circuit court set aside defendant's death sentence and resentence him to imprisonment for life without the possibility of parole.

State v. Hargett


CR-03-1548


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


935 So. 2d 1200; 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 49



February 25, 2005, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Later proceeding at State v. Hargett, 926 So. 2d 1080, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1222 (Ala. Crim. App., Apr. 1, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Chambers Circuit Court. (CC-04-40).



DISPOSITION: CASE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order ofthe Chambers Circuit Court (Alabama), which granted defendant's motion to suppress evidence of cocaine that police obtained after a traffic stop of an automobile defendant was driving.


OVERVIEW: Defendant moved to suppress cocaine that was found on him after a traffic stop. An officer testified that he pulled over the car defendant was driving because the occupants were not wearing seat belts. The officer claimed he smelled alcohol, asked defendant to get out of the car, and noticed defendant was having problems talking due to something in his mouth. The cocaine was discovered in defendant's mouth. Defendant argued that the initial stop of his vehicle was illegal and that, if the stop was legal, the cocaine was found pursuant to an unconstitutional warrantless search. Suppression was granted and the State appealed. It argued that the stop was lawful due to the seat belt violations and that the request for defendant to open his mouth was not improper. The court held that, on the record before it, it could not determine the basis for the trial court's suppression of the cocaine. Therefore, it could not properly review the decision. The trial court made no factual findings. It could have decided the case on the officer's credibility regarding the initial stop. Also, there appeared to be an issue on whether defendant consented to open his mouth or was ordered to do so.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the matter for clarification on the basis for suppression of the cocaine and for specific written findings of fact and conclusions of law regarding its determination of the validity of the initial stop of defendant's vehicle and the legality of the discovery and seizure of the cocaine in defendant's mouth.

Scott v. State


CR-02-0347


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


937 So. 2d 1065; 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 36



February 25, 2005, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Appeal after remand at Scott v. State, 937 So. 2d 1065, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 111 (Ala. Crim. App., May 27, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-2000-840, -841, -842).



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted him for capital murder, committed during the rape of a 10-year-old, and which convicted him for first-degree rape and attempted murder of another girl. He was sentenced to death for the capital murder and life imprisonment for the remaining convictions.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant on all charges related to attacks on two girls. It recommended death, which the trial court imposed. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in: (1) ordering counsel to call witnesses that defendant wanted, but who counsel believed were harmful; (2) not granting a continuance; (3) not severing capital murder charges from other charges; (4) not allowing counsel to withdraw; and (5) making the sentencing order. Defendant's insistence on calling the witnesses over counsel's objections invited any error, a continuance was not likely to produce a missing witness, severance was not mandatory given similarities in the crimes, and no conflict of interest was shown to justify withdrawal. The State conceded error in the sentencing order. Only facts related to the crime, and not defendant's lack of remorse after, could be considered for the heinous crime aggravator. The Ala. Code § 13A-5-47(d) directive for specific findings was not met where an aggravator that was not listed in Ala. Code § 13A-5-49 was applied, findings on each statutory mitigator in Ala. Code § 13A-5-51 were missing, and factors beyond Ala. Code § 13A-5-47(e) were considered.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the cause so that the trial court could amend its sentencing order. The trial court was directed to make findings as to and consider only those aggravating factors set out by statute and was to address each of statutory mitigating factors. The court pretermitted its complete plain error review of the case and its review of the sentence pending the trial court's return to remand.

CR-03-1063


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


922 So. 2d 145; 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 47

US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Washington v. Alabama, 546 U.S. 1142, 126 S. Ct. 1152, 163 L. Ed. 2d 1008, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 846 (2006)

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Elmore Circuit Court. (CC-03-186).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Elmore Circuit Court (Alabama) convicted defendant of five counts of capital murder under Ala. Code § 13A-5-40. The jury recommended that defendant be sentenced to death. The trial court accepted the jury's recommendation and sentenced defendant to death for his capital-murder convictions. OUTCOME: Defendant's capital-murder convictions and his death sentence were affirmed.

Ex parte Egbuonu


CR-03-1721


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


911 So. 2d 748; 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 244



November 24, 2004, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Ex parte Egbuonu, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 170 (Ala. Crim. App., Jan. 21, 2005)
Writ of certiorari denied Ex parte Egbuonu, 911 So. 2d 755, 2005 Ala. LEXIS 58 (Ala., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-04-1422).



DISPOSITION: Petition for a writ of habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A judge in the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) denied petitioner detainee's request for a writ of habeas corpus, in which he alleged that Ala. Code § 13A-8-196 was unconstitutional. The judge also denied the detainee's motion to reduce bail. The detainee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The detainee challenged the judgments entered against him, first contending that Ala. Code § 13A-8-196, which provided that venue for the offense of identity theft was proper in a county other than where the offense occurred, was unconstitutional because it conflicted with Ala. Const. art. I, § 6. The appeals court disagreed. The Alabama Legislature specifically designated that venue was proper either in the county where the crime took place or where the victim resided. Identity theft, by its definition under Ala. Code § 13A-8-192, was a continuing offense that in most instances occurred in more than one county or even more than one state. Further, no provision within Ala. Const. art. I, § 6 limited venue in a criminal case to one county or even one state. Second, as the detainee admitted in his petition that he waived extradition, the legality of said extradition was no longer a proper subject of any legal attack. Finally, given the unique circumstances of the instant case, specifically, the fact that defendant had no ties to Alabama, the $ 100,000 bail set against him was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The request for the writ was denied.

Harris v. State


CR-01-1748


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


947 So. 2d 1079; 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 203



October 29, 2004, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 1, 2007.
Rehearing overruled by Harris v. State, 947 So. 2d 1079, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 108 (Ala. Crim. App., 2005)
Writ of certiorari denied Ex parte Harris, 2005 Ala. LEXIS 130 (Ala., Aug. 19, 2005)
Writ of certiorari granted Ex parte Harris, 947 So. 2d 1139, 2005 Ala. LEXIS 175 (Ala., 2005)
Writ of certiorari quashed, in part, Affirmed by, in part Ex parte Harris, 947 So. 2d 1139, 2006 Ala. LEXIS 102 (Ala., 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-88-1237.60). William A. Shashy.
Ex parte Harris, 632 So. 2d 543, 1993 Ala. LEXIS 589 (Ala., 1993)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged the order of the Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama), which denied her Ala. R. Crim. P. R. 32 petition. The inmate had been convicted of murder made capital because it was committed for a pecuniary or other valuable consideration or pursuant to a contract or for hire, an offense made capital by Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(7) (1975).


OVERVIEW: The inmate first claimed on appeal that the circuit court erred in denying relief on her claim that the prosecution exercised peremptory strikes against black venire-members in violation of Batson. The court upheld the circuit court's ruling concluding that the inmate's presentation of only statistic information, and no facts, failed to support her claim that the principles of Batson had been violated that she failed to establish a prima facie showing of purposeful or intentional discrimination by the State in its exercise of peremptory strikes. The court concluded that most of the inmate's claims of ineffectiveness of counsel amounted to nothing more than a bare allegation, unsupported by any factual basis but that she did prove that her counsel was ineffective for failing to have presented mitigating evidence at sentencing. The court determined that had counsel conducted a reasonable investigation into possible mitigating evidence, the balance between the aggravating circumstance and the mitigating circumstances would have tipped further in favor of a sentence of life imprisonment without the possibility of parole.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's order as to sentencing and remanded the case to the circuit court for a new penalty-phase hearing before a jury and then an additional hearing before the trial judge.

 

506 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Walker v. State


CR-03-0226


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


932 So. 2d 140; 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 195



October 1, 2004, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Appeal after remand at Walker v. State, 932 So. 2d 140, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 25 (Ala. Crim. App., Jan. 28, 2005)
Related proceeding at Beckworth v. State, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 167 (Ala. Crim. App., Aug. 26, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Houston Circuit Court. (CC-00-863).



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Houston Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted him of capital murder pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(4) (1975), sentenced him to death, and, after conducting a hearing, denied his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital murder for killing an 87-year-old woman in her home during a first-degree burglary. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction, finding that, because the jury convicted defendant of the capital offense of burglary-murder, the statutory aggravating circumstance was proven beyond a reasonable doubt. Furthermore, the court found that, because the jury found the existence of one aggravating circumstance, defendant was exposed to or eligible for the death penalty. The court found also that the newspaper stories on the murder were factual and relatively objective and not accusatory, inflammatory, or sensational; therefore, they did not contain prejudicial information. Furthermore, the court found that defendant did not prove that the media attention inflamed or saturated the community so that there was an emotional tide against him; thus his case did not warrant a presumption of prejudice based on pretrial publicity. Lastly, the court found that the trial judge did not follow the sentencing procedures for death penalty cases outlined in Ala. Code § 13A-5-47 and remanded for written findings of aggravating and mitigating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction, but remanded the cause with instructions that the trial court enter specific written findings concerning the existence or nonexistence of each aggravating circumstance, each mitigating circumstance, and any additional mitigating circumstances offered, as mandated by statute.

Knight v. State


CR-00-2694


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


907 So. 2d 470; 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 197



October 1, 2004, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 23, 2005.
Appeal after remand at Knight v. State, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 35 (Ala. Crim. App., Feb. 25, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Baldwin Circuit Court. (CC-00-865).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS TO CONVICTION; REVERSED AS TO SENTENCING; AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Baldwin Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted him of killing his wife while she was in a motor vehicle, a murder defined as capital by Ala. Code § 13A- 5-40(a)(17) (1975), and, upon the jury's recommendation, sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his wife were separated. They had one child together and the wife had another child while defendant was serving a prison sentence in Florida. Defendant had learned that he was not the father of the second child and suspected that his wife was having an affair with his cousin. The wife went to defendant's father's house and asked defendant to come and talk with her. Defendant left the house with a butcher knife. While the two were in the car, the wife received a phone call from the cousin. Defendant became angry, pulled out the butcher knife, and stabbed his wife 32 times. Defendant was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction, finding that no heat-of-passion instruction was necessary because defendant did not catch his wife in the act of sexual intercourse. To the extent that Anderson v. State, 507 So. 2d 580 (Ala. Crim. App. 1987) held otherwise, the court overruled that case. The court then found that because the trial court erred in applying a non-statutory aggravating circumstance related to defendant's pattern of violence toward his wife, the cause had to be remanded for a new sentencing hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction but reversed as to sentencing and remanded the cause to the trial court with instructions that it hold a new sentencing hearing before a duly empaneled jury and enter a new sentencing order after weighing the aggravating circumstances and the mitigating circumstances.

Minor v. State


CR-00-1300


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


914 So. 2d 372; 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 156



August 27, 2004, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 27, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Minor v. State, 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 899 (Ala. Crim. App., Oct. 22, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Minor v. Alabama, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 5215 (U.S., June 30, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Tuscaloosa Circuit Court. (CC-95-1118.80).
Minor v. State, 780 So. 2d 804, 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 119 (Ala. Crim. App., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of capital murder of a child less than 14 years of age, Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(15), and sentenced to death, but the supreme court reversed. Once again, a jury found him guilty of capital murder as charged in the indictment, and recommended a death sentence. The Tuscaloosa Circuit Court (Alabama) accepted the jury's recommendation and sentenced defendant to death. From this conviction and sentence defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: There was no real dispute at trial that defendant's son was the victim of shaken impact syndrome--that he had been severely shaken and beaten. The only real issue was who had caused the son's injuries. The appeals court, among other rulings, found no error on the trial court's part in denying defendant's motion to suppress several statements made to police. There was no error, plain or otherwise, in the trial court's allowing a physician to testify in rebuttal, or in the denial of defendant's motions for a new trial. There was no error in the trial court's refusal to sua sponte declare a mistrial or remove a juror from the jury based on the prosecutor's comments. Defendant's contention that there was a cumulative prejudicial effect resulting from multiple improper arguments by the prosecutor was without merit. Finally, there was no evidence that the sentence was imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor. The appeals court concurred in the trial court's judgment that the aggravating circumstances outweighed the mitigating circumstances, and agreed that death was the appropriate sentence. The trial court's conclusions were supported.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence of death were affirmed.

Morrow v. State


CR-01-1619


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


928 So. 2d 315; 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 155



August 27, 2004, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 4, 2006.
Related proceeding at Flowers v. State, 922 So. 2d 938, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 34 (Ala. Crim. App., Feb. 25, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Baldwin Circuit Court. (CC-01-164).



DISPOSITION: Remanded with directions.

*Note from the reporter of decisions: On August 12, 2005, on return to remand, the Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed, without opinion. On September 2, 2005, that court denied rehearing, without opinion. On October 21, 2005, the Supreme Court denied certiorari review, without opinion (1041902).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Baldwin Circuit Court (Alabama) convicted defendant of three counts of capital murder and despite the jury's recommendation to sentence him to life in prison without the possibility of parole, the court sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the sentence imposed. The appeals court first held that his retardation was offered to establish a statutory mitigating circumstance. Second, while evidence raised an inference of mental retardation, contrary evidence also existed, and this conflict was better resolved by the trial court. The best course of action until the Legislature acted on the issue was under Ala. R. Crim. P. 32. Third, the trial court failed to state its reasons for giving the jury's recommendation of life in prison consideration, and that it considered that recommendation as a mitigating circumstance. It also found non-statutory mitigating circumstances existed, but failed to identify what they were. Thus, on remand, the trial court was to: (1) determine whether defendant was mentally retarded, (2) consider the jury's recommendation as a mitigating circumstance, (3) reweigh the aggravating and mitigating circumstances, and, if necessary, resentence defendant; (4) amend its sentencing order to reflect consideration of the jury's recommendation and the specific reasons it gave that recommendation consideration; and (5) identify the specific non-statutory mitigating circumstances found.


OUTCOME: The matter was remanded with instructions.

 

510 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Lee v. State


CR-02-1900


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


895 So. 2d 1038; 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 158



August 27, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 1, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Tuscaloosa Circuit Court. (CC-02-1016).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction by the Tuscaloosa Circuit Court (Alabama), upon his guilty plea, for a violation of the Alabama Community Notification Act (CNA), Ala. Code § 15-20-26(a), for establishing a residence within 2,000 feet of a child care facility, following the denial of his motion to dismiss the indictment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the CNA's residency requirement constituted retroactive punishment proscribed by the Ex Post Facto Clause. The appellate court held that defendant did not support his claim that the residency requirement constituted a punitive measure, either as applied to him or on its face. In enacting the CNA, the Alabama legislature intended to create a civil scheme designed to protect the citizens of Alabama and their children. That the CNA was found in the Alabama Criminal Code was not dispositive of whether it was punitive. Defendant failed to show how the CNA rendered defendant or any other sex offender homeless. Defendant also failed to show that defendant or any other sex offender was affirmatively disabled or restrained by the CNA. The CNA had a rational, nonpunitive purpose of public safety and was not excessive with respect to that purpose. Defendant failed to show that the effects of the CNA negated the Alabama legislature's intention to protect the public, in particular children, from convicted sex offenders. Therefore, the CNA was nonpunitive, both on its face and in terms of its effects and did not violate the Ex Post Facto Clause.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Ex parte Ray-El


CR-03-1257


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


911 So. 2d 1100; 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 132



July 23, 2004, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected September 13, 2004. Released for Publication September 29, 2005. As Corrected February 21, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Madison Circuit Court. (CC-2003-3288).



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ of habeas corpus dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The inmate was released on bail following his arrest for murder. His bail was revoked after he was arrested for reckless endangerment, giving a false name, driving without a license, and eluding the police. Subsequently, petitioner next friend filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus on behalf of the inmate, a minor. The State filed a motion to dismiss the petition.


OVERVIEW: The next friend claimed that the inmate was being held without the benefit of pretrial bail in violation of the United States Constitution. In its motion to dismiss the petition, the State argued that the next friend had no standing to file the petition. The appellate court held that it was without jurisdiction to entertain the petition because the petition failed to satisfy the requirements for next-friend status. The burden was on the next friend to clearly establish the propriety of his status and thereby justify the jurisdiction of the appellate court. The petition contained no explanation as to the next friend's relationship with the inmate, or as to why the inmate's attorney did not file the petition on his behalf. Nor was there a reference to the inmate's current age. Therefore, the petition, scant at best, totally failed to comply with the requirements for filing a habeas corpus petition pursuant to Ala. Code § 15-21-4.


OUTCOME: The petition for a writ of habeas corpus was dismissed.

 

512 of 745 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cortner


CR-02-1909


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


893 So. 2d 1264; 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 119



June 25, 2004, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 12, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Lauderdale Circuit Court. (CC-03-131).



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted in the Lauderdale Circuit Court (Alabama) for unlawful possession of cocaine and unlawful possession of marijuana for personal use. The trial court dismissed the indictment, finding that defendant and the State had agreed that the charges would be dismissed upon defendant's payment of money that was subject to a civil forfeiture proceeding to the State. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: At the time of defendant's arrest, officers seized $ 10,000 found at his home. This money was subject to a civil forfeiture proceeding. Under the plea agreement, defendant agreed to pay $ 5,000 to the State and the other $ 5,000 was to be paid to his counsel, if the charges were dismissed. The State argued that the trial court erred in finding an agreement and that if there was an agreement, it was never approved by the trial court. The court found that it could not review the State's objections for lack of approval because they were not raised below. The court upheld the trial court's finding that there was an agreement, but found that the agreement was unenforceable as against public policy. The State would not be allowed to forbear the prosecution of a suspected criminal in return for a payoff because of the public interest in prosecuting drug offenders. It was improper for the State to threaten a defendant in a civil forfeiture proceeding with criminal prosecution. Additionally, the agreement was unenforceable because the criminal court could not have ordered the civil court to accept the agreement between the parties.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment dismissing the indictment and remanded the cause to the trial court for further proceedings.

Deardorff v. State


CR-01-0794


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


6 So. 3d 1205; 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 118



June 25, 2004, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 27, 2009. [**1] 
Judgment entered by Ex parte Deardorff, 2008 Ala. LEXIS 1 (Ala., Jan. 4, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Baldwin Circuit Court. (CC-2000-151).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS. *



* Note from the reporter of decisions: On September 17, 2004, on return to remand, the Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed, without opinion. On October 22, 2004, that court denied rehearing, without opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant of three counts of capital murder, seven counts of theft, and one count of receiving stolen property and recommended the imposition of the death penalty. The Baldwin Circuit Court (Alabama) conducted a separate hearing and considered additional evidence, then ordered that the death penalty be imposed for the capital-murder convictions. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim was held in a hall closet for 24 hours and then shot in the back of the head. The appellate court held that defendant's double-jeopardy rights were violated because he was convicted of robbery-murder and also for the underlying thefts that constituted an element of the capital-murder charges. Thus, the theft convictions were in error. However, the remainder of defendant's convictions and sentences were upheld. The testimony about the victim's will that was elicited was properly admitted at trial because it was not hearsay. Further, the note the co-defendant wrote to his girlfriend was within the res gestae of the crime, and the trial court correctly admitted the note into evidence as a statement made in furtherance of a conspiracy. Next, defendant's motion to suppress evidence was properly denied because he did not have standing to object to the search of the vehicle and the seizure of the evidence from the vehicle as he did not own the vehicle. As to sentencing, the evidence established the aggravating circumstance that the murder was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel was fully supported by the record, as the victim suffered prolonged psychological torture.


OUTCOME: The cause was remanded with directions to vacate the theft convictions and sentences. The remaining convictions and sentences were affirmed.

Steele v. State


CR-02-1870


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


911 So. 2d 21; 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 115



May 28, 2004, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 31, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Cullman Circuit Court. (CC02-294).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Cullman Circuit Court (Alabama) convicted defendant of first-degree sexual abuse, in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-6-66(a)(3), and sentenced him, as an habitual felony offender, to 20 years in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court upheld defendant's conviction, despite his allegations that the testimony from the victim child was erroneously admitted. The child was available, subject to cross-examination, and her version of the facts was both corroborated and held to be sufficiently trustworthy. Further, the jury was free to afford the victim's out-of-court statements whatever weight that it deemed appropriate. Second, the filing of a notice of appeal did not divest the trial court of jurisdiction to address defendant's timely filed post-trial motions. Third, defendant was not entitled to an acquittal, as his act of placing his finger inside of the victim's vagina, and placing her hand on his penis, constituted sufficient sexual contact to support a conviction. Fourth, because he did not object to the State's failure to provide him with a copy of the Ohio conviction prior to sentencing, he waived the issue. However, because said conviction was for a crime which if committed in Alabama would not have been a felony, the State failed to meet its burden to invoke the Habitual Felony Offender Act, Ala. Code § 13A-5-9.


OUTCOME: The trial court erred in enhancing defendant's sentence based upon an Ohio conviction. Thus, the matter was remanded for resentencing. In all other respects, the judgment was affirmed.

McWilliams v. State


CR-01-0235


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


897 So. 2d 437; 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 74



April 30, 2004, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by McWilliams v. State, 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 262 (Ala. Crim. App., June 11, 2004)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at McWilliams v. Campbell, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 124114 (N.D. Ala., Feb. 1, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Tuscaloosa Circuit Court. (CC-85-437.60).
Ex parte McWilliams, 666 So. 2d 90, 1995 Ala. LEXIS 218 (Ala., 1995)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death. He filed an Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 petition, challenging his convictions, which the Tuscaloosa Circuit Court (Alabama) denied. The inmate appealed, raising several arguments.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued the circuit court improperly denied his motions to amend his petition and the discovery agreements. The appeals court found the circuit court did not abuse its discretion in denying his motions to amend his petition, as the inmate caused the majority of the delays, and the court would not reward him for doing so. The circuit court did not err in dismissing several of the inmate's claims on the grounds that he did not sufficiently plead them, as they were precluded by Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.7(d). He also argued that his Rule 32 attorneys rendered ineffective assistance, but the claim was invalid as there was no requirement in Alabama that indigent petitioners be furnished counsel regarding post-conviction proceedings. He claimed that his trial and appellate attorneys were ineffective, but trial counsel considered, investigated, and presented evidence relating to his mental health, and the fact that counsel's efforts did not result in a sentence less than death did not make their performance deficient. As Ring claims were not applied retroactively to postconviction proceedings, his claim that Ring applied retroactively to his death sentence was meritless.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Bargeron v. State


CR-03-0119


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


895 So. 2d 385; 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 85



April 30, 2004, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Released for Publication February 1, 2005. Rehearing denied by, Without opinion by Bargeron v. State, 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 259 (Ala. Crim. App., June 18, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Baldwin Circuit Court. (CC-97-534.60).
Bargeron v. State, 820 So. 2d 167, 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 3295 (Ala. Crim. App., 2000)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Baldwin Circuit Court (Alabama) denied defendant's petition for post-conviction relief, filed pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32, in which she challenged her conviction for first-degree theft of property and her resulting sentence asserting 11 claims. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the judgment entered against her claiming error. However, the appeals court first held that her first claim was precluded because she could have raised it at trial and on appeal, but did not. Her second claim was precluded pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.2(a)(4), because this claim was raised and addressed on direct appeal. As to claims 3 through 8, the appeals court agreed with the trial court that defendant failed to meet her burden of proving that her trial counsel's performance prejudiced her in any way. However, the failure of counsel to appear at the restitution hearing, as alleged in claim 3 constituted ineffective assistance of counsel. Further, issues regarding the legality of the restitution order were not addressed because a new restitution hearing was ordered. Finally, because the legislative intent of the restitution statute was to compensate, and not to punish, the special damages that the victim was entitled to were limited to an amount which fully compensated the victim, and said damages were not to be punitive in nature.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying the requested relief as to the non-jurisdictional claims was affirmed. But, due to the absence of counsel at the restitution hearing, the matter was remanded for a new restitution hearing.

Smith v. State


CR-02-1218


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


898 So. 2d 907; 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 93



April 30, 2004, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 15, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Smith v. State, 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 271 (Ala. Crim. App., July 30, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Etowah Circuit Court. (CC-1999-1347).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Etowah Circuit Court (Alabama) convicted defendant of manslaughter, and the trial court imposed a 20-year sentence against him. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction, first contending that the trial court erred when it permitted the State to present evidence regarding the victim's autopsy through the testimony of two medical examiners other than the medical examiner who performed the autopsy, thus causing a violation of his right to confrontation under both the U.S. and Alabama Constitutions. The State argued that the autopsy report and other associated evidence were admissible pursuant to the business-records exception to the rule excluding hearsay evidence. The appeals court held that admission of the report amounted to a constitutional violation, but that the error was harmless. The amount of evidence presented to support defendant's conviction, including his own testimony, was sufficient even without consideration of the autopsy report. Second, the demonstrative evidence presented by the State was not erroneously admitted, and the State did not fail to prove a proper chain of custody. Finally, because the jury found defendant guilty of manslaughter, the trial court did not err when it denied his motion for a judgment of acquittal as to the original murder charge.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

518 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Webster v. State


CR-01-1656


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


900 So. 2d 460; 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 52



March 26, 2004, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Webster v. State, 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 272 (Ala. Crim. App., May 21, 2004)
Reversed by Ex parte Stewart, 900 So. 2d 475, 2004 Ala. LEXIS 308 (Ala., Nov. 19, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Marshall Circuit Court. (CC-01-09; CC-01-10; and CC-01-11). Braxton L. Kittrell, Jr., TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.

* Note from the reporter of decisions: On November 19, 2004, on return to remand, the Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed as to defendant Greer, without opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the owner of a construction company and two county commissioners, challenged the decision of the Marshall Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted them under Alabama's Code of Ethics, Ala. Code § 136-25-1 et seq., specifically, for using an official position or office for personal gain, Ala. Code § 36-25-5(a), and for offering things of value for the purpose of influencing official action, Ala. Code § 36-25-7(a) and (b).


OVERVIEW: The evidence tended to establish that the commissioners would hire the construction company to do work in their districts, the company would overcharge the county, and then the commissioners would receive a share of the overcharge. Affirming in part, the court first held that the evidence presented by the State to corroborate the testimony of an accomplice witness was sufficient under Ala. Code § 12-21-222, and thus, defendants were not entitled to a judgment of acquittal. Moreover, it was within the State's discretion to charge the owner with an ethics violation because the Legislature did not intend to limit the application of the Ethics Code to public officials and employees and the owner was convicted under a complicity theory pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-2-23. And, finally, the court held that, although the State was not required to make an election when it charged one of the commissioners for violations of both Ala. Code § 36-25-5(a) and Ala. Code § 36-25-7(b), because the actions were alleged in the indictment to be part of one ongoing scheme or plan, it was error to convict him of both offenses because that was exactly the situation proscribed by Ala. Code § 13A-1-8(b).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the owners' convictions and sentences and one of the commissioner's conviction and sentence, but it remanded for the trial court to vacate one of the other commissioner's two convictions.

Adkins v. State


CR-99-0834


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


930 So. 2d 524; 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 68



March 26, 2004, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected September 13, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Adkins v. State, 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 2884 (Ala. Crim. App., May 28, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Adkins v. Alabama, 547 U.S. 1132, 126 S. Ct. 2022, 164 L. Ed. 2d 786, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 3889 (U.S., May 15, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from St. Clair Circuit Court. (CC-88-22.60).
Adkins v. State, 930 So. 2d 524, 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 85 (Ala. Crim. App., Apr. 26, 2002)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was convicted of three counts of capital murder and sentenced to death. His conviction and sentence were affirmed. The inmate filed a petition for postconviction relief pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32. The St. Clair Circuit Court (Alabama) denied the petition. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: In response to the inmate's various arguments that his attorneys failed to provide him with the effective assistance of counsel guaranteed by the Sixth Amendment, the appellate court concluded that: (1) the inmate was estopped from claiming ineffectiveness for failure to present mitigating evidence during the penalty phase of his trial when the inmate waived the presentation of mitigating evidence; (2) counsel's strategic choice not to present evidence regarding the inmate's mental health during the guilt phase of the inmate's trial did not satisfy the Strickland test for ineffective assistance; (3) the inmate failed to show that counsel provided ineffective assistance in arguing various pretrial motions as there was no evidence that, inter alia, motions were insufficient of incompletely drafted or that counsel did not effectively argue and present evidence in support of said motions; and (4) the trial court did not err in not allowing the inmate to introduce disciplinary reports from the Alabama State Bar concerning his attorneys as they were on unrelated matters and had no bearing on the attorneys' performance in the inmate's trial.


OUTCOME: The denial of the inmate's petition for postconviction relief was affirmed.

 

520 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Yeomans v. State


CR-01-0701   


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


898 So. 2d 878; 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 47



February 27, 2004, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 15, 2005.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Yeomans v. Alabama, 546 U.S. 879, 126 S. Ct. 175, 163 L. Ed. 2d 180, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 5875 (2005)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Yeomans v. State, 2013 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 23 (Ala. Crim. App., Mar. 29, 2013)
Post-conviction relief denied at Yeomans v. State, 2014 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 43 (Ala. Crim. App., June 13, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Geneva Circuit Court. (CC-2000-42; -43; -44; and -58).



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.

*Note from the reporter of decisions: On June 25, 2004, on return to remand, the Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed , without opinion. On October 15, 2004, that court denied rehearing, without opinion. On February 25, 2005, the Supreme Court denied certiorari review, without opinion (1040266).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Geneva Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted him of and sentenced him for three counts of capital murder under Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(10) for killing two or more persons during one course of conduct and one count of murder during the course of a robbery under § 13A-5-40(a)(2) following the beating and shooting deaths of his wife and her parents.


OVERVIEW: The evidence at trial established that defendant killed his wife and her parents after an altercation. Remanding, the court held, inter alia, that (1) because the incident giving right to three separate charges under § 13A-5-40(a)(10) were alternative methods of charging the same offense, double jeopardy principles were violated, and only one of these three convictions could stand; (2) there was no error, plain or otherwise, with regard to the consolidation of the charges for trial; (3) the jury had ample evidence from which it could reasonably conclude that defendant committed a robbery; (4) there was no plain error on the trial court's reasonable doubt instruction; (5) the record did not establish that defendant was mentally retarded, and thus, Atkins v. Virginia did not preclude imposition of the death sentence; (6) the sentencing order was remanded for compliance with Ala. Code § 13A-5-47 because the trial court's findings regarding the nonstatutory mitigation required clarification; and (7) on remand, the trial court was instructed to consider the aggravating circumstance of Ala. Code § 13A-5-49(8) because it was clearly supported by sufficient evidence.


OUTCOME: The court remanded to the trial court with directions to strike two of defendant's convictions and sentences for the murder of two or more persons pursuant to one scheme or course of conduct and to submit an amended sentencing order.

Jenkins v. State


CR-97-0864


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


972 So. 2d 111; 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 30



February 27, 2004, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected April 19, 2004.

As Corrected May 7, 2008.
Rehearing denied by Jenkins v. State, 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 2879 (Ala. Crim. App., May 21, 2004)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Ex parte Jenkins, 972 So. 2d 159, 2005 Ala. LEXIS 49 (Ala., 2005)
Motion denied by Jenkins v. Allen, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 41650 (N.D. Ala., Mar. 31, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from St. Clair Circuit Court. (CC-89-68.60).
Jenkins v. State, 627 So. 2d 1034, 1992 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 91 (Ala. Crim. App., 1992)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate, who was on death-row after being convicted of two counts of capital murder during the course of a kidnapping and a robbery, challenged the decision of the St. Clair Circuit Court (Alabama), which denied his petition for postconviction relief filed pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32, alleging, primarily, that he received ineffective assistance of trial and appellate counsel.


OVERVIEW: The victim's nude body was found on the side of a highway, and a witness testified that she last saw the victim with the inmate. Affirming the denial of the inmate's petition, the court held, inter alia, that (1) the inmate's claim that his constitutional rights were violated during voir dire was barred because it was first raised after the limitations period of former Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.2; (2) trial counsel was not ineffective for failing to pursue a Batson claim because Batson had not been extended to white defendants at the time of trial, and appellate counsel could not be deemed ineffective because the alleged error occurred on appeal to the state supreme court, where the inmate had no right to counsel, and thus, no right to effective assistance of counsel; (3) the inmate was not prejudiced by counsel's performance during sentencing because the aggravating circumstances far outweighed any mitigating circumstances, and, thus, death was the appropriate punishment; and (4) the trial court correctly determined that a sociologist's testimony was not mitigating evidence under Ala. Code § 13A-5-52 because it was not relevant to an "individualized sentencing determination."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's denial of the petition for postconviction relief.

Wood v. State


CR-01-0700


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


891 So. 2d 398; 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1

Writ of habeas corpus granted, in part, Writ of habeas corpus denied, in part Wood v. Allen, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 84933 (M.D. Ala., Nov. 20, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Pike Circuit Court. (CC-94-7.60).
Wood v. State, 891 So. 2d 398, 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 115 (Ala. Crim. App., 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellate court remanded the case to the Pike Circuit Court (Alabama) for the court to determine whether defendant was mentally retarded and whether his trial attorneys rendered ineffective assistance. After the circuit court complied with the appellate court's instructions, defendant submitted a brief concerning the remand proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's argument that he was mentally retarded, that his attorneys rendered ineffective assistance by not developing and presenting evidence that he was mentally retarded, and that his attorneys rendered ineffective assistance by not requesting a jury instruction on mental retardation was not properly before the appellate court, as they were not presented to the circuit court. Defendant also argued that his attorneys rendered ineffective assistance, because, inter alia, they allegedly did not investigate and present sufficient mitigating evidence during the penalty phase of his trial. The appellate court held that defendant failed to establish that the attorneys' performance was deficient and that he was prejudiced by their deficient performance. Finally, defendant argued that the circuit court improperly adopted verbatim the State's proposed order. The appellate court found no error, as the record was void of any indication that the circuit court's findings were clearly erroneous; the record supported the findings.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

McGowan v. State


CR-95-1775


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


990 So. 2d 931; 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 314



December 12, 2003, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication August 3, 2008.
As Corrected September 13, 2004.
Appeal after remand at McGowan v. State, 990 So. 2d 931, 2005 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 135 (Ala. Crim. App., July 8, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Conecuh Circuit Court. (CC-94-064).



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Conecuh Circuit Court, which convicted him of two counts of capital murder under Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(10) and (a)(2) and which sentenced him to death after conducting a sentencing hearing pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) in which the jury recommended that defendant be sentenced to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murdering the victims in the course of robbing them to secure funds to purchase crack-cocaine. Defendant raised numerous contentions on appeal, many of which were examined under the plain error doctrine of Ala. R. App. P. 45A. Remanding for further findings, the court held, among other things, that: (1) it was not error to deny defendant's challenge for cause to a juror who had been friends with a victim where she stated on voir dire that she could be impartial; (2) the trial court's "reasonable doubt" instruction did not constitute plain error; (3) defendant's statements that he was going to kill or injure the victims were admissible because they tended to show design to commit the crime; (4) defendant failed to show that the community was so saturated with prejudicial pretrial publicity that he was denied a fair trial; (5) the intent of Ala. Code § 13A-5-54 was followed when the trial court determined that defense counsel was qualified; (6) the trial court was required to make findings explaining its sentence of death where the jury recommended life without parole; and (7) defendant's substantial rights were not injuriously affected by cumulative error.


OUTCOME: The court remanded and instructed the trial court to enter a revised sentencing order containing written findings stating specific reasons regarding its consideration of the jury's recommendation of imprisonment for life without the possibility of parole, to treat the jury's recommendation as a mitigating circumstance, and to include specific findings regarding the aggravating circumstances that it found to exist.

Benton v. State


CR-02-0343


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


887 So. 2d 304; 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 298



December 2, 2003, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected January 14, 2004. Released for Publication October 1, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-00-5018.61).



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the dismissal of his petition for postconviction relief by the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama). Defendant had been convicted of the capital offense of robbery-murder. He was sentenced to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole. He did not appeal his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the State did not prove every element of the capital offense and that, therefore, the trial court did not have jurisdiction to render a judgment and impose a sentence in his case. The appellate court held the claims were nonjurisdictional and were precluded because he could have raised them at trial and on appeal, but did not. Defendant further argued that his trial counsel rendered ineffective assistance by allowing him to enter a guilty plea. Defendant did not specify which element or elements the State did not prove. Thus, his claim consisted of bare allegations and failed to satisfy his burden of pleading pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.3 and 32.6(b). The plea agreement was not necessarily void simply because defendant waived his right to pursue a direct appeal and postconviction relief. Finally, defendant argued that he did not voluntarily waive his right to pursue a direct appeal and postconviction relief. Specifically, he contended that the trial court and trial counsel did not properly explain to him those rights and the effects of waiving those rights. Neither the State nor the trial court refuted that claim. Thus, the matter had to be remanded.


OUTCOME: The appellate court remanded the case to the trial court for that court to make specific, written findings regarding defendant's claim that he did not voluntarily waive his right to pursue a direct appeal and postconviction relief.

 

525 of 745 DOCUMENTS


West v. State


CR-02-1219


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


890 So. 2d 205; 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 250



September 26, 2003, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Reversed by, Remanded by Ex parte West, 890 So. 2d 210, 2004 Ala. LEXIS 50 (Ala., Mar. 5, 2004)Released for Publication November 2, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Etowah Circuit Court. (CC-97-1105.60).
West v. State, 793 So. 2d 870, 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 255 (Ala. Crim. App., 2000)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed the judgment of the Etowah Circuit Court (Alabama) denying the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 where the inmate had been convicted of robbery-murder in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) (1975) and had been sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: A certificate of judgment was issued as to the inmate's conviction on February 23, 2001. On September 6, 2002, the inmate filed an Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 post-conviction petition. The trial court found that the inmate had not timely filed his petition within the one-year limitations period under Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.2(c). In making this finding, the trial court applied the version of Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.2 that had been amended on August 1, 2002, which had shortened the limitations period from two years to one year. The appellate court found that the amended version of Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.2 was properly applied. Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.2(c) was meant to apply retroactively to cases in which the appellate court issued a certificate of judgment before August 1, 2002, and cases in which the time to file an appeal lapsed before August 1, 2002. The Alabama Supreme Court issued an order that the two-year statute of limitations under former Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.2 was to remain in effect until July 31, 2002. The inmate, therefore, could have filed his petition as late as July 31, 2002, but he failed to do so.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Gavin v. Alabama, 160 L. Ed. 2d 1073, 125 S. Ct. 1054, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 840 (U.S., Jan. 24, 2005)

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from a judgment of the Cherokee Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted him of two counts of capital murder and one count of attempted murder. OVERVIEW: Appellant was seen by multiple witnesses shooting the driver of a van, then getting in and driving away. He fired shots at a police car in pursuit and was caught in the woods. Davis v. State


CR-02-0729


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


890 So. 2d 193; 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 247



September 26, 2003, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 2, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Davis v. State, 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1924 (Ala. Crim. App., Nov. 21, 2003)
Writ granted by, Reversed by, Remanded by Ex parte Davis, 890 So. 2d 199, 2004 Ala. LEXIS 18 (Ala., Feb. 6, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-98-131.60).
Davis v. State, 804 So. 2d 1153, 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 193 (Ala. Crim. App., 2000)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed from the denial by the Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama) of his motions for postconviction relief and to alter, amend, or vacate the denial of his postconviction motion, following the affirmance of his convictions and death sentences for capital murder and burglary-murder, and the denial by the Alabama Supreme Court and the United States Supreme Court and of his petitions for certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the postconviction motion was untimely under Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.2(c). The intermediate court held that the Alabama Supreme Court had amended Rule 32.2(c) to shorten the time-period for filing postconviction motions. In a later order, the Alabama Supreme Court provided an interpretation of the effective date of the amended rule, and had allowed the defendants affected by the change a reasonable time after the amendment to file a postconviction motion before the bar took effect. Because the inmate's motion was filed after that deadline, and because the applicable statute of limitations was the one that was in effect at the time an action was filed, Rule 32.2(c), as amended, applied to his motion. Thus the motion was untimely. The intermediate court held that it did not have the authority to grant him relief based on the amendment's violation of his rights to due process, to equal protection, to petition for habeas corpus review, and to not be exposed to ex post facto laws. Only the Alabama Supreme Court had rule-making authority, and the appellate court was bound by the Alabama Supreme Court's adoption of rules.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Slaton v. State


CR-00-1592


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


902 So. 2d 102; 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 243



September 26, 2003, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 28, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Slaton v. State, 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 3531 (Ala. Crim. App., Nov. 14, 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Decision reached on appeal by Slaton v. State, 27 So. 3d 626, 2008 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1418 (Ala. Crim. App., Aug. 15, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Marshall Circuit Court. (CC-87-200210.60).
Ex parte Slaton, 680 So. 2d 909, 1996 Ala. LEXIS 200 (Ala., July 12, 1996)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's conviction of committing a murder during the course of a rape, and associated death sentence, were affirmed, he petitioned the Marshall Circuit Court (Alabama) for postconviction relief under Ala. R. Crim. P. 32. The trial court denied his petition, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a juvenile at the time of the crime. The appellate court held Ala. Code § 15-12-21(d)'s scheme for paying defense counsel did not make counsel ineffective. No evidence showed counsel's conflict of interest for representing defendant's father against his mother or that counsel's adversarial relationship with the mother was deficient performance or prejudiced defendant. Counsel's failure to futilely seek to treat defendant as a youthful offender was not ineffective assistance. When the prosecutor recalled a witness, there was no misconduct to object to, as it was not shown the prosecutor discussed the witness's prior testimony with her or asked her to change it. Mental-health evidence presented on defendant's behalf was not deficient. Counsel was not ineffective by not seeking an instruction on felony murder as a lesser included offense due to diminished capacity, as Alabama did not observe diminished capacity. Counsel did not have to seek a "no significant criminal history" mitigator instruction, as the trial court so charged the jury. Waiving argument at sentencing before the court was not ineffective, as Ala. Code § 13A-5-47 did not allow more mitigation then.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

529 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Simmons v. State


CR-02-1477


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


879 So. 2d 1218; 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 218



August 29, 2003, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 3, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-00-508.61).
Simmons v. State, 854 So. 2d 1227, 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 872 (Ala. Crim. App., 2002)



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed the judgment of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) denying the inmate's Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 petition for post-conviction relief, where defendant pled guilty to unlawful distribution of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: The inmate pled guilty to the crime. The trial court sentenced him to a term of 20 years in prison. It split his sentence and ordered him to serve a term of three years in prison followed by five years on probation. The trial court also enhanced the inmate's sentence by five years, because the sale occurred within three miles of a school in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-12-250, and an additional five years, because the sale occurred within three miles of a public housing project in violation Ala. Code § 13A-12-270. Pursuant to Ala. Code § 15-18-8, the trial court was permitted to split the sentence if it was 20 years or less. The appellate court considered the enhancements under Ala. Code §§ 13A-12-250, -270 to be part of the aggregate sentence for the offense. As a result, the inmate's sentence was 30 years, not 20 years. Because the inmate's aggregate sentence was 30 years in prison, the trial court did not have jurisdiction to split his sentence. Where the State did not allege in the indictment the facts upon which the schoolyard and public housing project enhancements were based, this did not deprive the trial court of jurisdiction to impose the enhancements.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the trial court with instructions that the trial court was to set aside the split portion of the inmate's sentence. If the inmate moved to withdraw his guilty plea, the trial court was required to grant the motion.

Adams v. State


CR-98-0496


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


955 So. 2d 1037; 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 212



August 29, 2003, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
As Corrected January 18, 2008.
Appeal after remand at Adams v. State, 955 So. 2d 1037, 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 309 (Ala. Crim. App., Dec. 2, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-97-2403).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded.*



* Note from the Reporter of Decisions: On May 26, 2006, on return to remand, the Court of Criminal Appeals dismissed the appeal, without opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama) of four counts of capital murder and one count of robbery in the first degree. The jury recommended that defendant be sentenced to death for his capital-murder convictions. The trial court accepted the jury's recommendation and sentenced defendant to death. The trial court sentenced defendant to life imprisonment for his robbery conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a 17-year-old, entered the victim's home through a window at night, wearing a stocking mask, and threatened the husband with a knife. Defendant raped the victim, the wife. The husband left to get defendant money from an ATM machine. When he returned with the money, the victim sent the husband to a grocery store to cash a check. The husband told the store clerks what was happening. The police were notified. When the husband returned home, the police arrived, and entered the house with the husband. They found the wife's body, she had died from stab wounds, and saw defendant flee the house. Twenty minutes later, defendant was found hiding nearby. He had the victim's blood stains on his clothing. The knife and the mask were found nearby. Defendant told a jail instructor that he was the one who had raped and murdered the victim. On appeal, the court found that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction, defendant's statement was admissible for impeachment, the trial court properly ruled on the evidentiary issues and the jury selection, and the death sentence was proper. However, the robbery conviction was encompassed in one of the capital-murder convictions.


OUTCOME: The capital-murder convictions and death sentence were affirmed. However, the case was remanded for the circuit court to vacate defendant's conviction for robbery in the first degree and his sentence for that conviction because that offense was encompassed in one of his capital-murder convictions.

Ala. Dep't of Mental Health & Mental Retardation ex rel. McClothan v. State


CR-01-1508


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


873 So. 2d 1176; 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 182



August 29, 2003, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 13, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-92-3015) On Rehearing Ex Mero Motu.
Ala. Dep't of Mental Health & Mental Retardation ex rel. McClothan v. State, 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 116 (Ala. Crim. App., Apr. 25, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Alabama Department of Mental Health and Mental Retardation and a patient, challenged a decision from the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama), which denied the Department's motion to have the patient released from custody under Ala. R. Crim. P. 25.8.


OVERVIEW: The patient had been charged with arson in the first degree. A jury found the patient not guilty by reason of mental disease or defect. After the jury returned its verdict, an involuntary commitment proceeding was commenced. As a result, the patient was committed to the custody of the Department. Several years later, the Department filed a motion seeking to release the patient from its custody. After the motion was denied, the patient and the Department filed notice of appeal. In dismissing the appeal, the court determined that appellate jurisdiction only existed as provided by law. An appeal in a criminal case could have only been taken from a judgment of conviction. Moreover, a commitment proceeding following an acquittal was not a postconviction proceeding under Ala. Code § 12-3-9. Under Ala. R. Crim. P. 25.8, the Department, among other persons, was permitted to file a motion seeking release of a patient. Further procedures were outlined in the Alabama Criminal Psychopath Release Restriction Act, Ala. Code § 15-15-60 et seq. However, neither Ala. R. Crim. P. 25.8 nor the Act outlined any procedures for appeal. As such, the court had no choice but to dismiss the case.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

532 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Hyshaw v. State


CR-02-0635


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


893 So. 2d 1239; 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 194



August 29, 2003, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 12, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Hyshaw v. State, 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 2906 (Ala. Crim. App., Oct. 24, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-02-3597).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama), which sentenced him to 15 years in prison after he pleaded guilty to using a false identity to obstruct justice, a violation of Ala. Code § 13A-8-194.


OVERVIEW: When defendant, who had several outstanding arrest warrants, was caught by police officers, he gave a false name and birth date. On appeal, the court rejected defendant's challenges to § 13A-8-194. The court held that § 13A-8-194 was not unconstitutionally vague because it adequately put ordinary people on notice of the conduct that was prohibited, and further it did not criminalize innocent behavior. Nor was § 13A-8-194 unconstitutionally overbroad. The statute prohibited the use of identification documents or the identifying information of another person or of a fictitious person for the purpose of avoiding summons, arrest, or prosecution, or to impede a criminal investigation. Therefore, it did not involve constitutionally protected speech. Thus, the overbreadth doctrine did not apply. After a thorough examination of other jurisdictions' laws, the court held that there was no violation of Ala. Const. art. IV, § 45's single subject rule because the offense of using a false identity to obstruct justice was specifically listed in the title of 2001 Ala. Acts 2001-312 and that act dealt with only one subject. Finally, it was clear that defendant's conduct violated the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.
