Coleman v. State


CR-02-0683


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


886 So. 2d 891; 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 202



August 29, 2003, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 1, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Mobile Circuit Court. (CC-98-3451.61).
Coleman v. State, 836 So. 2d 999, 2001 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 2164 (Ala. Crim. App., 2001)



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a second Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 petition attacking his convictions for felony murder, first-degree robbery, first-degree burglary, and first-degree kidnapping. He was sentenced to life imprisonment on each conviction, the sentences to be served concurrently. The Mobile Circuit Court (Alabama) previously affirmed his convictions and sentences.


OVERVIEW: The jury found defendant guilty of robbery, burglary, kidnapping, and, without naming the included felony, felony murder. The trial court sentenced him to life imprisonment for the felony-murder conviction and to life imprisonment on each of the underlying convictions, to run concurrently with the other convictions. The appellate court found defendant's contention that he was subjected to double jeopardy had merit. The record was clear that at least one of the felonies had to be included in the felony-murder conviction and thus could not stand. Moreover, the fact that the felony-murder sentence was to run concurrently to the other sentences did not make the error harmless.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

Simpson v. State


CR-01-2408


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


874 So. 2d 575; 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 185



August 29, 2003, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected January 14, 2004. As Corrected February 6, 2004. Released for Publication March 12, 2004. As Corrected September 13, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Chambers Circuit Court. (CC-02-48).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Chambers Circuit Court (Alabama), which found him guilty of leaving the scene of an accident involving injuries or death without providing the information or assistance, as required under Ala. Code § 32-10-1. Defendant also challenged the 20-year sentence imposed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant struck a motorcycle rider while he was crossing some railroad tracks. Defendant left the scene of the accident, and he hid the vehicle involved in the accident. After the car was discovered, defendant contended that he hit the motorcycle because he did not see its brake lights. When defendant did not appear for his trial, it was conducted in absentia. Later, defendant challenged the verdict and the sentence imposed. In affirming, the court determined that defendant impliedly waived his right to presence under Ala. R. Crim. P. 9.1(b). The evidence showed that defendant had notice of the time and place of the trial. He was also informed of his right to be present. The court declined to find that defendant was only able to waive his rights after the trial had commenced. The court also noted that defendant failed to appear at his sentencing hearing. However, the court did not consider the issue because defendant did not include it in his appellate brief. The trial court did not err in failing to instruct the jury that defendant had a right to leave the scene. There was no evidence to show that defendant was threatened at the time of the accident.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the sentence imposed.

 

535 of 745 DOCUMENTS


State v. A.R.C.


CR-02-1359


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


873 So. 2d 261; 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 364



August 15, 2003, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 12, 2004. As Corrected September 13, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Covington Circuit Court. (CC-2001-321).



DISPOSITION:  Writ of mandamus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Covington Circuit Court (Alabama) made a ruling in defendant's trial on a charge of first-degree sodomy that the State could not admit out-of-court statements made by the five-year-old victim because the statements were not sufficiently corroborated. The State then filed a petition for writ of mandamus in the appellate court in an attempt to seek review of that ruling.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with first-degree sodomy. His case was called to trial. The State knew that it was going to try to introduce certain out-of-court statements made by the alleged five-year-old victim, but the State did not seek a pre-trial ruling on the admissibility of those statements, although it could have done so. Instead, during the middle of the trial, the State tried to get the statements admitted. The trial court excluded the statements after finding that they were not sufficiently corroborated. The State then filed a petition for writ of mandamus in the appellate court that would direct the trial court to set aside the order barring the admission of the statements. The jury in the trial was recessed pending the outcome of the mandamus petition. The appellate court found that the State had an adequate remedy at law which it chose not to exercise, that of obtaining a pretrial ruling on the admissibility of the statements, and which it could have appealed if the pretrial ruling was unfavorable. It then found that mandamus was not a substitute for an appeal and that it was not to be permitted where, as in the present case, a sufficient remedy at law existed.


OUTCOME: The State's petition for writ of mandamus was denied.

 

536 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Vaughn v. State


CR-01-1774


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


880 So. 2d 1178; 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 164



June 27, 2003, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 6, 2004. As Corrected April 19, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Vaughn v. State, 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 361 (Ala. Crim. App., Aug. 15, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-01-1491).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama) of failing to disclose a conflict of interest in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-10-62. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was hired by the State as a consultant to study sites under consideration by state agencies for building warehouses. He recommended that the State purchase certain property, and the State paid him $ 25,000 for his services. A company of which he was half owner acquired an option to buy the same property, but he did not disclose this to the State. The appellate court found the indictment was sufficient. For defendant to have been a "public servant" for purposes of § 13A-10-62, the compensation paid to him did not have to constitute more than 50 percent of his income; therefore, that fact was not an element of the offense and did not have to be charged in the indictment. The indictment did not have to set forth facts establishing a "known potential conflicting interest." As § 13A-10-62 defined the offense of failing to disclose a conflict of interest with sufficient definitiveness to provided fair warning of what conduct was prohibited and who fell within the scope of the statute, it was not void for vagueness. A jury instruction regarding the definition of "substantial discretionary function" was proper. The evidence had been sufficient to convict.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Clark v. State


CR-99-1062


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


896 So. 2d 584; 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 170



June 27, 2003, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected August 6, 2003.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Clark v. Alabama, 545 U.S. 1130, 125 S. Ct. 2930, 162 L. Ed. 2d 870, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 4899 (2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at Clark v. State, 2015 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 19 (Ala. Crim. App., Mar. 13, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Baldwin Circuit Court. (CC-98-0353).
Clark v. State, 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 68 (Ala. Crim. App., Feb. 28, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Conviction and sentence of death affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Baldwin Circuit Court (Alabama). A jury convicted defendant of capital murder that was committed during first-degree robbery. The trial court accepted the jury's recommendation of a death sentence. On remand, the trial court submitted an amended sentencing order.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of capital murder following the robbery and stabbing death of a gas station owner. The court reviewed most of his claims for plain error and affirmed the judgment. The trial court had not improperly expanded the heinous, atrocious, or cruel criteria when it stated that its finding that the murder was especially heinous was based in part on the victim's mental and physical handicap and that defendant was aware of that when he killed him. The procedure by which defendant was sentenced to death fully complied with the Ring decision of the United States Supreme Court. The existence of the aggravating circumstance that the capital offense was committed during a robbery was proven beyond a reasonable doubt. Because only one aggravating circumstance had to exist to impose a death sentence, the jury's guilt-phase verdict alone exposed defendant to a range of punishment that included the death penalty. The trial court's finding of the additional aggravating circumstance that the murder was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel was a factor that only had application in the weighing of aggravating and mitigating circumstances, which was not a factual determination.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the judgment.

Writ of habeas corpus denied Lee v. Thomas, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 75470 (S.D. Ala., May 30, 2012)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Lee v. State, 2017 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 10 (Ala. Crim. App., Feb. 10, 2017)

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Dallas Circuit Court (Alabama) of three counts of capital murder and one count of attempted murder. The jury recommended that defendant be sentenced to life imprisonment without possibility of parole. The trial court overrode the jury's recommendation and sentenced defendant to death for the capital offenses and life imprisonment for the attempted murder conviction. Defendant appealed.

Defendant's actions were captured by a surveillance camera. He gave a confession after he was captured. OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed.

 

539 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. State


CR-99-2249


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


931 So. 2d 736; 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 136



May 30, 2003, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 12, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Martin v. State, 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 348 (Ala. Crim. App., Aug. 22, 2003)
Motion to strike granted by, Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Ex parte Martin, 931 So. 2d 759, 2004 Ala. LEXIS 337 (Ala., Dec. 10, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Mobile Circuit Court. (CC-99-2696).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Mobile Circuit Court (Alabama), after a jury trial, convicted defendant of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(7) (1975) murder made capital because it was committed for pecuniary gain. Defendant killed his wife to collect about $ 377,000 of life insurance proceeds from a number of policies. The trial court overrode the jury's eight to four recommendation for life in prison and sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The jury found defendant killed his wife by staging a car wreck, and while she was still alive, intentionally burned her to death. Defendant did not challenge the sufficiency of the State's evidence, but because the death penalty was imposed, the appeals court reviewed the evidence to find it was sufficient to support the capital murder conviction. Defendant had told another inmate he killed his wife. The wife's friend's hearsay testimony that the wife said she thought defendant might kill her was admissible to show the wife's state of mind to refute defendant's statement that they had a good relationship. The appeals court restated chain of custody rules and determined the weakness of a link in the custody of defendant's clothing, containing petroleum residue, raised a credibility, not admissibility issue. The appeals court discussed Frye, Brady, suppression of his abandoned highway patrolman footlocker evidence, continuances, police opinion (as opposed to expert) testimony on the crime scene, and judicial bias issues in its primarily plain error review. The jury's finding the pecuniary gain aggravator satisfied Ring and permitted the trial court to impose death.


OUTCOME: The appeals court stated (1) the trial court's imposition of sentence after giving weight to the jury's recommendation was approved and did not violate Ring since the jury found one aggravator, so finding a second did not increase the sentence, and (2) the death sentence was constitutional, proportionate, and not imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor, and affirmed the judgment.

Lewis v. State


CR-99-1155


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


889 So. 2d 623; 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 135



May 30, 2003, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 2, 2004.
Writ of mandamus denied, in part, Writ of mandamus granted, in part Ex parte Lewis, 2008 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 123 (Ala. Crim. App., July 25, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Baldwin Circuit Court. (CC-98-664; CC-98-879; and CC-98-880).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.

*Note from the reporter of decisions: On October 24, 2003, on return to remand, the Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed, without opinion. On November 14, 2003, that court denied rehearing, without opinion. On April 30, 2004, the Supreme Court denied certiorari review, without opinion (1030298).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Baldwin Circuit Court (Alabama) of capital murder, attempted murder, first degree attempted kidnapping, first degree attempted rape, and first degree robbery, and was sentenced to death and eight consecutive sentences of life imprisonment without parole. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found competent. The appellate court held admitting crime circumstances at the competency trial was proper, and any error was invited. Consolidating similar noncapital and capital offenses was proper. Ala. R. Crim. P. 11.2(b)(1), precluding competency test results in the guilt phase, was not violated by telling the guilt phase jury it would only hear the case if another jury found defendant competent. Matching evidence and population-frequency-statistical evidence as to nuclear deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA) and mitochondrial DNA were admissible, without the known or potential rate of error. The State proved a corpus delicti independent of defendant's confessions, which were admissible. Defendant was not entitled to an abuse of a corpse lesser-included offense instruction. All mitigating evidence was considered. Defendant was not mentally retarded. A jury found aggravators allowing a death sentence arising from the offenses, beyond a reasonable doubt, and factors not so found involved prior convictions or weighing aggravators and mitigators and did not have to be found by a jury. Defendant's attempted kidnapping sentences exceeded the maximum and were void.


OUTCOME: Defendant's capital murder, attempted murder, attempted rape, and robbery convictions and sentences were affirmed, as was his attempted kidnapping conviction, but his attempted kidnapping sentences were reversed, and the matter was remanded for resentencing on those convictions.

Peraita v. State


CR-01-0289


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


897 So. 2d 1161; 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 137



May 30, 2003, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected July 21, 2003. Released for Publication February 16, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Peraita v. State, 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 344 (Ala. Crim. App., Aug. 15, 2003)
Affirmed by Ex parte Peraita, 897 So. 2d 1227, 2004 Ala. LEXIS 138 (Ala., June 4, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Escambia Circuit Court. (CC-00-293).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of two counts of capital murder; the murder was made capital because the defendant committed it while under sentence of life imprisonment, Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(6), and because he had been convicted of murder within the 20 years preceding the capital offense, § 13A-5-40(a)(13). The Escambia Circuit Court (Alabama) sentenced defendant to death; his motion for a new trial was overruled by operation of law. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another inmate fatally stabbed the victim after he slapped defendant. The trial court did not allow a prison psychology expert to testify as to defendant's state of mind and the process of institutionalization. The appellate court approved, as such testimony would have been speculation; and even if it had been relevant to the self-defense issue, it was excludable under Miss. R. Evid. 403 due to the danger of confusing the issues or misleading the jury. The State was properly allowed to prove defendant's prior convictions, as they were elements of the offense, and were not introduced to prove his bad character. His conviction and sentence for capital murder were not disproportionate because his allegedly more culpable co-defendant was not charged with capital murder, since the co-defendant was not eligible for such prosecution. Improper testimony about defendant's admission of killing the victim was not grounds for a mistrial, as the judge struck it and gave a curative instruction, and the evidence was cumulative to defendant's other statements that were properly admitted. As defendant was not mentally retarded, executing him was not cruel or unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentence of death were affirmed.

Wood v. State


CR-01-0700


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


891 So. 2d 398; 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 115



April 25, 2003, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 11, 2004. Released for Publication November 24, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Wood v. State, 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 329 (Ala. Crim. App., May 23, 2003)
Appeal after remand at Wood v. State, 891 So. 2d 398, 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1 (Ala. Crim. App., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Pike Circuit Court. (CC-94-7.60).
Ex parte Wood, 715 So. 2d 819, 1998 Ala. LEXIS 84 (Ala., 1998)



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of the capital offense of burglary-murder and was sentenced to death. His conviction was affirmed on direct appeal. He filed an Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 petition, challenging his conviction and sentence of death on grounds that he was mentally retarded and his counsel had been ineffective in not raising this issue. The Pike Circuit Court (Alabama) denied relief, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed that his trial attorneys were ineffective because they did not develop and present evidence that he was retarded. The appellate court held that in light of the Atkins decision, the inmate was entitled to an evidentiary hearing to determine if he was retarded and whether his counsel had been ineffective. The circuit court erred by refusing to allow a psychologist to testify as an expert on the grounds that she was not licensed to practice psychology in Alabama and that practicing psychology without a license was a misdemeanor; Ala. R. Evid. 702, not the licensing statutes, governed the qualifications of expert witnesses. The circuit court erred in using a bifurcated approach to determine whether to allow the inmate to present expert psychological testimony, as the inmate did not merely make bare allegations, but produced an IQ in the borderline range of intellectual functioning, and a letter in which one of his attorneys recommended that they request an independent psychological evaluation for purposes of sentencing. Finally, the circuit court erred in finding that the inmate was not retarded, as it lacked sufficient information to make this finding.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the circuit court with instructions that it conduct an evidentiary hearing and make specific findings of fact as to the inmate's claims that he was mentally retarded and that his trial attorneys rendered ineffective assistance.

Moody v. State


CR-96-0994


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA

Writ of certiorari denied Ex parte Moody, 888 So. 2d 605, 2004 Ala. LEXIS 68 (Ala., 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Moody v. Alabama, 543 U.S. 964, 125 S. Ct. 442, 160 L. Ed. 2d 331, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 7231 (2004)

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-92-726).
Ex parte Moody, 681 So. 2d 276, 1996 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 155 (Ala. Crim. App., 1996)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) of two counts of capital murder and assault in the first-degree. The trial court accepted the jury's recommendation and sentenced defendant to death. The trial court also sentenced defendant, as a habitual felony offender, to life imprisonment for the first-degree assault conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant mailed pipe bombs to a federal judge and other parties. The judge was killed by the pipe bomb that he received and his wife was injured. Defendant represented himself at trial, as he refused the court-appointed lawyers and the trial court would not grant another continuance so that defendant could be represented by the lawyers that he wanted on the eve of trial. OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed.

Ziegler v. State


CR-00-1987


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


886 So. 2d 127; 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 56



February 28, 2003, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 1, 2004.
Appeal after remand at Ziegler v. State, 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 147 (Ala. Crim. App., June 27, 2003). As Corrected August 6, 2003. As Corrected October 23, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Mobile Circuit Court. (CC00-2891).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as to conviction; remanded with directions as to sentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murder in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(1) (1975), made capital because it was committed during the course of a kidnapping. The Mobile Circuit Court (Alabama) ordered that defendant be sentenced to death. Defendant filed a motion for a new trial, which was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim was brutally beaten and stabbed to death by several people including defendant. The appellate court held that the jury instructions on intent and on accomplice liability, when considered together, were proper, and they were thorough and specific enough to ensure that a guilty verdict would not be returned unless the jury found that defendant had the specific intent to kill. Sufficient evidence was admitted to find defendant had the specific intent to kill. Thus, no plain error occurred with regard to the jury instruction. Further, there was no plain error as to the trial court's instructions on the "especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel" aggravating circumstance in Ala. Code § 13A-5-49(8) (1975), as it effectively narrowed the scope of the aggravating circumstance and informed the jury that it applied only to those capital offenses that were "unnecessarily torturous" to the victim. The evidence overwhelmingly established that aggravating circumstance. However, the trial court did not make specific findings regarding the existence or nonexistence of the remainder of the statutory aggravating and mitigating circumstances, as required.


OUTCOME: The portion of the judgment which ordered the death sentence was remanded for resentencing. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

 

545 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Quetgles v. State


CR-01-1596


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


884 So. 2d 911; 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 64



February 28, 2003, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 8, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Quetgles v. State, 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 341 (Ala. Crim. App., Apr. 18, 2003)
Writ of certiorari quashed Ex parte Quetgles, 2004 Ala. LEXIS 16 (Ala., Jan. 30, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Mobile Circuit Court. (CC-01-1382 and CC-01-1383).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Mobile Circuit Court, Alabama, convicted defendant of two counts of violating Ala. Code § 13A-12-200.11 (1975), which prohibited displaying genitals, and sentenced him thereon. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his convictions, arguing that the statute under which he was convicted was unconstitutional. Specifically, he contended that the statute was overbroad, and that it was a content-based restriction on his First Amendment right to free expression. The appeals court disagreed. The statute distinguished among the forms of expression being proscribed; it was not all nudity, but rather only nudity for entertainment purposes, that the Alabama Legislature sought to ban. Ala. Code § 13A-12-200.11 (1975) was not neutral as to content because it explicitly permitted certain types of nude expression while restricting other types of nude expression based entirely on whether the expression is for entertainment purposes. The appeals court thus held that the State met its burden of proving that the state legislature's predominant motive in passing the statute was a concern about increased crime and other secondary effects. Section 200.11 restricted no more expression than was essential to accomplish the government's substantial interest in protecting public order and morality by combating the negative secondary effects of nude entertainment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Stallworth v. State


CR-98-0366


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


868 So. 2d 1128; 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 21



January 31, 2003, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected September 10, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Stallworth v. State, 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 321 (Ala. Crim. App., Mar. 7, 2003)
Writ of certiorari denied Ex parte Stallworth, 868 So. 2d 1189, 2003 Ala. LEXIS 210 (Ala., 2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Stallworth v. Alabama, 540 U.S. 1057, 124 S. Ct. 828, 157 L. Ed. 2d 711, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 8732 (2003)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Writ of mandamus granted, Stay lifted by State v. Stallworth, 941 So. 2d 327, 2006 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 65 (Ala. Crim. App., 2006)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Remanded by Stallworth v. State, 2013 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 100 (Ala. Crim. App., Nov. 8, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Baldwin Circuit Court. (CC-98-112 and CC-98-113).
Stallworth v. State, 868 So. 2d 1128, 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 42 (Ala. Crim. App., 2002)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon request of the appellate court, defendant and the State briefed the applicability of the Atkins and Ring decisions on defendant's death sentence. Defendant's convictions for two murders had been affirmed and the case had been remanded for the trial court (Alabama) to correct deficiencies in its sentencing order twice. The trial court had complied with the appellate court's instructions to amend the sentencing orders.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he should be resentenced, as he was borderline mentally retarded. The appellate court held defendant was not mentally retarded under Ala. Code § 15-24-2 or under any State's statute that prohibited the execution of a mentally retarded person. Defendant's IQ tested above the significant sub-average range. Defendant functioned in society. There was no evidence that defendant had a history of mental retardation. The jury found that defendant committed two murders during the course of a robbery. Robbery was an aggravating circumstance that supported a death sentence. The trial court was left to decide under Apprendi and Ring whether defendant was under a sentence of imprisonment, as he was on probation for a prior assault conviction. The evidence supported the trial court's finding that the murders were especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel as compared to other capital murders. The indictment was not required to list the aggravating circumstances the State intended to prove. The sentence was not imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor. The aggravating circumstances outweighed the mitigating circumstances in each case.


OUTCOME: The death sentence was affirmed.

Turner v. State


CR-99-1568


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


924 So. 2d 737; 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 245



November 22, 2002, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected December 12, 2002. Second Correction January 30, 2003. As Corrected July 21, 2003. As Corrected October 10, 2006.
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Turner v. State, 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 113 (Ala. Crim. App., Apr. 25, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Limestone Circuit Court. (CC-99-318; CC-96-568).
Harris v. State, 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 198 (Ala. Crim. App., Sept. 27, 2002)



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Limestone Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted him of two counts of capital murder, robbery, theft, burglary, and rape, and sentenced him to various terms of imprisonment, and to death based on a finding of four aggravating circumstances.


OVERVIEW: Defendant murdered his victim during the course of a rape and robbery. His appeal on multiple issues required remand on several issues. However, the court found the following to lack merit: (1) a 46-month delay, although presumptively prejudicial, was not erroneous based on other factors, including that delays were all attributable to defendant; (2) there was no racial discrimination found in the method of selecting grand jury-forepersons; (3) there was no prosecutorial vindictiveness in a second indictment which contained additional charges; (4) removal of prospective jurors was proper where some had medical issues and others had been properly challenged for cause; (5) defendant's arrest was proper and his confession was voluntary; (6) photographs and DNA evidence were properly admitted; (7) there was no reversible prosecutor misconduct; and (8) jury instructions were proper. Remand was required due to double jeopardy issues on the lesser-included offenses and deficiencies in the death sentence order. Aggravating circumstances that were remanded included a prior conviction based on a nolo contendere plea and the need for further details as to the heinous nature of the crime.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the matter in order to vacate defendant's convictions and sentences for robbery, theft, and rape. Remand was further required in order to correct deficiencies in the sentencing order with respect to several of the aggravating circumstances, including the prohibition against consideration of a prior conviction and arrests, and for further fact-finding as to the heinousness or cruelty of the crime.

Jolly v. State


CR-00-2693


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


858 So. 2d 305; 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 246



November 22, 2002, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected. Rehearing Denied January 24, 2003. Released for Publication September 24, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Jolly v. Ala., 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 326 (Ala. Crim. App., Jan. 24, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Calhoun Circuit Court. (CC-00-456).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Calhoun Circuit Court (Alabama) that convicted him of reckless manslaughter pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-6-3 after he consumed alcohol, and was involved in a head-on automobile accident.


OVERVIEW: Various witnesses either saw defendant, aged 20, drinking or smelled alcohol on his breath. The appellate court held, inter alia, that a number of defendant's allegations were not preserved for appeal. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by denying defendant's application for youthful offender status. It properly limited defendant's character evidence to his general reputation in the community, and terminated the evidence when it became cumulative. Although Ala. Code § 32-5A-191(b) treated those under 21 years of age differently than those over 21 years of age, the statute was not unconstitutional, since it was rationally related to the government purpose of prohibiting underage drinking and driving. There was no evidence that the trial court was biased or hostile. Defendant's sentences were within the statutory range, and the trial court explained its reasons for imposing them pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 26.8.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

549 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Tomlin v. State


CR-98-2126


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


909 So. 2d 213; 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 257



November 22, 2002, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled November 22, 2002. As Corrected September 10, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Mobile Circuit Court. (CC-93-1494.80).
Tomlin v. State, 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 124 (Ala. Crim. App., May 31, 2002)



DISPOSITION: APPLICATION OVERRULED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed an application for rehearing in an attempt to have the appellate court consider the effect of a recent United States Supreme Court case after he was convicted of capital murder and sentenced to death for killing two people, and his conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of killing two people during one course of conduct and sentenced to death. The appellate court affirmed. While defendant's application for rehearing was pending, the United States Supreme Court released its Ring decision which applied its Apprendi holding to death-penalty cases and stated that any fact that increased a defendant's punishment to death had to be presented to a jury and proven beyond a reasonable doubt. Defendant argued in a supplemental brief that because the fact findings necessary to support imposition of the death penalty in his case were never made by a jury, he had to be resentenced. He also argued that federal law should condemn imposition of the death penalty by a judge rather than a jury. The appellate court rejected both arguments and denied his application for rehearing. It found that the jury's verdict that he killed two people during one course of conduct necessarily meant the jury found, beyond a reasonable doubt, that at least one aggravating circumstance existed that supported a death sentence. It also found that the United States Constitution permitted a trial judge, acting alone, to impose a capital sentence.


OUTCOME: The application for rehearing was overruled.

 

550 of 745 DOCUMENTS


J.L.N. v. State


CR-00-2209


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


894 So. 2d 738; 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 231



October 25, 2002, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 1, 2005. As Modified on Denial of Rehearing January 7, 2003.
Reversed by, Remanded by J.L.N. v. State, 2004 Ala. LEXIS 140 (Ala., June 4, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Chambers Circuit Court. (CC-01-24).
Nelson v. State, 837 So. 2d 900, 2001 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1785 (Ala. Crim. App., 2001)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND JUDGMENT RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with establishing a residence in violation of the residence restrictions set forth in the Alabama Community Notification Act, Ala. Code §§ 15-20-20 to 15-20-37 (1975), in violation of Ala. Code § 15-20-26(b) (1975), and he filed a motion to dismiss the charges. The Chambers Circuit Court (Alabama) denied defendant's motion, convicted defendant of the charge, and sentenced him to six years in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of second-degree rape after he had consensual sexual intercourse with his girlfriend, who was 15 years old at the time. After defendant was released from confinement, his girlfriend and his girlfriend's mother moved into his house. When police learned that defendant was living with his girlfriend, they charged him with violating Ala. Code § 15-20-26(b) (1975) by establishing a residence within 1,000 feet of property on which his victim or any member of the victim's immediate family lived. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the charges and attached statements from his girlfriend and his girlfriend's mother to his motion which showed that defendant and his girlfriend were engaged to be married and that his girlfriend's mother had consented to the marriage. The appellate court held that (1) defendant had standing to challenge the statute on the basis of the argument that it unconstitutionally impinged on his right to marry; and (2) the statute was overbroad because it contained no exemption from its punitive provisions and no procedure by which a convicted sex offender could petition a court for an exemption.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and rendered judgment for defendant.

Looney v. State


CR-01-0162


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


881 So. 2d 1061; 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 199



September 27, 2002, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected August 6, 2003. Released for Publication August 17, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Limestone Circuit Court. (CV-01-349.60).



DISPOSITION: CASE TRANSFERRED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant inmate filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus on the ground that he had been subject to cruel and unusual punishment in prison. The Limestone Circuit Court, Alabama, denied the inmate's petition. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate alleged that he was subjected to cruel and unusual punishment because there was no intercom system in the prison and the guards were unable to hear him yell for help if he was injured. The trial court denied the petition on the ground that it failed to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. The inmate's notice appeal indicated that he wished to appeal the ruling to the court of civil appeals, however, the notice of appeal completed by the circuit clerk's office indicated that the appeal was to the court of criminal appeals. The appellate court held that the inmate's manipulation of the system by mislabeling the petition to avoid paying a filing fee did not raise a claim that was cognizable in a habeas corpus petition but instead asked for injunctive and monetary relief. Thus, the case was transferred to the court of civil appeals.


OUTCOME: The case was transferred.

553 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Dowdell v. State


CR-01-0610


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


854 So. 2d 1195; 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 150



June 28, 2002, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 24, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Dowdell v. State, 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1136 (Ala. Crim. App., Aug. 9, 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-86-2293.61; CC-86-2294.61).
Dowdell v. State, 555 So. 2d 1198, 1989 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 3043 (Ala. Crim. App., 1989)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) which denied his petition for postconviction relief, filed pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32, in which he attacked his 1986 conviction for first-degree rape and the resulting prison sentence.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied defendant relief because it determined the petition was time-barred under Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.2(c), and procedurally barred under Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.2(a)(3). On appeal, defendant argued the trial court erred in summarily denying his petition. The appellate court advised defendant had until April 1, 1989, to timely file a petition for postconviction relief based on his claim the Alabama Constitution of 1901 was unconstitutional because it had been adopted to disenfranchise African-Americans. Because defendant failed to do so, the appellate court concluded that claim was barred by the two-year limitations period set out in Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.2(c). In addition, the appellate court noted that Alabama courts recognized the admissibility of DNA testing since 1991. The appellate court determined that had defendant filed his petition within a reasonable time, his claim that he had only recently learned about DNA testing would have been credible and would have been considered on the merits. However, because defendant waited more than 10 years to file his petition, the appellate court concluded the trial court correctly determined the claim was time-barred.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment.

 

554 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Baird v. State


CR-00-2047


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


849 So. 2d 223; 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 156



June 28, 2002, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected July 27, 2002. As Corrected November 11, 2002. As Corrected October 23, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Baird v. State, 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1139 (Ala. Crim. App., Aug. 16, 2002)
Writ of certiorari denied Ex parte Baird, 849 So. 2d 251, 2002 Ala. LEXIS 325 (Ala., 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. CC-99-1607.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) of intentional murder and felony-murder. The trial court sentenced defendant, as a habitual offender, to two consecutive terms of life in prison without the possibility of parole. Defendant filed a motion for a new trial, which the trial court denied following a hearing. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant threatened to kill the two victims, husband and wife, the day of the murders. Defendant was arrested for driving under the influence the evening of the murders. The victims' bodies were later found with six bullets in them. A gun with six empty cartridges, one victim's prescription bottles, and other items belonging to that victim were discovered in defendant's vehicle. Two witnesses testified that defendant took measures while in jail to dispose of his clothing. An investigator told defendant he needed to work things out with God and pray. Later, defendant confessed to killing the victims in video and audio recordings in the presence of his wife and the investigator. On appeal, the court found that (1) the video confession and statement were properly admitted; (2) the investigator was not a counselor; (3) defendant was allowed to cross-examine witnesses; (4) the items found in the car were admissible; (5) the trial court did not permit hearsay evidence to be admitted; (6) a videotape and photographs of the crime scene were admissible; (7) the trial court did not improperly instruct the jury; (8) there was no double jeopardy; and (9) the evidence was sufficient.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Duke v. State


CR-98-1218


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


889 So. 2d 1; 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 115



May 31, 2002, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected October 17, 2002. Released for Publication November 2, 2004.
Appeal after remand at Duke v. State, 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 84 (Ala. Crim. App., Mar. 21, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Shelby Circuit Court. (CC-97-383).
Samra v. State, 771 So. 2d 1108, 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 171 (Ala. Crim. App., 1999)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS TO CONVICTION; REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS AS TO SENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of capital murder in the Shelby Circuit Court (Alabama) and sentenced to death. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his accomplices murdered four people. The appellate court held the trial court did not abuse its discretion by denying a change of venue for pre-trial publicity, nor did it err in trying defendant as an adult. Defendant did not show the trial court's trial security measures were an abuse of discretion. Defendant's accomplice could use a mannequin to show how two victims were killed. The State's peremptory challenges were not purposeful racial or gender discrimination. Each juror affirmatively said he or she could set aside feelings in favor of the death penalty. The exclusion of jurors unalterably opposed to the death penalty was proper. The prosecutor did not impermissibly bolster a prosecution witness's credibility, and the jury was instructed not to consider any such comment. The trial court's failure to charge the jury on the need for accomplice corroboration was harmless. But the trial court did not specify why it found the "especially heinous, atrocious or cruel" aggravating circumstance applicable. The trial court had to find if defendant's background and family history was mitigating evidence, and state what weight it gave this evidence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed. The matter was remanded for further findings as to sentencing.

Tomlin v. State


CR-98-2126


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


909 So. 2d 213; 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 124



May 31, 2002, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected September 10, 2003.
Rehearing overruled by Tomlin v. State, 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 257 (Ala. Crim. App., Nov. 22, 2002)
Reversed by, Remanded by Ex parte Tomlin, 2003 Ala. LEXIS 301 (Ala., Oct. 3, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Mobile Circuit Court. (CC-93-1494.80).
Tomlin v. State, 695 So. 2d 157, 1996 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 158 (Ala. Crim. App., 1996)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who underwent his fourth trial, appealed from his conviction and sentence by the Mobile Circuit Court (Alabama) for murder, an offense punishable by death because two or more people were intentionally killed pursuant to one act or a series of acts. Defendant moved that the trial court accept the previously entered jury recommendation of 12-0 for life imprisonment without the possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant did not allege the prosecutor intentionally invited reversal at previous trials, and the record did not support such an allegation. The prosecution did not place defendant twice in jeopardy on the charge of murder-for-hire, and the trial court properly allowed the trial to proceed under the indictment that charged him with double murder. The publicity surrounding the case was extensive. However, most of it occurred during earlier trials which supported denying a change of venue. There was no indication that the method used by the trial court to question prospective jurors prejudiced defendant. Defendant was not prejudiced by the accommodations made for the sequestered jurors. There was no reason to remove any of the challenged jurors for cause. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the Batson motion. Defendant's testimony from his first trial was proper to prove his state of mind. Both the old and the new death penalty statutes clearly embodied the principle that the judge was the final sentencing authority and could override the jury's recommendation. The death sentence was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Hocker v. State


CR-00-0453


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


840 So. 2d 197; 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 99



April 26, 2002, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 21, 2002. As Corrected September 25, 2002. Released for Publication February 7, 2003.
Later proceeding at State v. Hocker, 920 So. 2d 1139, 2004 Ala. LEXIS 1177 (Ala., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Henry Circuit Court. (CC-99-124).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted on a jury verdict in the Henry Circuit Court (Alabama) of capital murder, and he was sentenced to death. His motion for a new trial was denied after a hearing, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted killing the victim during the course of a robbery. Evidence showed that the victim was viciously beaten, and would have felt pain before he died. The appellate court held that (1) defendant failed to show presumed prejudice or actual prejudice so as to justify a change of venue based on adverse publicity; (2) his Batson challenge was properly denied, as the State gave race-neutral reasons for excluding two black venire members; (3) the evidence did not support his claim that his confession was involuntary because he had been under the influence of drugs when he made it; (4) prior-crime evidence was relevant to show his motive for the murder, and this evidence's prejudicial effect did not outweigh its probative value; (5) the trial court's instruction about circumstantial evidence was a correct statement of the law; (6) death by electrocution was not unconstitutional; (7) evidence established the aggravating factors that the murder was committed during a robbery, and was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel; (8) "double counting" the commission of the murder during a robbery as an element of the capital crime and as an aggravating factor was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant of capital murder and sentencing him to death was affirmed.

Key v. State


CR-99-0220


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


891 So. 2d 353; 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 44



March 1, 2002, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 15, 2005. As Corrected April 8, 2002. As Corrected September 9, 2002. As Corrected September 25, 2002. As Corrected November 11, 2002. As Corrected April 19, 2004.
Appeal after remand at Key v. State, 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 130 (Ala. Crim. App., May 31, 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Calhoun Circuit Court. (CC-98-924).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Calhoun Circuit Court (Alabama) of capital murder. Following a sentencing hearing, the jury unanimously recommended that a death sentence be imposed. The trial court held a separate hearing, determined that the aggravating circumstances outweighed the mitigating circumstances, and sentenced defendant to death. Defendant moved for a new trial. The trial court denied the motion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to aggravated stalking of his ex-wife. The next day, defendant, in his car, chased his ex-wife and her friend while they were riding in the friend's car. Defendant caused the friend to crash her car by colliding with it. Defendant approached the crashed car and shot and wounded the friend. He shot his ex-wife five times. She died from her wounds. Defendant pleaded guilty at his trial. On appeal, the court found that the case had to be remanded for resentencing because the trial court failed to meet the requirements of Ala. Code § 13A-5-47(d) (1975) by not entering specific findings as to each aggravating circumstance, each statutory mitigating circumstance, and each nonstatutory mitigating circumstance, and failed to discuss the weight it accorded the jury's sentencing recommendation. Further, the trial court did not err by admitting evidence of the aggravated stalking conviction, permitting testimony about the victim's character, refusing to recuse itself, admitting photographs of the victim into evidence, denying defendant's motion challenging the racial makeup of the jury, and finding defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed; however, the case was remanded for amendment of the sentencing order so that the appellate court could review the findings concerning the existence or nonexistence of aggravating and mitigating circumstances upon resubmission.

OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

White v. State


CR-00-1374


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


832 So. 2d 676; 2001 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 287



November 30, 2001, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected December 24, 2001. As Corrected July 17, 2002. Released for Publication November 20, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Etowah Circuit Court. (CC-99-1024.02).



DISPOSITION: Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Etowah Circuit Court, Alabama, convicted defendant, upon his guilty plea, of trafficking in cocaine. Subsequently, the trial court determined that it did not have the authority to grant probation because the district attorney had not recommended probation. The trial court denied defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the district attorney abused his discretion in refusing to recommend probation because defendant rendered substantial assistance to law enforcement pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-12-232(b). The appellate court determined that there was a three-prong test for determining the unconstitutionality of Ala. Code § 13A-12-232(b) as applied to a defendant. The appellate court found that a plea agreement existed, but that there was a dispute as to the terms and conditions of that agreement. Because the appellate court could not determine the terms of the plea agreement, it could not determine whether the State arbitrarily or unjustifiably breached the terms of the plea agreement. Thus, the appellate court could not review the merits of defendant's claims.


OUTCOME: The appellate court remanded the case to the trial court with directions for the trial court to hold an evidentiary hearing to determine the terms of the plea agreement.

State v. K. C. L.

COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA

DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state filed a petition in the Calhoun, Alabama, Juvenile Court, alleging appellee child was in need of supervision because the child was not attending school as required by the compulsory school attendance law, Ala. Code §§ 16-28-1 through -24 (1975). The trial court declared a part of the school attendance law unconstitutional and dismissed the petition. The state appealed.

Const. art. IV, § 45, by dealing with more than one subject. The appellate court reversed the juvenile court on the authority of State v. L.N.A. and remanded the case for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed.

 

563 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Hodges v. State


CR-98-1988


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


856 So. 2d 875; 2001 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 279



October 26, 2001, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected December 24, 2001. As Corrected April 15, 2002. As Corrected As Corrected February 11, 2004. December 12, 2002.
Affirmed by Ex parte Hodges, 2003 Ala. LEXIS 84 (Ala., Mar. 14, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Lee Circuit Court. (CC-99-264).
Hodges v. State, 2001 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 40 (Ala. Crim. App., Mar. 30, 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murder during the course of a robbery in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) (1975). A jury, by eight to four vote, recommended a sentence of life imprisonment without possibility of parole. The Lee Circuit Court (Alabama) sentenced him to death by electrocution. Upon remand of the sentencing order, the trial court found the especially heinous aggravator and again resentenced defendant to death. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a woman were restaurant co-workers. Her nude body was found by a road with defendant's work nametag next to it. A participant in the crime led police to where he had disposed of defendant's bloody clothes from the crime, made a plea-agreement for a life sentence, and testified against defendant that he gave him $ 2,500 from the restaurant robbery/murder. Defendant admitted planning the robbery, but denied being present at either the robbery or murder. His aunt testified that he had admitted the murder to her. DNA evidence connected him to the murder sight. The appellate court found no prejudice to defendant from the grand jury foreperson whose role was purely ministerial. Alabama's statutory compensation scheme for court-appointed lawyers was not unconstitutional. A detective was properly excluded from the sequestration rule. Juror selection was proper and many alleged errors were harmless given that defendant exercised his peremptory strikes over veniremembers in question anyway. Defendant's motions for funds for mitigation and electrocution experts were properly denied. There was no evidence the robbery and murder were separate crimes.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence to death by electrocution were affirmed.

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected April 15, 2002. As Corrected September 6, 2002. As Corrected October 23, 2003. Released for Publication November 2, 2004.
Appeal after remand at McNabb v. State, 887 So. 2d 929, 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 33 (Ala. Crim. App., 2002)
Affirmed by Ex parte McNabb, 887 So. 2d 998, 2004 Ala. LEXIS 46 (Ala., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Montgomery Circuit Court. (CC-97-2541; CC-97-2542; and CC-97-2543).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS TO CONVICTIONS; REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS AS TO SENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of two counts of capital murder in connection with the murder of a police officer. Defendant was also convicted of two counts of attempted murder. The jury recommended that defendant be sentenced to death for his capital-murder convictions and the trial court accepted the jury's recommendation. The trial court also sentenced him to 20 years' imprisonment for each count of attempted murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that the trial court did not err in refusing to grant defendant's challenges for cause as to several prospective jurors. The copy of the booking report was certified by the custodian of inmate records at the detention facility and was properly admitted into evidence under the business records exception to the hearsay rule, Ala. R. Evid. 803(6). The log from the police department was properly admitted under the public records exception to the hearsay rule, Ala. R. Evid. 803(8). Additionally, the trial court properly instructed the jury on intent to kill and the statutory and nonstatutory mitigating circumstances. Although the trial court thoroughly addressed the statutory aggravating circumstances and statutory mitigating circumstances that it expressly found to exist, it did not make specific findings regarding the existence or nonexistence of the remainder of the statutory aggravating and mitigating circumstances in Ala. Code §§ 13A-5-49, 13A-5-51. On remand, the trial court was ordered to make specific findings regarding each statutory aggravating and statutory mitigating circumstance.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of capital murder and attempted murder; however, the appellate court remanded the case with directions as to sentencing.

Chatman v. State


CR-99-0572


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


813 So. 2d 956; 2001 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 234



September 28, 2001, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 1, 2002. As Corrected September 6, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-98-4733).



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of vehicular homicide, a violation of Ala. Code §32-5A-192(b), following his guilty plea before the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the State presented insufficient evidence to sustain his conviction. More particularly, he argued that the evidence did not establish the appropriate mens rea required by the vehicular homicide statute. The appellate court agreed and held that the indictment was fatally flawed because it did not charge a mental state based on Ala. Code § 13A-2-2(2)-(4), and therefore, the trial court never acquired jurisdiction to enter a judgment of conviction. However, the appellate court also held that the State could reindict defendant because there was no adjudication regarding the sufficiency of the evidence to support the vehicular homicide charge.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the decision of the trial court.

Stallworth v. State


CR-98-0366


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


868 So. 2d 1128; 2001 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 243



September 28, 2001, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 19, 2004. As Corrected February 14, 2002. As Corrected March 18, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Baldwin Circuit Court. (CC-98-112 & CC-98-113).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS TO CONVICTIONS; REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS AS TO SENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Baldwin Circuit Court, Alabama, convicted defendant of two counts of capital murder. The jury, by a vote of 10 to 2, recommended that defendant be sentenced to death in each case. The trial court accepted the jury's recommendation and sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found, inter alia, that: (1) there was no error in failing to order that the grand jury testimony be transcribed because defendant had made no showing that he had a particularized need for the testimony; (2) the trial judge did not err in denying defendant's motion to recuse because defendant failed to present any evidence that would require the trial judge to disqualify himself from the case or that would cast doubt on the trial judge's impartiality; (3) there was absolutely no evidence that the trial court abused its discretion in denying the motion for a change of venue because the pretrial publicity did not make it impossible for defendant to receive a fair and impartial trial; (4) the trial court did not err in consolidating the two capital indictments because both crimes were similar; and (5) the photographs, the prosecutor's comments, and defendant's confession were admissible. However, the trial court's sentencing orders were deficient for several reasons and the appellate court remanded defendant's case to the trial court with directions that the trial court comply with Ala. Code § 13A-5-47(e).


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's convictions, but remanded the case with directions as to sentencing.

568 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Poole v. State


CR-99-1200


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


846 So. 2d 370; 2001 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 173



August 31, 2001, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected December 24, 2001. As Corrected February 14, 2002. As Corrected March 1, 2002. As Corrected April 8, 2002. Released for Publication May 25, 2003. As corrected November 11, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Etowah Circuit Court. (CC-95-785.01 through .05).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED BY UNPUBLISHED MEMORANDUM IN PART *; REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.



* Note from the reporter of decisions: This case will also appear on a table of decisions without opinions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Etowah Circuit Court (Alabama) of distributing controlled substances, and the trial court enhanced his sentence under Ala. Code §§ 13A-12-250, -270, because the distribution occurred within three miles of a school and a housing project. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Any fact which enhanced defendant's sentence beyond the statutory range for the crime he was convicted of had to be submitted to the jury and proved beyond a reasonable doubt. The enhancement of defendant's sentence for committing his crime within a prescribed distance from a school and a housing project was only proved to the trial judge by a preponderance of the evidence. As a result, defendant's sentence had to be vacated. The error was not so structural as to require the vacation of defendant's conviction. There was no requirement that facts causing the possible enhancement of defendant's sentence be alleged in the indictment. The indictment's failure to include the facts did not rise to the level of a jurisdictional defect. The requirements of due process under Ala. Const. art. I, § 6 did, however, require that defendant be provided notice of the intent to seek a sentencing enhancement at a reasonable time before the facts supporting that enhancement were submitted to the jury.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was vacated, and the matter was remanded for resentencing. Defendant's conviction was affirmed in a separate, unpublished, opinion.

Centobie v. State


CR-98-2056


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


861 So. 2d 1111; 2001 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 174



August 31, 2001, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected January 30, 2003. Released for Publication January 5, 2004. As Corrected April 19, 2004.
On rehearing at, Writ of certiorari denied Ex parte Centobie, 861 So. 2d 1145, 2003 Ala. LEXIS 41 (Ala., 2003)
Rehearing denied by Centobie v. State, 2003 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 353 (Ala. Crim. App., Nov. 21, 2003)
Later proceeding at Ex parte Centobie, 2005 Ala. LEXIS 229 (Ala., Mar. 17, 2005)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Stay denied by Centobie v. Campbell, 407 F.3d 1149, 2005 U.S. App. LEXIS 7600 (11th Cir. Ala., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from St. Clair Circuit Court. (CC-98-67).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion for a change of venue, which the St. Clair Circuit Court, Alabama, granted to the Elmore County Circuit Court. A jury for the trial court found defendant guilty of capital murder for intentionally causing the death of a police officer while he was on duty and recommended that he be sentenced to death. The trial court accepted the jury's recommendation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A Federal Bureau of Investigation agent informed defendant of his Miranda rights. Defendant understood his rights and agreed to speak with the agent and an investigator for the Alabama Bureau of Investigation. Defendant knowingly and voluntarily signed a form waiving his rights. Thus, the appellate court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress his confession. The appellate court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting evidence of uncharged collateral robberies that occurred after defendant's escape from the county jail. Also, the trial court did not err in admitting the photographs of the victim's body into evidence because the photographs were used to corroborate the medical examiner's testimony. Additionally, the trial court properly weighed the mitigating and aggravating circumstances when determining defendant's sentence. Finally, the trial court compared defendant's sentence to sentences imposed in similar cases and found that defendant's sentence was not disproportionate or excessive. Thus, defendant's conviction and sentence of death were proper.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

570 of 745 DOCUMENTS


State v. L.N.A.


CR-00-1554


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


811 So. 2d 637; 2001 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 180



August 31, 2001, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 22, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Morgan Juvenile Court. (JU-98-593.03).



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A child in need of supervision petition was filed against the appellee student based on a charge of truancy for violating the compulsory school attendance law. On its own motion, before it conducted a hearing on the petition, the Morgan County Juvenile Court (Alabama) entered an order, finding that 1999 Ala. Acts 99-705 was unconstitutional. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the juvenile court erroneously concluded that 1999 Ala. Act 99-705 violated Ala. Const. art. IV, § 45 (1901). The State specifically contended that Ala. Code §16-28-16 (amended 2000) did not amend or extend Ala. Code § 16-28-3. Section 16-28-3 specified which children were required by law to attend school. In contrast, § 16-28-16 provided that, with certain listed exceptions, each child who was enrolled in a public school, whether or not that child was required by law to enroll, was subject to attendance and truancy provisions. Contrary to the juvenile court's finding, the amendment to § 16-28-16, did not amend or extend the provisions of Ala. Code §16-28-3. Furthermore, when it amended § 16-28-16, the Alabama legislature complied with the requirements of Ala. Const. art. IV, § 45, because it reenacted and published at length that entire section. The juvenile court erroneously concluded that the act violated the state constitution and erroneously dismissed the petition.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the juvenile court's judgment.

 

571 of 745 DOCUMENTS


McGriff v. State


CR-97-0179


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


908 So. 2d 961; 2001 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 181



August 31, 2001, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As corrected.
Rehearing denied by McGriff v. State, 2001 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 3618 (Ala. Crim. App., Nov. 21, 2001)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Houston Circuit Court. (CC-97-267).
McGriff v. State, 908 So. 2d 961, 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 121 (Ala. Crim. App., 2000)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of capital murder in the Houston Circuit Court (Alabama) and was sentenced to death. The matter was remanded to the trial court for findings regarding its consideration of mitigating factors, under Ala. Code § 13A-5-47(d), and was returned to the appellate court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted under Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(18), which authorized the death penalty for an intentional murder committed by firing a weapon from a vehicle. The statute did not disproportionately or arbitrarily authorize the death penalty. The trial court did not have to state the weight given to the jury's sentencing recommendation. The only objectionable statement the prosecutor made was that told the jurors they were making a sentencing recommendation, and they should not let the defense "put a guilt trip" on them. The comment was not objected to at trial, and its allowance was not plain error. The prosecutor's other challenged comments were not improper. The jury instructions at sentencing, viewed as a whole, correctly stated the law. The trial court did not have to instruct the jury on mitigating circumstances not relied on at sentencing. While the trial court had to consider mitigating factors offered by defendant, it was not required to find that they were mitigating. The trial court's findings made in imposing the death sentence were supported by the record, and the sentence was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

572 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Wilson v. State


CR-97-1494


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


830 So. 2d 765; 2001 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 182



August 31, 2001, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Fourth Correction February 19, 2003. Third Correction January 30, 2003. Second Correction July 27, 2002. Released for Publication October 25, 2002. Rehearing Denied October 26, 2001. As Corrected December 17, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-97-1728; -1729) (CC-97-1728.60; -1729.60).



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) of distribution of a controlled substance and trafficking in morphine. She was given a mandatory sentence of life imprisonment without parole on the trafficking charge. Defendant's appeal was stayed when she filed an Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 petition challenging the mandatory sentence. The trial court denied the petition and the case was resubmitted for appellate review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who testified she was addicted to drugs, sold prescription drugs to an undercover officer. When the officer asked her whether she could obtain any other substances, she obtained a bottle of liquid morphine from a neighbor. The appellate court first determined that the issue of whether the life sentence amounted to cruel and unusual punishment had been preserved for review because the appellate court had sanctioned the procedural sequence. The appellate court then found that it was required to apply a narrow proportionality analysis, which required an initial determination that the sentence was grossly disproportionate to the crime. Defendant's life sentence without parole was grossly disproportionate given that it was her first offense and that Ala. Code § 13A-12-231 was meant to punish "drug barons" who habitually dealt large quantities of drugs. As defendant was the only noncapital offender with no prior felony convictions who was serving a life sentence without parole in an Alabama prison, and she would have received a much more lenient sentence in many other jurisdictions, the mandatory sentence was unconstitutional as applied to defendant.


OUTCOME: The life sentence was reversed and remanded.

Johnson v. State


CR-98-0391


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


823 So. 2d 1; 2001 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 108



June 29, 2001, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 17, 2001. Writ of certiorari denied: Johnson v. Alabama, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 3713 (U.S. May 20, 2002). Released for Publication August 9, 2002.
Writ of certiorari denied Ex parte Johnson, 823 So. 2d 57, 2001 Ala. LEXIS 450 (Ala., 2001)
Writ of certiorari denied Johnson v. Alabama, 535 U.S. 1085, 122 S. Ct. 1978, 152 L. Ed. 2d 1035, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 3713 (2002)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Johnson v. State, 2007 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 178 (Ala. Crim. App., Sept. 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-96-386).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) entered a final judgment of conviction and sentence of death after a jury convicted defendant of the murder of a deputy sheriff while the deputy was on duty or because of the deputy's official or job-related act or performance, a capital offense pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(5). Defendant appealed his conviction and death sentence.


OVERVIEW: A deputy sheriff was moonlighting as a hotel security guard. He heard a disturbance and went to investigate suspected criminal activity. He was shot twice and died. Criminal defendant was soon taken into custody. Weeks later, while in prison, another inmate helped defendant make several calls. The calls were initially placed to a young woman who allowed her three-way calling mechanism to be used so inmates could speak with several different people. The daughter consented to having her mother listen in on the calls and the mother took notes. Defendant talked on the phone about shooting the deputy in the head. Defendant was convicted of murdering a law enforcement officer, a capital offense under Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(5) and the case facts. After he was sentenced to death, the appellate court found the deputy was on duty, which was one way of showing the statute applied, as he was investigating criminal activity. It also found the mother was not illegally eavesdropping and her notes could be admitted as present sense impressions. It further found ineffective assistance of counsel was not shown, the evidence supported the conviction, and the death sentence was proper.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. State could "death-qualify" jury, jury selection was proper and State did not misuse peremptory strikes, arguments unsupported by the record could not be reviewed, evidence was properly admitted including evidence of telephone calls defendant made from jail, evidence supported defendant's conviction, State's closing argument was proper, ineffective assistance of counsel was not shown, and sentencing was proper.

Dorsey v. State


CR-97-1522


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


881 So. 2d 460; 2001 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 91



May 25, 2001, Released


NOTICE:

 [**1] [EDITOR'S NOTE: PART 1 OF 2. THIS DOCUMENT HAS BEEN SPLIT INTO MULTIPLE PARTS ON LEXIS TO ACCOMMODATE ITS LARGE SIZE. EACH PART CONTAINS THE SAME LEXIS CITE.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 1, 2002. As Corrected January 30, 2003. Released for Publication August 17, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Conecuh Circuit Court. (CC-97-037).



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Conecuh Circuit Court, Alabama, convicted appellant of two counts of felony murder, robbery, and one count of capital murder. The trial court chose not to follow the jury's recommendation and sentenced appellant to death for the capital murder charge.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that (1) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying appellant's motion to depose the government's witnesses; (2) appellant was not entitled to discovery of witness's prior convictions or his institutional records; (3) the trial court did not err in limiting the scope of the voir dire examination of the jury venire; (4) the jurors expressed views that would affect their impartiality as a juror; thus, the strikes for cause were proper; (5) the trial court did not err in excluding testimony that others committed the murders; (6) while the trial court did not condone prosecutor's rebuttal arguments, there was no reversible error; (7) appellant's convictions for felony murder were affirmed, however, his convictions for robbery were to be vacated; and (8) there was sufficient evidence to convict appellant. However, the case was remanded to correct the trial court's sentencing order to specifically designate the evidence it found to present nonstatutory mitigating circumstances and why it did not follow jury's recommendation regarding life imprisonment and instead imposed a death sentence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court remanded the case to the trial court with directions.
