577 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Baker v. State


CR-00-0155


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


819 So. 2d 87; 2001 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 97



May 25, 2001, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 10, 2001. Released for Publication May 3, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Morgan Circuit Court. (CC-97-1144.60).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Morgan Circuit Court, Alabama, denying his petition for postconviction relief, filed pursuant to Ala. R. Crim. P. 32, attacking his conviction for distributing cocaine. The conviction had been affirmed on direct appeal.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed a pro se brief in which he reasserted two of the claims raised in his Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 postconviction relief petition, namely (1) that the trial court was without jurisdiction to render judgment or to impose sentence because his conviction was obtained in violation of the prohibition against double jeopardy; and (2) he was unconstitutionally convicted of an offense not charged in the indictment. Appellant's double jeopardy claim was based on his contention that he could not be prosecuted criminally for an offense as to which he had been previously subjected to civil asset forfeiture. The reviewing court found no error harmful to appellant's substantial rights. The court concluded that appellant's double jeopardy claim was precluded by Rule 32 because it could have been raised at trial and on appeal, but was not. In addition, appellant's second claim was barred by Rule 32 because the claim, which involved the variance between the indictment and the trial court's oral charge to the jury, could have been, but was not, raised at trial and on direct appeal. A misdescription of an element of the offense did not affect the trial court's jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Appellant's collateral challenge to his drug conviction, based upon double jeopardy implications of an asset forfeiture action, could not be raised for the first time in his postconviction petition. The variance between the indictment and oral charge was a misdescription of the elements of the offense and thus did not implicate trial court's jurisdiction. Appellant's failure to object at trial to waived this claim.

Arthur v. State


CR-00-1393


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


820 So. 2d 886; 2001 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 57



April 25, 2001, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected. Released for Publication July 11, 2002. Rehearing Denied July 27, 2001. As Corrected September 25, 2002.
Writ of certiorari denied Arthur v. Alabama, 535 U.S. 1053, 122 S. Ct. 1909, 152 L. Ed. 2d 819, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 3233 (2002)
Later proceeding at Ex parte Arthur, 2007 Ala. LEXIS 513 (Ala., June 22, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-87-577.60).
Ex parte Arthur, 821 So. 2d 251, 2001 Ala. LEXIS 486 (Ala., 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's third trial and conviction of capital murder and sentence of death, in the Jefferson County Circuit Court (Alabama), he sought post-conviction relief under Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. Ala. R. Crim. P. 32, providing for petitions for postconviction relief, provided, in Ala. R. Crim. P. 32.2(c), that a petition for postconviction relief on constitutional grounds or alleging failure to appeal within the prescribed time, had to be filed within two years after the issuance of the certificate of judgment. Defendant filed a petition for postconviction relief nearly three years after issuance of the certificate of judgment. The limitations provision was mandatory and jurisdictional, and there were no exceptions to its application. It was not a prohibited suspension of the writ of habeas corpus under 28 U.S.C.S. § 2244 because it was a procedural mechanism which the state had no obligation to provide and was subject to reasonable restriction. Defendant's attempt to couch his complaint as a jurisdictional issue not subject to any statute of limitations was without merit.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of defendant's petition for postconviction relief, because it was filed outside the two-year statute of limitations, was affirmed because there were no exceptions to that limitations period for defendant's constitutional claims.

State v. Maddox


CR-00-0690


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


828 So. 2d 946; 2001 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 21



March 2, 2001, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Second Correction January 30, 2003. Later proceeding: State v. Maddox, 2002 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 41 (Ala. Crim. App. Mar. 1, 2002). As Corrected. Released for Publication September 26, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Mobile Circuit Court. (CC-2000-2581). TRIAL JUDGE: Herman Y. Thomas.



DISPOSITION: PETITION GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of mandamus directing the Mobile Circuit Court (Alabama) to vacate its order dismissing theft charges against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the petition for writ of mandamus was untimely. The court granted the petition for writ of mandamus, and ordered the lower court to reinstate the indictment. Petitioner filed the petition 35 days after the lower court dismissed the charges against defendant; thus, the petition was filed within a presumptively reasonable time. Because defendant did not respond to the allegations in the petition, the court considered the allegations to be true. Defendant exerted unauthorized control over moneys that he received from an individual with whom defendant had contracted. The court found, however, that it was for a jury to decide whether defendant had the intent to deprive the individual of the moneys.


OUTCOME: Petition for writ of mandamus was granted. Petition was presumptively timely. Defendant exercised unauthorized control over moneys, but it was for jury to determine if defendant had requisite intent to be found guilty.

Ray v. State


CR-99-0135


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


809 So. 2d 875; 2001 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 6



January 12, 2001, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 21, 2002. As Corrected July 1, 2002.
Writ of certiorari denied Ex parte Ray, 809 So. 2d 891, 2001 Ala. LEXIS 294 (Ala., 2001)
Writ of certiorari denied Ray v. Alabama, 534 U.S. 1142, 122 S. Ct. 1096, 151 L. Ed. 2d 993, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 1008 (2002)
Post-conviction relief denied at Ray v. State, 80 So. 3d 965, 2011 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 6 (Ala. Crim. App., 2011)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Ray v. Thomas, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 138780 (S.D. Ala., Sept. 26, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Dallas Circuit Court. (CC-97-375). TRIAL JUDGE: Thomas R. Jones.
Ray v. State, 810 So. 2d 805, 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1188 (Ala. Crim. App., 2000)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction, in the Dallas Circuit Court (Alabama), of capital murder committed during first degree rape, in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(3) (1975), and of capital murder committed during first degree robbery, in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) (1975), and his death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and an accomplice raped, robbed, and murdered a 15 year-old girl. Defendant appealed his convictions of capital murder during first degree rape and during first degree robbery, and his electrocution sentence. Defendant's conviction of another capital crime before sentencing was admissible at that hearing. There was no comment on defendant's failure to testify, nor did the prosecutor incorrectly state the jury's sentencing role. Defendant waived arraignment on a second indictment substituted for the original. Defendant was not entitled to challenge jury panel members for cause who knew the victim, after they stated they could be fair and impartial. Death by electrocution was not cruel or unusual. Defendant's custodial statements to police were either voluntary or spontaneous, and, therefore, admissible. Relevant victim photographs were admissible, even if they inflamed the jury. Defendant's accomplice's testimony was corroborated, as required by Ala. Code § 12-22-222 (1975), by defendant's confession and crime scene evidence. The evidence was sufficient. Defendant's intent could be inferred from his use of a deadly weapon. The conviction and sentence were proper.


OUTCOME: The trial court was affirmed because the evidence received at trial and sentencing was admissible; there was no prosecutorial misconduct; arraignment on a second indictment was waived; under the circumstances, challenges for cause to jury panel members were properly denied; electrocution was not cruel or unusual; and defendant's intent could be inferred from use of a deadly weapon.

Smith v. State


CR-97-0069


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


908 So. 2d 273; 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 274



December 22, 2000, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended. 02-23-2001: REHEARING DENIED; NO OPINION. cert pending (3-13-01). As Corrected July 1, 2002.
Rehearing denied by Smith v. State, 2001 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 3620 (Ala. Crim. App., Feb. 23, 2001)
Writ of certiorari quashed Ex parte Smith, 908 So. 2d 302, 2005 Ala. LEXIS 43 (Ala., 2005)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Smith v. Alabama, 546 U.S. 928, 126 S. Ct. 148, 163 L. Ed. 2d 277, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 7200 (2005)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Smith v. State, 2010 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 131 (Ala. Crim. App., Dec. 17, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-89-1149.80). TRIAL JUDGE: N. Pride Tompkins.
Smith v. State, 620 So. 2d 732, 1992 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 1086 (Ala. Crim. App., 1992)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the jury in the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) of murder for a pecuniary or other valuable consideration under Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(7) (1975). The jury recommended that defendant be sentenced to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole. The trial court, pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-5-47(e) (1975), overrode the jury's recommendation and sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was hired by a minister to murder the minister's wife. Defendant and one other man entered the minister's home and beat and stabbed the woman to death. A woman telephoned the police and anonymously identified the murderers and told the police that defendant had a videocassette recorder stolen from the minister's home. The police obtained a warrant to search defendant's home for the videocassette recorder and arrested him when the stolen property was found. Defendant then signed a written confession. On appeal, the court found (1) defendant's constitutional rights were not violated by the prosecutors refusal to plea bargain; (2) the trial court did not err in refusing to strike for cause a juror who stated the death penalty should be used more often, admitting photos of the victim into evidence, or balancing the aggravating and mitigating factors in sentencing defendant to death; (3) the police did not have to discover and notify defendant of the identity of the informant and her private search was not unconstitutional; (5) the confession was admissible and the jury could examine it during deliberations; and (6) evidence of the minister's suicide was admissible.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence of death were affirmed.

 

582 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


CR-97-1258


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


213 So. 3d 108; 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 3289



December 22, 2000, Released


NOTICE:

 [**1] THIS OPINION IS SUBJECT TO CORRECTION OR REVISION BEFORE PUBLICATION IN THE OFFICIAL REPORTER.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Houston Circuit Court. (CC-97-270).



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS TO CONVICTION; REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS AS TO SENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant fatally shot three persons, and attempted to kill a fourth, in connection with a drug deal. He was convicted of the capital offense of murder under Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(10), and the Houston Circuit Court (Alabama) sentenced him to death. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a drug dealer with a full scale IQ of 72, confessed to the shootings. At trial, he claimed he did not intend to kill the victims, but "snapped" because, inter alia, he smoked crack and drank alcohol and was under duress from another drug dealer. The appellate court held that each alleged error in the guilt and jury-sentencing phase was without merit or was harmless. The trial court's findings that the confession was voluntary and that defendant was competent to stand trial were supported by the record. Though the prosecutor improperly commented on his own credibility and, in effect, gave his personal opinion of defendant's guilt, this was not plain error. But the trial court erred by rejecting Ala. Code § 13A-5-51(6) (substantially impaired capacity) as a mitigating circumstance solely on its finding that defendant intended to kill the victims, as intent to kill and substantially impaired capacity were not mutually exclusive. While the trial court noted that there were "some" statutory mitigating circumstances, it addressed only § 13A-5-51(6); its failure to make specific written findings as to the existence vel non of each mitigating circumstance required remand.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed, and the case was remanded to the trial court for that court's review and/or reconsideration of its sentence, and for its entry of a new sentencing order. The trial court was instructed not to exclude evidence regarding one of defendant's relatives to the extent it was probative of how defendant's life had been affected by his experiences with and deficiencies of his family members.

Reeves v. State


CR-98-0777


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


807 So. 2d 18; 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 175



October 27, 2000, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 27, 2001. As Amended November 17, 2000. Released for Publication January 4, 2002. As Corrected April 8, 2002.
Writ of certiorari denied Reeves v. Alabama, 534 U.S. 1026, 122 S. Ct. 558, 151 L. Ed. 2d 433, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 10444 (2001)
Post-conviction relief denied at Reeves v. State, 2016 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 37 (Ala. Crim. App., June 10, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Dallas Circuit Court. (CC-97-31). TRIAL JUDGE: Thomas R. Jones.



DISPOSITION: APPLICATION FOR REHEARING DENIED; OPINION OF AUGUST 25, 2000, WITHDRAWN; OPINION SUBSTITUTED; AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction, in the Dallas Circuit Court (Alabama), of murder made capital because it was committed during the course of a robbery in the first degree, alleging numerous constitutional and procedural errors. The appellate court reviewed the defendant's sentence in accordance with Ala. Code § 13A-5-51 (1975).


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of capital murder, Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) (1975), for the death of a man which occurred in the course of a robbery. In a bifurcated trial, the jury recommended the death sentence. Pursuant to its review under Ala. R. App. P. 45A, the appellate court reviewed all of defendant's claimed errors, whether objected to or not at the trial level, including jury selection and alleged prosecutorial misconduct, and found no error that mandated reversal. Specifically, the appellate court held that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress evidence found in defendant's bedroom because defendant's mother clearly had the authority to consent to the search of her home. The appellate court further held that the trial court neither abused its discretion in limiting cross-examination of the State's witness nor in refusing defendant's requested jury instructions on complicity. Last, under its direct review of death penalty sentences, Ala. Code § 13A-5-51 (1975), the appellate court found that the sentence was neither excessive nor disproportionate to the penalty imposed.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed. The trial court did not err in denying motion to suppress evidence found after defendant's mother consented to a search and defendant was arrested. After carefully reviewing the record, the appellate court concluded that the findings and conclusions of the trial court were amply supported by the evidence and that death was the appropriate sentence.

 

584 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Hooks v. State


CR-99-2212


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


822 So. 2d 476; 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 138



October 6, 2000, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As corrected. Released for Publication July 24, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Montgomery Circuit Court (CC-85-588.60). William A. Shashy, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: PETITION GRANTED IN PART; DENIED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prosecutor sought review by mandamus of the order of the Montgomery Circuit Court (Alabama) directing post-conviction discovery in a death penalty case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sentenced to death filed a petition for postconviction relief, followed by a request for production, seeking materials maintained by the prison and state department of forensic sciences regarding executions since 1976, as well as prosecutor's records regarding defendant's criminal and drug-related offenses. The trial court granted the request for production, and the state sought review by way of mandamus. Good cause was the appropriate standard by which to judge postconviction discovery motions, but the movant had to allege facts which would entitle him to relief. Request for production from prison and forensic sciences department should not have been granted because it related to defendant's claim that death by electrocution was cruel and unusual punishment, which was procedurally barred because it could have been raised at trial or on appeal. A procedurally barred claim did not entitle a movant for discovery to relief. Defendant's claim that his trial counsel was ineffective in failing to reasonably investigate his background established good cause for discovery because it presented the issue of possible mitigating evidence that could have been presented to the jury.


OUTCOME: Petition for mandamus was granted as to postconviction discovery order as it applied to state prison and department of forensic sciences because defendant did not have good cause for this request, as it related to a claim which was procedurally barred, but was denied as to prosecutor because defendant did have good cause.

Wash. v. State


CR-97-0055


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


818 So. 2d 411; 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 120



September 29, 2000, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended November 17, 2000. As Corrected September 25, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court (CC-95-5653 and 95-5654).

Original Opinion of August 14, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 149.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT ON TRIAL ON REMAND AFFIRMED; CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES FOR TRAFFICKING IN COCAINE, DISTRIBUTING A CONTROLLED SUBSTANCE, AND FAILING TO AFFIX TAX STAMPS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment from the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama), convicting and sentencing him for distribution of a controlled substance, trafficking in cocaine, and two counts of failure to affix tax stamps.


OVERVIEW: The appellant was charged with, and convicted of, distribution of a controlled substance, trafficking in cocaine, and two counts of failure to affix tax stamps. Appellant challenged the convictions. This appeal addressed both the trial on remand as to whether the actions of the prosecutor were meant to provoke a mistrial and the trial that resulted in the appellant's convictions. There was no evidence that the prosecutor intended to prejudice the appellant or to provoke a mistrial. As to the appellant's attack on his convictions, persons who traffic in mixtures of cocaine and marijuana were treated similarly; therefore equal protection of the laws was not violated. The appellant's requested instruction that, with regard to the trafficking case, the appellant must have had knowledge that the amount of cocaine being sold exceeded 28 grams, was not a correct statement of the law. The trial court properly denied the appellant's motion for a judgment of acquittal. The judgment of the trial court on remand, holding that the prosecutor's misconduct was not intended to provoke a mistrial, was affirmed. The appellant's convictions and sentences were likewise affirmed.


OUTCOME: Convictions and sentences were affirmed, as well as judgment of the trial court that prosecutor's conduct was not intended to provoke a mistrial. Drug trafficking statute did not violate the equal protection clause, appellant's requested jury instruction was not a correct statement of the law, and evidence was sufficient to sustain appellant's convictions.

Cayson v. State


CR-99-1577


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


778 So. 2d 261; 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 249



August 25, 2000, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 23, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Escambia Circuit Court. (CV-2000-2.60). TRIAL JUDGE: Joseph B. Brogden.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the summary denial of his petition for a writ of habeas corpus in the Escambia Circuit Court, Alabama, based upon his assertion that the trial court did not have jurisdiction over him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in Montgomery Circuit Court of trafficking in cocaine and was sentenced as a habitual felony offender to life in prison without parole. Defendant filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus in Escambia Circuit Court, claiming that the trial court did not have jurisdiction over him. Escambia Circuit Court summarily denied the petition. On appeal from the denial, the court noted that defendant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus should have been treated as an Ala. R. Crim. P. 32 petition because the claims made in the petition challenged his conviction. The court then held that the circuit court in which the petition was filed, Escambia, did not have jurisdiction to dispose of the petition, and reversed and remanded the case to that circuit court with directions to transfer the petition to the Montgomery Circuit Court, which could address defendant's issues, which were cognizable in a Rule 32 petition.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the cause with directions that the circuit court transfer the petition to the circuit court of original jurisdiction, in which defendant was convicted, which would have had proper jurisdiction over what was not actually a habeas petition but rather an improperly labeled rule 32 petition.

CASE SUMMARY:

 [**1] [EDITOR'S NOTE: PART 2 OF 3. THIS DOCUMENT HAS BEEN SPLIT INTO MULTIPLE PARTS ON LEXIS TO ACCOMMODATE ITS LARGE SIZE. EACH PART CONTAINS THE SAME LEXIS CITE.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected December 24, 2001. As Amended October 16, 2000. As Corrected October 17, 2002.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) of four counts of capital murder for two deaths. He further appealed his death sentence and the denial of his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of four counts of capital murder for the deaths of his wife and her grandson; he was sentenced to death. Defendant filed a motion for a new trial, which was denied. There were numerous issues raised on appeal, including: venue, voir dire, the prosecution's closing arguments, jury instructions, Brady materials, discovery, victim and autopsy photographs, Miranda warnings, deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA) evidence and chain of custody, expert testimony, due process, double jeopardy, and lesser-included offense instructions. OUTCOME: Conviction was affirmed. Plain error standard was used to review assignments of error for which no timely objections were made. The case was remanded for the trial court to make written findings of each aggravating and mitigating factor and to enter a new sentencing order. Aggravating factors of prior violent murder conviction, murder during kidnapping, and current imprisonment were proved.

 

589 of 745 DOCUMENTS


State v. S.L.S.


CR-99-0600


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


777 So. 2d 318; 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 217



June 30, 2000, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 17, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Montgomery Juvenile Court. (JU-96-1161.04 and JU-96-1161.05). TRIAL JUDGE: W. Mark Anderson.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State appealed from the judgment of the Montgomery Juvenile Court (Alabama), which granted appellee's motion to suppress evidence seized from the appellee after an arrest.


OVERVIEW: When asked by a police officer, appellee gave a false age. When asked for identification, appellee admitted to being 16. Appellee was arrested under Montgomery, Ala., Municipal Code § 29-18 for making a false statement to police. During a search of appellee's purse, the officer discovered marijuana. Appellee was arrested and charged with second-degree possession of marijuana under Ala. Code § 13A-12-214 (1975). Appellee moved to suppress the evidence discovered in her purse and the district court granted the motion on the ground that the city ordinance was unconstitutional. Appellant State appealed and judgment was reversed and remanded. The city ordinance was not inconsistent with the state law and the state law did not contain any exclusivity provisions. Furthermore, the city ordinance merely expanded upon the statute by providing that making any false statement in a matter within the jurisdiction of a city department or agency was an offense. Accordingly, the juvenile court improperly granted the appellee's motion to suppress. Appellee was lawfully arrested, and the warrantless search of her purse was a valid search incident to her arrest.


OUTCOME: Judgment was reversed and remanded. The juvenile court improperly granted appellee's motion to suppress. The city ordinance was not inconsistent with state law because the state law did not contain any exclusivity provisions. Because the ordinance merely enlarged the provisions of the state law and did not prohibit an activity that the state law specifically allowed, it was not inconsistent with the state law.

Snavely v. City of Huntsville


CR-99-0802


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


785 So. 2d 1162; 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 223



June 30, 2000, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 18, 2000. Released for Publication May 22, 2001. As Corrected September 4, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Madison Circuit Court. (CC-98-0236; 98-0237; and 98-0238). TRIAL JUDGE: Bruce E. Williams.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Madison Circuit Court (Alabama) convicting him of driving without a proper license plate, driving while his license was revoked, and failing to wear a properly fastened seat belt. He was ordered to pay fines and was placed on probation for one year.


OVERVIEW: A police officer stopped appellant for driving without a proper license plate. Appellant was not wearing a seatbelt when stopped. Additionally, appellant handed the officer a homemade identification card with his name and identification number. The officer discovered appellant had never had a valid driver's license in Alabama. Appellant was convicted of several offenses related the police stop. Judgment was reversed in part. As appellant had never obtained a valid driver's license in Alabama, he was not properly charged with driving while his license was revoked. The court also concluded that the State's requirement that appellant, and every other vehicle owner, renew or obtain a driver's license and register his vehicle placed no impermissible restrictions on appellant's constitutional right to travel. Computer printout of appellant's driving history was properly admitted into evidence under the public records exception to the hearsay rule.


OUTCOME: Judgment of was affirmed as to the convictions for driving without a proper license plate and for failing to wear a properly fastened seat belt. Judgment was reversed as to the conviction for driving with a revoked license, as appellant had never obtained a valid driver's license in Alabama.

Ferguson v. State


CR-97-2524


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


814 So. 2d 925; 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 224

Affirmed by Ex parte Ferguson, 814 So. 2d 970, 2001 Ala. LEXIS 243 (Ala., 2001)

Maxwell v. State, 828 So. 2d 347, 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 141 (Ala. Crim. App., 2000)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his convictions and death sentence, entered by the Mobile Circuit Court (Alabama), where he was convicted of two counts of capital murder because the killings occurred during a first-degree robbery, one count of capital murder because the killings involved the murder of two or more persons by one act or pursuant to one scheme or course of conduct, and one count of capital murder as one victim was less than age 14.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with four counts of capital murder for killing a man and his 11-year old son. Two counts of capital murder were charged because the killings occurred during a first-degree robbery, one capital murder count was lodged since the killings involved the murder of two or more persons by one act or pursuant to one scheme or course of conduct, and one count of capital murder was because one of the victims was less than 14 years old. Appellant and four codefendants planned to steal some vehicles. A man and his 11-year old son with a vehicle were parked at a boat landing. None of the allegations raised regarding jury issues, admission of evidence, prosecutorial misconduct, sufficiency of evidence, sentencing, and propriety of the death penalty warranted reversal of the convictions or death sentence.


OUTCOME: Judgments and sentences affirmed because none of the multiple issues appellant raised on appeal demonstrated either plain error or a defect in the proceedings occurred in either the guilt or sentencing phases of his trial. The trial court's findings and conclusions were amply supported by the evidence. No evidence existed the sentence was the result of passion, prejudice, or other arbitrary factor, and the death sentence was appropriate.

 

592 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Thomas v. State


CR-96-0876


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


824 So. 2d 1; 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 216



June 30, 2000, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appeal from Mobile Circuit Court. (CC-96-1040). TRIAL JUDGE: Edward B. McDermott.

Original Opinion of December 30, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 298.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Mobile Circuit Court (Alabama) sentencing him to death for the murder of the victim during a rape and a burglary.


OVERVIEW: The jury unanimously recommended death for appellant's murder-rape conviction. The trial court subsequently sentenced appellant to death. The trial court did not give any instructions informing the jury as to the burdens of proof for the aggravating circumstances evidence. The jury's consideration of any aggravating circumstance, besides those established during the guilt/innocence phase was invalid because it was not guided by sufficient instruction, i.e., an instruction that the prosecution had to convince each juror beyond a reasonable doubt as to the existence of any aggravating circumstance. Also, as a matter of state law, appellant was entitled to appropriate instructions on mitigating circumstances. Taking all the instructional errors cumulatively, the appellate court was constrained to find that the jury was without sufficient guidance to make a proper determination of the presence or absence of any proposed aggravating circumstance or of any offered mitigating circumstance. Thus, the court remanded appellant's case for a sentencing hearing before a properly instructed jury.


OUTCOME: Case remanded for resentencing; appellant was sentenced to death for his murder-rape conviction. Jury charge on aggravating and mitigating circumstances did not inform the jury regarding the proper burdens of proof. Thus, jury could not make a proper determination regarding aggravating or mitigating circumstances and the sentence was improper.

Hutchins v. City of Alexander City


CR-99-0139


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


822 So. 2d 459; 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 65



April 28, 2000, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April 26, 2002. Released for Publication July 24, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from Tallapoosa Circuit Court. (CC-97-123 and -124). TRIAL JUDGE: Philip Dale Segrest.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS TO CONVICTIONS AND AS TO SENTENCE FOR RESISTING ARREST; REVERSED AS TO SENTENCE FOR DISORDERLY CONDUCT; AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS. * 



* Note from the reporter of decisions: On June 30, 2000, on return to remand, the Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed, without opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of her convictions and sentences for disorderly conduct in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-11-7 (1975) and resisting arrest in violation of Ala. Code § 13A-10-41, in the Tallapoosa Circuit Court (Alabama).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was sentenced to six months' imprisonment, and the sentences were to run concurrently. Because the maximum sentence for a Class C misdemeanor such as disorderly conduct was three months under Ala. Code § 13A-5-7(a)(3), the case was remanded for resentencing on that charge. Appellant argued that she did not intend to cause "public inconvenience, annoyance, or alarm," that she did not use obscene language, and that a prima facie case was not proven. The State's witnesses provided sufficient evidence of those factors and her "unreasonable noise" to submit the case to the jury. Evidence appellant proffered concerning the reasons for her behavior at the police station were properly excluded as not relevant under Ala. R. Evid. 403. Her argument that the disorderly conduct statute, Ala. Code § 13A-11-7, violated U.S. Const. amend. I was not raised at trial and was therefore waived.


OUTCOME: Appellant's convictions were affirmed because she did not raise her free speech arguments at trial, the jury's holdings were credible, and the evidence defendant proffered concerning the reasons for her behavior at the police station was cumulative, hearsay, and did not establish a complete defense. Remanded for resentencing.

 

594 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Harris v. State


CR-98-2452


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


794 So. 2d 1214; 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 85



April 28, 2000, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected July 26, 2000. The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published August 15, 2001. As Corrected December 24, 2001. Third correction.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Morgan Circuit Court. (CC-98-424). TRIAL JUDGE: Steven E. Haddock.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS. * 



* Note from the reporter of decisions: On June 23, 2000, on return to remand, the Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed, without opinion. On September 15, 2000, that court denied rehearing, without opinion. On March 23, 2001, the Supreme Court denied certiorari review, without opinion (1000015).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed his convictions of cocaine possession and distribution in the Morgan Circuit Court (Alabama), the imposition of a sentence enhancement for distribution within three miles of a school or housing project, and denial of his defense of entrapment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried by a jury and found guilty of several counts of drug distribution. He was sentenced to consecutive 10 year terms based on enhancements under Ala. Code §§ 13A-12-250 & 13A-12-270 (1975) for selling drugs within three miles of a school or housing project. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence, arguing he should not have been denied the opportunity to present an entrapment defense, the State did not prove the sales occurred within three miles of a school or housing project, and the enhancement violated his constitutional rights. The court found defendant was given multiple opportunities to present evidence that he was not disposed to committing the crime before being approached by police and failed to do so. Proximity was proved by sufficient evidence. Defendant was granted actual notice the enhancements were being sought and he waived any constitutional objections to attack the constitutionality of his sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction, finding the entrapment defense was properly excluded where the evidence did not show defendant had no predisposition to do the crime before being approached by police; While the sentence was not unconstitutional, the court remanded for a determination of whether the sentences should run concurrently.

 

595 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


CR-98-1688


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


820 So. 2d 842; 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 86



April 28, 2000, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 16, 2000. As Amended June 22, 2000. As Corrected August 21, 2000. As Corrected October 2, 2000. Rehearing Denied November 2, 2001. Released for Publication July 11, 2002. As Corrected October 17, 2002. As Corrected September 6, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Walker Circuit Court. (CC-1999-18). TRIAL JUDGE: James C. Brotherton.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant felon appealed from the judgment of the Walker Circuit Court (Alabama) convicting appellant of murder during the course of a robbery, a capital offense pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) (1975), on the jury's recommendation, and sentencing appellant to death by electrocution.


OVERVIEW: Appellant felon shot and killed a gas station attendant during the course of a robbery, having planned the felony several weeks in advance. Appellant was convicted of the capital offense of murder during the course of a robbery pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-5-40(a)(2) (1975) and sentenced to death. Appellant challenged both the conviction and the sentence, alleging 20 assignments of error. As required by Ala. Code § 13A-5-53, the court addressed the propriety of appellant's conviction and sentence to death by electrocution. The court affirmed appellant's conviction of capital murder and sentence to death. The grand jury had jurisdiction to issue the second indictment. Because appellant did not consent to the amended indictment, the proper procedure was followed in sending the case back to the grand jury to issue a new, second indictment. Appellant's challenges for cause of potential jurors were properly denied; the jurors demonstrated that they could adhere to the law as instructed. Appellant's sentence did not constitute cruel or unusual punishment; the aggravating circumstances far outweighed the mitigating circumstances, supporting the sentence imposed.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Issuance of second indictment was not beyond grand jury's jurisdiction. Appellant did not consent to amended indictment; proper procedure was to send case back to grand jury for issuance of new indictment. Court properly denied appellant's challenges for cause of potential jurors, who demonstrated that they could follow the law as directed. Aggravating circumstances warranted sentence which was neither cruel nor unusual.

 

596 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Simmons v. State


CR-97-0768


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


797 So. 2d 1134; 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 98



April 28, 2000, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 14, 2002.
Writ of certiorari denied Ex parte Simmons, 797 So. 2d 1186, 2001 Ala. LEXIS 155 (Ala., 2001)
Writ of certiorari denied Simmons v. Alabama, 534 U.S. 932, 151 L. Ed. 2d 221, 122 S. Ct. 298, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 7190 (2001)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Simmons v. State, 2004 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 57 (Ala. Crim. App., Mar. 26, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-96-3812).

Original Opinion of September 17, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 222.
Simmons v. State, 797 So. 2d 1134, 1999 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 222 (Ala. Crim. App., 1999)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS TO CONVICTION FOR COUNT III; REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS AS TO SENTENCING FOR COUNT III; AND REVERSED AS TO CONVICTION AND SENTENCE IMPOSED PURSUANT TO COUNT II.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an appeal from the Jefferson Circuit Court (Alabama) which ordered his conviction and sentence for the capital offense of murder during a robbery and for intentional murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted for three counts of capital murder, and later sentenced to death. On appeal, he raised several points of error. The court affirmed his conviction for capital murder. Upon review, the court found no error occurred in the admission of DNA evidence at trial, because the trial court considered the reliability and relevance of the evidence. The testimony of an agent for the Federal Bureau of Investigation, who believed the offense was sexually motivated, was properly admitted under Ala. R. Evid. 702. The agent testified that he had specialized knowledge in crime scene analysis and victimology. Given the task before the jury, the probative value of the agent's testimony outweighed its prejudicial impact. Further, photographs of the victim's body were admissible to illustrate how the crime occurred; they were not unduly prejudicial. Appellant's Batson challenges were denied, because no inference was raised that the State engaged in purposeful racial discrimination in its use of peremptory challenges.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed conviction for capital murder. No error occurred in the admission of contested evidence. Conviction for the lesser-included offense of intentional murder was vacated and the matter remanded so appellant's sentence for intentional murder conviction could be set aside.

 

597 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Wooden v. State


CR-98-2167


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


822 So. 2d 455; 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 58



March 31, 2000, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 24, 2002. As Corrected September 25, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Jefferson Circuit Court. (CC-95-1781). TRIAL JUDGE: Gloria T. Bahakel.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the Jefferson Circuit Court's (Alabama) judgment denying his motion to dismiss, finding him guilty of unlawful distribution of a controlled substance, sentencing him to life imprisonment as a habitual offender, and enhancing his sentence with two additional five-year terms, pursuant to Ala. Code § 13A-12-250, -270 (1975).


OVERVIEW: Undercover officer bought narcotics from appellant. Appellant's trial began over four and one-half years after his arrest. No motions for continuance or other delay was requested by State. Therefore, the delay should not weigh against State. Appellant failed to assert his right to a speedy trial for approximately three years and seven months. Because appellant was tried within 15 months of his first assertion of his right to a speedy trial, the delay should not have weighed heavily against State. Appellant failed to show that he suffered any actual prejudice from the delay. Therefore, the trial court properly denied appellant's motion to dismiss for failure to grant a speedy trial. Appellant's life imprisonment sentence and the two five-year enhancements were mandatory under Ala. Code §§ 13A-5-9(c)(2), 13A-12-250, 13A-12-270. Therefore, appellant's sentence was clearly within the statutory range, it was not unconstitutional, and the court would not overturn the sentence.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part; court affirmed appellant's sentence because it was within the statutory range. Appellant failed to show that delay in trial should be weigh against State and that he suffered prejudice from delay; therefore, denial of motion to dismiss for failure to grant a speedy trial was proper.

Gamble v. State


CR-97-0698


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


791 So. 2d 409; 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 16



February 4, 2000, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 14, 2000. The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published August 7, 2001. Second correction.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Shelby Circuit Court. (CC-96-813 and CC-96-814). TRIAL JUDGE: J. Michael Joiner.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS TO CONVICTIONS; REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS AS TO SENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from Shelby Circuit Court (Alabama), which convicted him of capital murder as an accomplice and sentenced him to death by electrocution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of capital murder and death sentence on grounds that he was denied: right to counsel, treatment as youthful offender, full mental examination, right to confront witnesses for non-presence at pretrial, motion to suppress statements in violation of Miranda rights, and motion for mistrial for jury tampering. He also claimed that there was improper removal of black jurors from venire, prosecutorial misconduct, and error for allowing evidence of collateral crimes. Defendant appealed death penalty sentence as improper because defendant was not shooter and court double counted charges. The court affirmed defendant's conviction because no plain error was found in guilt or sentencing proceedings before the jury. The court remanded as to sentencing, finding error because no prior conviction was found to negate existence of statutory mitigating circumstance of no significant prior criminal activity.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for capital murder as an accomplice was affirmed because court found no plain error in guilt or sentencing proceedings before jury. The court remanded for sentencing, finding error because no prior conviction was found to negate existence of statutory mitigating circumstance.

 

600 of 745 DOCUMENTS


Tyson v. State


CR-98-0267


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF ALABAMA


784 So. 2d 328; 2000 Ala. Crim. App. LEXIS 20



February 4, 2000, Released


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 24, 2000. As Corrected June 22, 2000. Released for Publication May 22, 2001. As Corrected September 4, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Macon Circuit Court. (CC-97-54). TRIAL JUDGE: Philip Dale Segrest.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, convicted of capital murder, appealed from a judgment of the Macon Circuit Court (Alabama), which sentenced him to death by electrocution because the murders occurred during the course of a robbery and involved the killing of two or more people during one act.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, convicted of murder, raised several issues on appeal. The court affirmed both conviction and death sentence, holding that a search warrant technical errors did not result in constitutional violations, nor invalidate the search. Additionally, the affidavit supporting the search warrant was thorough; it established probable cause for police to believe the murder weapon was in appellant's apartment, thus, evidence was properly admitted. After reviewing the record, the court concluded that appellant's right to cross-examine the expert witness regarding his DNA testimony was not limited in any respect. Since the identity of the murderer was at issue, evidence of another shooting was admitted to establish appellant's connection to the murder weapon. The trial court properly instructed the jury that it did not need to unanimously find mitigating circumstances. The court independently weighed aggravating and mitigating circumstances, determining that the death sentence was appropriate for appellant's conduct.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Technical error on the search warrant did not result in constitutional violations or invalidate police search. Since identity of the murderer was at issue, evidence of other shooting was admitted to establish appellant's connection to the murder weapon.
